Sulh for More than Prescribed Value in Jointly-Owned Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the invalidity of sulh excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sulh exceeding the sharia-prescribed value in a jointly-owned slave and differentiate between the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When sharia prescribes a value, sulh for excess is invalid; Sahibayn see riba, Imam sees a fixed textual value.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sulh (compromise) for an amount exceeding the value prescribed by sharia in the context of a jointly-owned slave. While both parties agree on the invalidity of the excess, they differ on the underlying rationale. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct principle in analogous cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Two co-owners share a slave. One owner frees his share while wealthy. The other co-owner makes a sulh with him for more than half the slave's value. Determine the ruling on the excess.
The freeing triggers evaluation of the slave's value as per sharia.
2
State the Agreed Ruling
Both Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree that the excess in sulh is invalid (batil). This is the agreed position (bil ittifaq).
The disagreement is only on the reasoning, not the outcome.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's Reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the excess constitutes riba because after the freeing, the right of the other owner is transferred to the value. Taking more than that value is pure interest.
This reasoning aligns with the general prohibition of riba in exchanges.
4
Explain Imam Abu Hanifa's Reasoning
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the value is textually prescribed (manṣūṣ) by the hadith: 'Whoever frees a share in a jointly-owned slave, it is assessed for his share.' Therefore, the price is fixed by revelation and cannot be exceeded by mutual agreement.
This distinction is based on the source of the valuation: sharia text vs. expert opinion.
5
Contrast with the Case of Ghasb (Usurpation)
In ghasb, the value is not textually fixed; it is determined by experts. Hence, sulh for more than expert valuation is permissible because the excess is not clearly riba. This contrast highlights the key difference: textually prescribed vs. non-prescribed values.
Imam's reasoning draws a sharp line between cases with a textual basis for valuation and those without.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہوگا ۔ بخلاف صلح بعد از قضاء کے۔ کیونکہ اب حق قیمت کی طرف منتقل ہو چکا۔ جب ایک غلام دو میں مشترک ہو اور ان میں سے ایک آزاد کر دے در آنحالیکہ وہ مالدار ہے اور دوسرا اس کی نصف قیمت سے زائد پر صلح کرے تو زیادتی باطل ہے اور یہ بالا تفاق ہے۔صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے لئے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ عشق کی صورت منصوص ہے اور شرع کا مقرر کرنا قاضی کے مقرر کرنے سے کم نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لہذا اس پر زیادتی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف سابقہ مسلہ کے کہ اس میں قیمت منصوص نہیں ہے اور اگر اسباب پر صلح کی تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ ہم بیان کر چکے۔ کہ زیادتی ظاہر نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اور قوله و اذا كان العبد ایک غلام میں دو شخص شریک تھے۔ ان میں سے شریک نے اپنا حصہ [؟] اور دوسرے شریک نے اس کی نصف قیمت سے زائد پر صلح کرلی تو بالا تفاق صلح ناجائز اور زیادتی باطل ہوگی۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک تو وجہ بطلان وہی ہے جو اوپر مذکور ہوئی (یعنی زیادتی کا ربا ہونا) امام صاحب کے نزدیک وجہ بطلان یہ ہے کہ عشق کی صورت میں قیمت شرعاً مقدر و منصوص علیہ ہے۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے۔ "من اعتق شقضا من عبد مشترك بينه وبين شريكه قوم عليه نصیب شریكه" پس قیمت پر زیادتی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف غصب کے کہ اس میں قیمت منصوص علیہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے غصب کی صورت میں زائد قیمت پر صلح جائز ہوگی۔
It will be. Contrary to sulh after the judge's ruling, because now the right has been transferred to the value. When a slave is jointly owned by two, and one of them frees him while he is wealthy, and the other makes a sulh for more than half its value, then the excess is invalid and this is by agreement. According to the Sahibayn, for the reason we mentioned, and for Imam Abu Hanifah, the reason for distinction is that the case of freeing (a share) is prescribed by sharia, and what is fixed by sharia cannot be less than what is fixed by a judge. Therefore, excess upon it will not be permissible. Contrary to the previous issue, because in it the value is not prescribed, and if sulh was made upon commodities, it is permissible, because we have mentioned that excess cannot become apparent. And the saying: 'And when the slave...' Two persons were partners in a slave. One of them freed his share [?] and the other partner made a sulh for more than half its value, then by agreement the sulh is invalid and the excess is void. According to the Sahibayn, the reason for nullity is what was mentioned above (i.e., the excess being riba). According to Imam, the reason for nullity is that in the case of freeing, the value is legally determined and prescribed, because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave jointly owned between him and his partner, it is assessed for his partner's share.' So excess over the value will not be permissible. Contrary to usurpation, because in it the value is not prescribed. Therefore, in the case of usurpation, sulh for an excess value is permissible.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a sulh (compromise) for an amount exceeding the sharia-prescribed value of a jointly-owned slave. The issue arises when two co-owners share a slave, one frees his share (being wealthy), and the other co-owner makes a sulh with him for more than half the slave's value. The ruling states that such excess is invalid by agreement. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that any excess constitutes riba (usury) because the right has transferred to the value, and taking more than the right is interest. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, provides a different reasoning: he distinguishes this case from the earlier case of ghasb (usurpation). In the freeing scenario, the value is textually prescribed (manṣūṣ) by the hadith of the Prophet: 'Whoever frees a share in a jointly-owned slave, it is assessed for his share.' Hence, the amount is fixed by revelation, and any excess is invalid. In contrast, in the ghasb case, the value is not textually prescribed; it is determined by experts, so sulh for more is permissible because the excess does not clearly appear as riba. The passage emphasizes that when the value is prescribed by sharia (as in itq), it cannot be overridden by private agreement.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise or settlement where one party gives up a claim in exchange for something.
عبد مشترك ('abd mushtarak): A slave jointly owned by two or more persons.
قيمة مقدرة (qīmah muqaddarah): Value assessed by experts or prescribed by sharia.
منصوص (manṣūṣ): Textually prescribed in the Quran or hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider the excess in sulh invalid in the case of freeing a jointly-owned slave?
A) Because it is riba.
B) Because the value is fixed by the judge's ruling.
C) Because the value is textually prescribed by a hadith.
D) Because the other owner is not present.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when sharia prescribes a value (as in freeing a share of a jointly-owned slave), sulh for any excess is invalid, but the reasoning may differ between riba-based and text-based arguments, affecting other cases.

Sulh for Excess Value on Usurped Garment: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on sulh for excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa permits sulh for more than the market value of a usurped item before a judge's ruling, and contrast the Sahibayn's reasoning based on the transfer of right.

Core Idea
Before a judge's ruling, the owner's right remains in the 'ayn: excess payment is compensation, not riba.

This passage presents a nuanced dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (joined by Shafi'i and Hanbali) regarding the validity of sulh where the usurper pays more than the market value of a destroyed garment before any judicial decree. The core issue is the timing of the transfer of the owner's right from the specific property to its monetary value. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of ghasb and riba in transactional contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the positions
Identify the facts: usurpation, destruction, no judge's ruling yet, sulh for excess. State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling (valid) and the Sahibayn's ruling (invalid).
The Sahibayn are joined by Shafi'i and Hanbali.
2
Identify the opposing proof
The Sahibayn argue that the owner's right is only to the value (qimah), which is fixed; taking excess is riba. Understand their reasoning: the right becomes monetary upon destruction.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the owner's right remains in the 'ayn (the destroyed garment) or its mithl until the judge transfers it to value. Thus, excess payment is compensation, not riba.
Key point: right transfers only after judge's decree.
4
Recognize the agreed exceptions
Both sides agree sulh is valid if the excess is within the range of expert estimation or if the sulh is upon different genus (commodities vs. money).
These exceptions show that not all excess is automatically riba.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if sulh is made before judgment, the extra amount is valid in Hanafi view, but invalid for others. Later Hanafi fatwa often prefers the Sahibayn's view for caution.
This affects advice given to parties in a tort settlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ومن غصب ثوباً يهوديا .... بقول شیخ اکمل یہوداہل کتاب کی ایک قوم ہے جن کی طرف ایک خاص کپڑا منسوب ہے۔ یقال ثوب یهودی لیکن علامہ کا کی اور شیخ انزاری فرماتے ہیں کہ ظابز الفظ یہود یہاں ایک جگہ کا نام ہے جس کی طرف معلوم القیمۃ کپڑا منسوب ہے۔ بہر کیف مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک یہودی تھان جس کی قیمت سوروپے سے کم ہے غصب کر کے تلف کر دیا اور ابھی قاضی نے اس کی قیمت دینے کا حکم نہیں کیا تھا۔ کہ غاصب نے اس کے مالک کو سوروپے دے کر صلح کرلی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ صلح جائز ہے۔ صاحبین ، امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ جس قیمت کے اندازہ میں عام لوگ خسارہ نہیں اٹھاتے اس قیمت سے زیادہ پر صلح کرنا جائز نہیں کیونکہ مالک کا حق صرف اس کی قیمت میں ہے جو ایک معین مقدار ہے تو اس سے زائد لینا سود ہوگا۔ بخلاف اس کے جب غاصب نے اسباب معین پر صلح کی ہو کہ یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے خواہ اسباب کی قیمت زائد ہو یا کم ، کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کے وقت زیادتی کا ظہور نہیں ہوتا اور بخلاف اس کے جب اتنی قیمت پر صلح کی ہو جو اندازہ کرنے والوں کے اندازہ کے تحت داخل ہو کہ یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ لأنه لم يعد ذالك فضلا فلم يكن ربا قوله ولابی حنیفه ... الخ - امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالک کا حق ثوب ہالک میں ابھی باقی ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر بجائے کپڑے کے کوئی غام ہوتا اور آقا قیمت لینا چھوڑ دیتا تو اس کا کفن آقا پر واجب ہوتا یا یوں کہو کہ ایسی صورت میں آقا کا حق ایسے مثل سے متعلق ہوتا ہے، جو صورت و معنی ہر دو لحاظ سے مثل ہو۔ کیونکہ عدوان کا تاوان بمثل ہوتا ہے اور قیمت کی طرف جو اس کا حق منتقل ہوتا ہے۔ وہ قضاء قاضی کے ذریعہ سے ہوتا ہے اور جب وہ قضاء سے پیشتر زائد قیمت پر رضامند ہو گئے۔ تو یہ اپنے حق کا عوض لینا ہوگا نہ کہ سود۔ البتہ اگر قاضی نے قیمت کا حکم دے دیا ہو تو اس سے زائد پر صلح کرنا بیاج ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اب اس کا حق قیمت کی جانب منتقل ہو چکا۔
His saying: 'And whoever usurps a Jewish garment...' According to Shaykh Akmal, 'Yahud' is a community of the People of the Book to which a specific cloth is attributed. It is said 'Jewish garment'. But Allamah Kay and Shaykh Ansari say that the word 'Yahud' here is a place name to which a cloth of known value is attributed. Anyway, the issue is that a person usurped a Jewish cloth whose value is less than one hundred dirhams and destroyed it, and the judge had not yet ordered the payment of its value. Then the usurper gave the owner one hundred dirhams and made sulh. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this sulh is valid. The Sahibayn, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad say that making sulh for more than the value which people generally do not consider a loss is not permissible, because the owner's right is only in its value, which is a fixed amount; taking more than that would be usury. Contrary to the case where the usurper made sulh upon specific commodities: it is permissible by agreement, whether the value of the commodities is more or less, because when the types differ, excess does not become apparent. And contrary to the case where sulh is made for an amount that falls within the estimation of assessors: that is also permissible, because that is not considered excess, so it is not riba. His saying: 'And for Abu Hanifah...' The proof of Imam is that the owner's right remains in the destroyed garment. Even if, instead of the cloth, it were a shroud and the owner left taking the value, his shroud would be obligatory upon the owner, or you could say that in such a situation, the owner's right is related to the exact like (mithl) in terms of form and meaning, because the compensation for transgression is by way of like. And his right transferring to the value occurs through the judge's ruling. When they agreed upon an excess value before the ruling, this will be taking compensation for his right, not usury. However, if the judge had ordered the value, then making sulh for more would be usury, because now his right has transferred to the value.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of sulh for an amount exceeding the market value of a usurped and destroyed garment. The scenario: a person usurps a Jewish garment worth less than one hundred dirhams, destroys it, and before any judge's verdict, the usurper gives the owner one hundred dirhams in sulh. Imam Abu Hanifa rules this sulh valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), along with Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, hold it invalid because the owner's right is only the value; taking excess is riba. They distinguish two cases where excess is permissible: (1) sulh upon specific commodities (different genus) because excess is not apparent; (2) sulh for an amount within the range of expert estimation (not clearly excess). Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that before the judge's ruling, the owner's right remains attached to the destroyed garment itself (or its like in qimiyat). The right only transfers to the value after the judge's verdict. Until then, the parties may agree on any amount as compensation for the right, and it is not riba. If the judge had already fixed the value, then excess would be riba because the right is now established in that specific amount.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful usurpation of property; the act of taking and destroying someone else's property without right.
قیمی (qīmī): Non-fungible property; compensation is by value (qīmah) not by like (mithl).
صلح (ṣulḥ): Amicable settlement; transaction to end a dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is sulh for an excess over the value of a usurped item valid before the judge's ruling?
A) Because the owner can demand any price.
B) Because the right remains in the 'ayn, not yet transferred to the value.
C) Because usury only applies to loans, not contracts.
D) Because the usurper has already destroyed the item.

Key Takeaway
The validity of sulh for excess over value depends on whether the owner's right has been transferred to the value by a judge's ruling; before that, excess is not riba.

Agency in Sulh: When Is the Agent Liable?
Ruling on agent's liability in sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when an agent appointed for sulh is liable for payment and when he is not, based on the type of sulh and whether a guarantee is given.

Core Idea
An agent for sulh is liable only if the sulh involves property exchange or if he guarantees; otherwise he is a mere messenger.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling on agency in sulh (compromise). Sulh can involve pure remission (isqāt) or exchange of property (mu'awada). The agent's liability depends on which type he undertakes and whether he personally guarantees the payment. We will explore the rationale and the conditions that shift liability from principal to agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of sulh
Read the passage carefully to distinguish between sulh that is pure remission (isqāt) — like sulh for intentional blood or part of a debt — and sulh that involves property-for-property exchange (like a sale).
The key is whether the sulh is a transfer of property or a waiver of rights.
2
Determine the agent's role
In remission sulh, the agent is a mere messenger (safīr), not a party; in property exchange sulh, the agent acts as a party (like a seller).
Compare with a marriage agent who is also a messenger.
3
Apply the exception: guarantee
Even in remission sulh, if the agent guarantees the payment, he becomes liable by the contract of guarantee, not by the sulh itself.
The guarantee overrides the default no-liability rule.
4
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the agent is liable in two situations: (1) property-for-property sulh, or (2) any sulh where he guarantees payment. Otherwise, liability rests with the principal.
Memorize the distinction as it applies in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التبرع بالصُّلْحُ والتوكيل بـــه ترجمہ یہ باب صلح کے ساتھ احسان اور وکیل کرنے کے بیان میں ہے تشریح قوله باب نهایه وغایہ اور عنایہ میں ہے کہ آدمی کا تصرف خود اپنی ذات کے لئے چونکہ اصل ہے اس لئے اس کے بیان کو غیر کے لئے تصرف کے بیان پر مقدم کیا ہے اور تبرع با صلح سے مراد یہی ہے کیونکہ آدمی جو کام غیر کے لئے کرے وہ اس میں متبرع ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں تبرع با صلح سے مراد صرف غیر کے لئے تصرف کرنا نہیں ہے ورنہ اس کے بعد کے الفاظ والتوکیل بہ "مستدرک ہو جائیں گے۔ بلکہ یہاں تبرع سے مراد دوسرے کی طرف سے اس کے حکم کے بغیر صلح کرنا ہے۔ اور " والتوکیل بہ سے مراد اس کے حکم سے صلح کرنا ہے۔ صلح کے وکیل نے اپنی طرف سے صلح کر لی تو مال وکیل کو لازم نہ ہوگا بلکہ موکل کو لازم ہوگا بشرطیکہ وکیل اس کی ضمانت نہ اٹھائے قَالَ وَمَنْ وَكَلَ رَجُلًا بِالصُّلْحِ عَنْهُ فَصَالَحَ لَمْ يَلْزَمِ الْوَكِيلِ مَا صَالَحَ عَنْهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَضْمَنَهُ وَالْمَالُ لَازِمٌ لِلْمُوَكَّلِ وَتَاوِيلُ هَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ إِذَا كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ اَوْ كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَلَى بَعْضِ مَا يَدَّعِيهِ مِنَ الدَّيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ اسْقَاطُ مَحضِ فَكَانَ الْوَكِيلُ فِيهِ سَفِيرًا وَمُعَبِّرًا فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِ كَالْوَكِيْلِ بِالنِّكَاحِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَضْمَنَهُ لِأَنَّهُ حِينَئِذٍ هُوَ مُوَاخِذْ بِعَقْدِ الصَّمَانِ لَا بِعَقْدِ الصُّلْحِ أَمَا إِذَا كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ مَالٍ بِمَالٍ فَهُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْبَيْعِ فَيَرْجِعُ الْحُقُوق إِلَى الْوَكِيلِ فَيَكُونُ الْمُطَالِبُ ِبالْمَالَ هُوَ الْوَكِيلُ دُونَ الْمُوَكِل
Voluntary sulh and agency for it. Translation: This chapter is about benevolence with sulh and appointing an agent. Commentary on his saying: The chapter... In an-Nihayah and al-‘Inayah, it is said that since a person’s disposition for his own self is the original, its explanation is preceded over the explanation of disposition for others. And 'tabarru' bi as-sulh' refers to this, because a person who acts for another is doing a voluntary act. But the author of an-Nata’ij says that here 'tabarru' bi as-sulh' does not mean merely acting for another; otherwise the subsequent words 'wa at-tawkīlu bihī' would be redundant. Rather, 'tabarru' here means making sulh on behalf of another without his command, and 'at-tawkīlu bihī' means making sulh with his command. When the agent of sulh made sulh on his own behalf, the property does not become binding on the agent, but on the principal, provided the agent does not assume liability. He said: 'And whoever appoints a man as agent for sulh on his behalf, and he makes sulh, what he made sulh for does not become binding on the agent unless he guarantees it, and the property is binding on the principal. The interpretation of this issue is when the sulh is for intentional blood or for part of a debt that he claims, because it is pure remission, so the agent therein is a messenger and interpreter, so there is no liability upon him, like the agent for marriage, unless he guarantees it, because then he is held by the contract of guarantee, not by the contract of sulh. However, if the sulh is for property against property, it is like a sale, so rights revert to the agent, and the demand for property is against the agent, not the principal.'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on voluntary sulh (tabarru' bi as-sulh) and agency (tawkīl) in sulh. The commentators explain that 'tabarru' here specifically means making sulh on behalf of another without that person's prior command, while 'tawkīl' refers to sulh by command. The main ruling: When an agent (wakīl) is appointed to make sulh on behalf of the principal (muwakkil), the property (i.e., what is given in sulh) is not binding on the agent but on the principal, unless the agent guarantees it. This applies when the sulh is for intentional homicide (dam al-'amd) or for partial remission of a claimed debt—these are pure remissions, and the agent is merely a messenger (safīr) like a marriage agent. If the agent guarantees payment, he is bound by the guarantee contract, not by the sulh. However, if the sulh is for property in exchange for property (like a sale), then the agent becomes the party responsible; rights and claims are directed to the agent, not the principal. The distinction rests on the nature of the sulh: if it involves remission (isqāt), the agent is a mere conduit; if it involves exchange of property, the agent is like a buyer.

Key Terms
تبرع بالصلح (tabarru' bi as-sulh): Making sulh on behalf of another without being commanded; a voluntary act.
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another in a contract.
سفير (safīr): A messenger or intermediary who merely communicates, not a party to the contract.
ضمان (damān): Guarantee; a contract by which one assumes liability for another's obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does an agent appointed for sulh become liable for the payment?
A) Always, as he is the one who made the contract.
B) Only if the sulh is for property against property, like a sale.
C) Only if he guarantees the payment.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
An agent for sulh is not liable for payment unless the sulh is a property exchange or he personally guarantees the payment.

Distinguishing Tabarru' from Tawkeel in Sulh
Definition of tabarru' and tawkeel in sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tabarru' (gratuitous act without authorization) and tawkeel (act with authorization) in the context of sulh, and explain the reason for Sahib al-Nata'ij's refinement.

Core Idea
Tabarru' in sulh is acting without order; tawkeel is acting with order.

This passage clarifies the chapter heading 'Tabarru' bil-Sulh and Tawkeel bihi'. At first glance, tabarru' seems to mean any act done for another. However, a later commentator, Sahib al-Nata'ij, refines the definition: tabarru' specifically refers to making sulh without the other party's order, while tawkeel refers to sulh with his order. This refinement avoids redundancy and has important legal consequences for liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms in the heading.
The heading contains two key terms: tabarru' bil-sulh and tawkeel bihi. Understand that they represent two distinct scenarios of making sulh on behalf of another.
Tabarru' literally means 'gratuitous act'; tawkeel means 'appointing an agent'.
2
Understand the initial interpretation.
Commentators like the authors of al-Nihayah and al-Inayah initially interpret tabarru' as any act done for another, since a person acting for someone else is doing a favor.
This interpretation makes tabarru' very broad, covering both authorized and unauthorized acts.
3
Recognize the problem of redundancy.
Sahib al-Nata'ij points out that if tabarru' includes all acts for others, then the separate mention of 'tawkeel' would be redundant (mustadrak), because tawkeel is also an act for another.
To avoid repetition, a more precise distinction is needed.
4
Apply the refinement.
Sahib al-Nata'ij narrows the definition: tabarru' now specifically means making sulh without the other person's order (i.e., as a fudooli), whereas tawkeel means making sulh with his order.
Thus, the two terms become mutually exclusive.
5
Note the legal significance.
This distinction determines liability: an unauthorized actor (tabarru') may not bind the principal unless ratified, while an authorized agent (tawkeel) binds the principal within the scope of agency.
This affects the validity and consequences of the sulh.

Source Text

التبرع بالصُّلْحُ والتوكيل بــه ترجمہ یہ باب صلح کے ساتھ احسان اور وکیل کرنے کے بیان میں ہے تشریح قوله باب نهایه وغایہ اور عنایہ میں ہے کہ آدمی کا تصرف خود اپنی ذات کے لئے چونکہ اصل ہے اس لئے اس کے بیان کو غیر کے لئے تصرف کے بیان پر مقدم کیا ہے اور تبرع با صلح سے مراد یہی ہے کیونکہ آدمی جو کام غیز کے لئے کرے وہ اس میں متبرع ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں تبرع با صلح سے مراد صرف غیر کے لئے تصرف کرنا نہیں ہے ورنہ اس کے بعد کے الفاظ والتوکیل بہ "مستدرک ہو جائیں گے۔ بلکہ یہاں تبرع سے مراد دوسرے کی طرف سے اس کے حکم کے بغیر صلح کرنا ہے۔ اور " والتوکیل بہ سے مراد اس کے حکم سے صلح کرنا ہے۔
Tabarru' bil-sulh and tawkeel bihi. Translation: This chapter is about doing a favor with sulh and appointing an agent. Explanation: In al-Nihayah, al-Ghayah, and al-Inayah, it is said that a person's own disposition for himself is the origin, so its explanation is given precedence over the explanation of disposition for others. And tabarru' bil-sulh means this, because whatever a person does for others, he is doing a favor. However, Sahib al-Nata'ij says that here tabarru' bil-sulh does not mean only disposition for others; otherwise the following words 'wa al-tawkeel bihi' would be repetitious. Rather, here tabarru' means making sulh on behalf of another without his order, and 'wa al-tawkeel bihi' means making sulh with his order.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a terminological clarification of the heading. The author explains that the chapter covers two aspects: tabarru' (doing a favor) and tawkeel (appointing an agent) in sulh. Initially, it seems tabarru' means any act done for another. But a later commentator (Sahib al-Nata'ij) refines: tabarru' here specifically means making sulh without the other party's instruction (fudooli), while tawkeel means sulh with his instruction. This distinction is important for the rulings that follow, as the liability of the actor differs based on whether he had authorization.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): Making sulh on behalf of another without his order or authorization.
توکیل (tawkeel): Appointing an agent (wakeel) to make sulh with the principal's order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Making sulh as a favor for oneself.
B) Making sulh as a favor for another person with their order.
C) Making sulh as a favor for another person without their order.
D) Making sulh for the sake of God.

Key Takeaway
Tabarru' in sulh means acting without authorization; tawkeel means acting with authorization — a distinction that avoids redundancy and determines liability.

Liability of a Wakil in Sulh (Compromise)
Declares that a wakil is not liable for sulh payment unless he guarantees it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on a wakil's liability in a sulh contract and identify the exception when he guarantees the payment.

Core Idea
A wakil in sulh is a mere messenger; he bears no liability unless he explicitly guarantees.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between a wakil (agent) and a safir (messenger). In a sulh (compromise) contract, the wakil is treated as a safir, meaning he does not become personally liable for the payment. This lesson examines the default rule and the exception when the wakil voluntarily guarantees the payment. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion in agency law and ensures that liability is assigned correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Determine who appointed the wakil (principal/muwakkil) and what the wakil is authorized to do (sulh on a murder or debt claim).
The wakil is not a party to the sulh; he is only a representative.
2
Apply the default ruling
The sulh payment is binding on the principal (muwakkil), not on the wakil. The wakil is like a safir (messenger) in marriage contracts who is not liable for the mahr.
Rights and obligations revert to the principal.
3
Identify the exception
If the wakil explicitly guarantees (daman) the payment at the time of sulh, he becomes personally liable. This liability is from the guarantee, not from his agency.
The guarantee is an independent contract of daman.

Source Text

كتاب الصلح.

یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے قتل عمد کی طرف سے یا اس پر جس قدر دین کا دعویٰ ہے اس کے کسی حصہ پر صلح کرنے کے لئے دوسرے کو وکیل بنایا تو بدل صلح موکل پر لازم نہ ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل پر۔ کیونکہ یہ صلح قاتل سے اسقاط قصاص ہے۔ اور مدعی علیہ سے استقاط بعض دین ۔ تو وکیل سفیر محض ٹھہرانہ کہ عاقد لہذا حقوق مؤکل کی طرف راجع ہوں گے۔ جیسے نکاح کا وکیل مہر وغیرہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں اگر وکیل صلح کرتے وقت بدل صلح کا ضامن ہو جائے تو بدل صلح اسی پر لازم ہو گا۔ لیکن تو کیل کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ اس کے ضامن ہونے کی وجہ سے تاویل مذکور کی ضرورت اس لئے پڑی کہ اگر مال سے صلح مال پر ہو تو یہ بمنزلہ بیج ہوتی ہے۔ پس حقوق وکیل کیجانب راجع ہوتے ہیں اور مال کا مطالبہ اسی سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل سے۔ قـولـه والـمـال لازم للمول ....نهایي، درایہ عنایہ، بنایہ، غایہ شرح اقطع سب میں للموکل کا لازم بمعنی علی لیا گیا ہے۔ ای المال لازم على المؤكل ۔ جیسے ”و ان أسأتم فلها “ میں لام بمعنی علی ہے۔ ای فعلیها، صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ۔ اس لئے کر للموکل لازم سے متعلق ہے۔ اور کلمہ لزوم متعدی بنفسہ بھی ہوتا اور باء کے ساتھ بھی ، يقال لزمه ولزم بہ لیکن علی کے ساتھ متعدی نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا کلمہ لا کو بحالہ رکھ کر تقویت عمل ہوتا ہے جو کلام عرب میں شائع ذائع ہے۔ بخلاف ایت مذکورہ کے کہ اس میں لام کلمہ مقدر سے متعلق ہے تو کوئی ایسا ہی کلمہ مقدر مانا جائے گا۔ جس کے لئے اس کا صلہ ہونا مناسب ہو۔

Book of Sulh (Compromise). It is that if a person appoints another as a wakil (agent) to make a sulh on behalf of a murder case or on any part of a debt claimed, then the sulh payment is not binding on the principal nor on the wakil. Because this sulh from the murderer is the dropping of qisas, and from the defendant is the dropping of some debt. So the wakil is merely a messenger (safir), not a contracting party; therefore rights revert to the principal. Just as a wakil in marriage is not guarantor for the mahr. However, if the wakil at the time of sulh guarantees the sulh payment, then the sulh payment is binding on him. But not because of wakalah, rather because of his guarantee. This interpretation is needed because if the sulh is on property, it is like a sale. So rights revert to the wakil and the property is demanded from him, not from the principal. His saying: 'wal-mal lazim lil-mawla' ... in Nihayah, Dirayah, Inayah, Binyah, Ghayah sharh Aqta', all have 'laazim li al-mawla' meaning 'laazim ala al-mawla' (binding upon the principal). Like in the verse 'wa in asa'tunna fa laha' where 'la' means 'ala'. So it is 'alaiha'. Sahib Nata'ij says there is no reason for that. Therefore, the word 'la' is related to 'lazim'. And the verb 'lazima' is transitive by itself and with 'ba', you say 'lazimahu' and 'lazima bihi', but it is not transitive with 'ala'. So keeping the word as is gives strength to the action, which is common in Arabic speech. Unlike the mentioned verse, where 'la' is related to an implied word, so some such implied word must be assumed which would be appropriate as its complement. It will not be binding on the dhimma, but will be on the dhimma of the principal. Unless the wakil guarantees it. The author of Hidayah says regarding this issue (the non-binding on the wakil) the interpretation...
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the liability of a wakil (agent) in a sulh (compromise) contract. The ruling clarifies that when a person appoints a wakil to negotiate a sulh—whether it involves dropping qisas (retaliation) in a murder case or reducing a debt—the wakil does not become personally liable for the payment. The wakil is considered a safir (messenger), not a contracting party (aqid). Therefore, the rights and obligations revert to the principal (muwakkil). The author draws an analogy with a wakil in marriage, who is not responsible for the mahr. However, if the wakil explicitly guarantees (daman) the sulh payment, he becomes personally liable, not due to his agency but due to his independent guarantee. A linguistic discussion follows about the phrase 'wal-mal lazim lil-mawla', analyzing whether it means 'binding upon' or 'binding for' the principal. The author prefers the meaning 'binding upon' to align with the Hanafi position that the payment is due from the principal, not the wakil. The passage concludes that the dhimma (liability) does not become binding on the wakil but remains on the principal's dhimma, unless the wakil guarantees it.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): A person appointed to act on behalf of another in a sulh contract.
بدل صلح (badal al-sulh): The payment or consideration given in the compromise.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor who becomes personally liable for the sulh payment.
سفیر (safir): A mere messenger who does not bear liability for the contract.

Key Takeaway
A wakil in sulh is not liable for the payment unless he explicitly guarantees it; his default role is that of a messenger.

Fuduli's Sulh: First Two Valid Forms
Ruling on the first two valid forms of sulh by a fuduli

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two forms of sulh by a fuduli that are valid in the Hanafi school and explain the legal basis (guarantee, specification, and isqat) for each.

Core Idea
A fuduli can make a valid sulh if he guarantees payment or specifies his own property; the sulh is validated as isqat, not exchange.

This lesson examines a passage from Al-Hidayah that details when a settlement (sulh) made by an unauthorized person (fuduli) is valid. The text presents four forms; here we cover the first two. Understanding these forms clarifies how Hanafi fiqh balances the rights of the plaintiff, defendant, and the fuduli, using principles of guarantee and isqat (dropping of rights).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two forms
From the passage, extract the first two forms of fuduli's sulh: (1) when the fuduli makes a sulh with property and personally guarantees the payment, and (2) when the fuduli attributes the consideration to his own property (e.g., 'my thousand dirhams' or 'my slave').
The text also mentions a sub-case of the second form: if the fuduli says 'for a thousand' and hands them over, it is also valid.
2
Analyze the first form: guarantee
In the first form, the fuduli becomes a principal (asil) by virtue of his guarantee. The defendant receives only bara'ah (acquittal), and regarding bara'ah, the stranger and the defendant are equal. The fuduli is considered a benefactor (mutabarri') towards the defendant, like someone who voluntarily pays the defendant's debt.
The analogy is drawn to khul' where a fuduli guarantees the payment.
3
Analyze the second form: specification of own property
When the fuduli attributes the consideration to his own property (e.g., 'on my thousand dirhams'), he commits to delivering it, making the sulh valid and binding. Similarly, if he simply hands over the consideration without specification, the contract is perfected because the plaintiff receives the consideration.
The key is that the fuduli takes personal responsibility for the specified property.
4
Understand the isqat basis
In both forms, the sulh is validated as isqat (dropping of the plaintiff's right) rather than as an exchange. Therefore, the fuduli does not receive any part of the claimed property; it remains with the defendant. This applies regardless of whether the defendant admits or denies the claim.
This distinguishes fuduli's sulh from a regular sulh where the defendant pays from the claimed property.
5
Contrast with unauthorized sulh without guarantee/specification
If the fuduli does not guarantee or specify his own property, the sulh is not valid under these forms. The text implies that only these two forms (and the sub-case) are valid among the four total forms.
The remaining two forms will be covered in a subsequent lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضولی کی مصالحت کا حکم
قَالَ وَإِنْ صَالَحَ عَنْهُ رَجُلٌ بِغَيْر أَمْرِهِ فَهُوَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَوْجُهِ إِنْ صَالحَ بِمَالٍ وَضَمَنَهُ ثُمَّ الصُّلْحُ لَانَّ الْحَاصِلَ لِلْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لَيْسَ إِلَّا الْبَرَاءَةُ وَفِي حَقِهَا الْأَجْنَبِيُّ وَالْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ سَوَاءٌ فَصَلُحَ أَصِيلًا فِيْهِ إِذَا ضَمَنَهُ كَالْفُضُولِى بِالْخُلُعِ إِذَا ضَمَنَ الْبَدَلَ وَيَكُونُ مُتَبَرِّعاً عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ كَمَا لَوْ تَبَرَّعَ بِقَضَاءِ الدَّيْنِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بِأَمْرِهِ وَلَا يَكُونُ لِهَذَا الْمَصَالِحِ شَيْءٌ مِنَ الْمُدَّعَى وَإِنَّمَا ذَلِكَ لِلَّذِي فِي يَدِهِ لان تَصْحِيحه بطريق الاسْقَاطِ وَلَا فَرْقَ فِى هَذَا بَيْنَ مَا إِذَا كَانَ مُقِرًّا أَوْ مُنْكِرًا وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ صَالَحَتُكَ عَلَى الْفَى هَذِهِ أَوْ عَلَى عَبْدِى هَذَا صَحَ الصُّلْحُ وَلَزِمَه تَسْلِيْمُهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا أَضَافَهِ إِلَى مَالِ نَفْسِهِ فَقَدْ الْعَزَمَ تَسْلِيمَه فَصَحَ الصُّلْحُ وَكَذَلِكَ لَوْ قَالَ عَلَى الْفْ وَسَلَّمَهَا لِاَنَّ التَّسْلِيمَ إِلَيْهِ يُوجِبُ سَلَامَةَ الْعِوَض لَهُ فَيَتِمُ الْعَقْدُ لِحُصُولِ مَقْصُودِهِ
ترجمہ اگر صلح کی کسی نے اس کی طرف سے اس کے حکم کے بغیر تو یہ چار طرح پر ہے۔ اگر صلح کی مال کے عوض اور خود ضامن ہو گیا تو صلح پوری ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ مدعی علیہ کے لئے کچھ حاصل نہیں سوائے برات کے اور برات کے حق میں اجنبی اور بدعی علیہ برابر ہیں۔ تو اجنبی اس میں اصیل ہو سکتا ہے۔ جب کہ اس کا ضامن ہو جائے۔ جیسے خلع کا فضولی جب بدل ضلع کا ضامن ہو جائے اور وہ احسان کنندہ ہوگا مدعی علیہ پر جیسے اگر وہ قرض چکانے کا احسان کرے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب صلح اس کے حکم سے ہو۔ پھر اجنبی مصالح کے لئے دین مدعی بہ سے کچھ نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ وہ اسی کے لئے رہے گی ۔ جس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صلح کی تصیح بطریق اسقاط ہے اور اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں کہ مدعی علیہ مقر ہو یا منکر ۔ اسی طرح اگر فضولی نے کہا کہ میں نے اپنی ان ہزار پر یا اپنے اس غلام پر تجھ سے صلح کی تو صلح ہوگی اور اس پر سپرد کرنالازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب اس نے صلح کو اپنی ذاتی مال کی طرف منسوب کیا تو اس کے سپرد کرنے کا التزام کر لیا۔ لہذا صلح صیح ہوگئی۔ ایسے ہی اگر اس نے کہا کہ میں نے ہزار پر صلح کی اور ہزار اس کوسپر دکر دیئے۔ کیونکہ اس کو سپر د کر دینا اس کے لئے عوض کی سلامتی کا موجب ہے تو عقد صلح پورا ہو جائے گا۔ اس کا مقصد حاصل ہو جانے کے وجہ سے۔

۔
مدعی علیہ کو بری کر دیا تو یہ مبادلہ نہیں ہے۔ پھر مصالح مذکور کو کچھ نہ ملنے میں مدعی علیہ کے مقز یا منکر ہونے سے کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ قوله على الفى هذه .. بدل صلح کی نسبت اپنے مال کی طرف کی۔ مثلا یوں کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے اپنے ان ہزار درہموں یا اپنے اس غلام پر صلح کی ۔ اس صورت میں بھی صلح صحیح ہوگی اور فضولی پر وہ ہزار درہم یا وہ غلام سپرد کر نالازم ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس نے صلح کی نسبت اپنے ذاتی مال کی طرف کی تو اس کے سپرد کرنے کا التزام کر لیا۔
اپنے ذاتی مال کی طرف تو نسبت نہیں کی ۔ مگر بدل صلح سپرد کر دیا۔ اس صورت میں بھی صلح صحیح ہوگی کیونکہ مدعی کا مقصود یہ تھا کہ اس کوعوض پہنچ جائے اور وہ اس کو پہنچ گیا۔
The ruling of fuduli's sulh. He said: And if a man makes a sulh on his (the defendant's) behalf without his command, then it is of four forms: If he makes a sulh with (payment of) property and he guarantees it, then the sulh is valid, because what is obtained for the defendant is only bara'ah (acquittal), and in respect of that, the stranger and the defendant are equal. So the stranger can be an agent (asil) in it when he guarantees it, like the fuduli in khul' when he guarantees the payment. And he will be a benefactor (mutabarri') towards the defendant, just as if he voluntarily pays off a debt. Unlike when it is done by his command. And nothing of the claimed property will be for this musalih (the one who settles); rather it will be for the one in whose possession it is, because the validation is by way of isqat (dropping of right). And there is no difference in this whether the defendant is admitting or denying. Similarly, if he says: 'I have settled with you for my thousand dirhams' or 'for my this slave', the sulh is valid and it is binding on him to deliver it, because when he attributed it to his own property, he committed to delivering it, so the sulh is valid. Similarly, if he says 'for a thousand' and hands it over, because handing it over ensures the safety of the consideration for him, so the contract is perfected due to the achievement of its purpose. Translation: If someone makes a sulh on behalf of another without his command, then it is of four types. If he makes a sulh with property and himself becomes a guarantor, then the sulh is valid. Because the defendant obtains nothing but bara'ah, and in the right of bara'ah, the stranger and the defendant are equal. So the stranger can become an asil (principal) in it when he becomes its guarantor, like the fuduli in khul' when he guarantees the payment. And he will be a benefactor towards the defendant, just as if he pays off a debt as a favor. Unlike when the sulh is by his command. Then for this stranger musalih, nothing of the claimed property will be; rather it will remain for the one in whose possession it is, because this sulh is validated by way of isqat (dropping of right). And there is no difference in this whether the defendant is admitting or denying. Similarly, if the fuduli says: 'I have settled with you for my thousand dirhams' or 'for my this slave', the sulh is valid and it is binding on him to deliver it, because when he attributed the sulh to his own property, he committed to delivering it, so the sulh is valid. Similarly, if he says 'for a thousand' and hands them over, because handing them over ensures the safety of the consideration for him, so the contract is perfected due to the achievement of its purpose.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the sulh made by a fuduli (a person acting without authorization). The text, citing the Hidayah, enumerates four forms of fuduli's sulh. This lesson covers the first two forms. The first form occurs when the fuduli makes a sulh with property and personally guarantees the payment. The sulh is valid because the defendant only receives bara'ah (acquittal from the claim), and in terms of bara'ah, a stranger and the defendant are on equal footing. The fuduli thus becomes an asil (principal) by virtue of his guarantee, analogous to a fuduli in khul' (divorce by redemption) who guarantees the payment. The fuduli is considered a mutabarri' (benefactor) towards the defendant, similar to someone who voluntarily pays off the defendant's debt. However, if the defendant had authorized the sulh, the fuduli would not be a benefactor and could reclaim the payment. The second form occurs when the fuduli attributes the payment to his own property, such as saying 'on my thousand dirhams' or 'on my slave.' This sulh is valid, and the fuduli is obligated to deliver that property. The commentary explains that attributing the payment to his own property shows a commitment to deliver, hence the sulh is binding. A sub-case is also discussed: if the fuduli simply says 'on a thousand' and hands over the payment, the sulh is also valid because the plaintiff receives the consideration, achieving the contract's purpose. The fuduli does not receive any part of the claimed property; it remains with the defendant, as the sulh is validated through isqat (dropping of rights), not through exchange. This applies whether the defendant admits or denies the claim.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): A person who acts on behalf of another without prior authorization (ghayr amrihi).
برات (bara'ah): Acquittal; the release of the defendant from the claim through the sulh.
اصیل (asil): A principal party in the contract; here the fuduli becomes asil by guaranteeing the payment.
متبرع (mutabarri'): A benefactor who does an act of charity or favor without expectation of return.
اسقاط (isqat): Dropping or relinquishing a right; the sulh is validated as isqat, not as exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the role of the fuduli in the first form of sulh?
A) He acts as a messenger for the defendant, and the defendant becomes liable for payment.
B) He becomes a principal (asil) by guaranteeing the payment and is considered a benefactor to the defendant.
C) He is the sole beneficiary of the claimed property.
D) He must get the defendant's ratification for the sulh to be valid.

Key Takeaway
A fuduli's sulh is valid in two forms: with guarantee or with specification of own property; both rely on isqat, not exchange, and the fuduli becomes personally liable for the consideration.

The Suspended Sulh: When a Fuduli's Settlement Requires Ratification
Explains the third form of fuduli's sulh: suspended contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a fuduli's sulh without specification or guarantee is suspended (mawquf) and explain why the defendant's ratification is necessary.

Core Idea
A fuduli's sulh without guarantee is suspended until the defendant ratifies.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani explains the third form of fuduli's sulh. The fuduli offers a settlement of 'a thousand' without specifying the source or guaranteeing payment. This creates a suspended contract that only becomes binding if the defendant (the true principal) approves. Understanding when a contract is mawquf versus immediately valid is crucial in Hanafi muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third form
The fuduli says 'I have settled with you for a thousand' without attributing the payment to himself or specifying the property.
No guarantee (damn) is attached.
2
State the ruling
The contract is mawquf (suspended). It is not immediately valid.
3
Understand the reason
The defendant is the true principal because he gains the benefit of repelling litigation. The fuduli only becomes asil if he adds a guarantee to himself.
See the qiyas: if no guarantee, he acts on behalf of the defendant, so ratification is needed.
4
Note the consequence of ratification
If the defendant ratifies, the sulh becomes valid and the defendant must pay the thousand. If he refuses, the sulh is void.
5
Distinguish from the guaranteed case
Compare with the case where the fuduli guarantees: then he becomes asil and the contract is binding on him without ratification.
This contrast appears later in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ صَالحَتُكَ عَلَى الْفِ فَالْعَقْدُ مَوْقُوفٌ فَإِنْ آجَازَهُ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ جَازَ وَلَزِمَهُ الْأَلْفُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُجِزْهُ بطل لاتَ الْأَصْلَ فِى الْعَقْدِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لَانَّ دَفَعَ الْخُصُومَةِ حَاصِلْ لَهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْفُضُولِي يَصِيرُ أصِيلًا بِوَاسِطَةِ إِضَافَةِ الصَّمَانِ إِلى نَفْسِهِ فَإِذَا لَمْ يَضِفُ بَقِيَ عَاقِدًا مِنْ جِهَةِ الْمَطْلُوبِ فَيَتَوَفَّفُ عَلَى إِجَازَتِهِ قَالَ وَوَجْهُ آخَرَ أَنْ يَقُولَ صَالَحْتُكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْأَلْفِ اَوْ عَلَى هَذَا الْعَبْدِ وَلَمْ يَنْسِبُهُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَا عَيَّنَهُ لِلتَّسْلِيمِ صَارَ شَارِطًا سَلَامَتَهُ لَهُ فَيَتِمُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَلَوِ اسْتَحَقَّ الْعَبْدُ أَوْ وَجَدَ بِهِ عَيْبًا فَرَدَّهُ فَلَا سَبِيلَ لَهُ عَلَى الْمَصَالِحِ لِأَنَّهُ الْتَزَمَ الْإِنْفَاءَ مِنْ مَحَلَّ بِعَيْنِهِ وَلَمْ يَلْتَزِمْ شَيْئًا سَوَاهُ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَ الْمَحَلَّ لَهُ تَمَّ الصُّلْحُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَلَّمْ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ عَلَيْهِ بِشَيْءٍ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَرَاهِمٍ مُسْمَاةٍ وَضَمَنَهَا وَدَفَعَهَا ثُمَّ اسْتَحَقَّتْ أَوْ وَجَدَهَا زُيُوفًا حَيْثُ يَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ نَفْسَه أَصِيلًا فِي حَقِ الضَّمَانِ وَلِهَذَا يُجْبَرُ عَلَى التَّسْلِيمِ فَإِذَا لَمْ يُسَلَّمْ لَهُ مَا سَلَّمَهُ يَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ بِبَدَلِهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کہا کہ میں نے ہزار پر صلح کی تو عقد موقوف ہوگا۔ اگر مدعی علیہ نے اجازت دے دی تو جائز ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس پر ہزار لازم ہوں گے اور اگر اجازت نہ دی تو باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ عقد میں اصل مدعی علیہ ہے اس لئے کہ دفع خصومت اسی کو حاصل ہے مگر فضولی ضمان کو اپنی طرف منسوب کرنے کے واسطہ سے اصیل ہو جاتا ہے اور جب اس نے اپنی طرف نسبت نہیں کی تو وہ مطلوب کی طرف سے عاقد رہا پس مطلوب کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک اور صورت یہ ہے کہ فضولی کہے میں نے ان ہزار پر یا اس غلام پر صلح کی اور اس کو اپنی طرف
And if he says 'I have settled with you for a thousand', then the contract is suspended (mawquf). If the defendant ratifies it, it becomes valid and the thousand becomes binding on him; and if he does not ratify it, it becomes void, because the original party in the contract is the defendant, since the repelling of litigation is obtained by him. But the fuduli becomes a principal (asil) through the addition of guarantee to himself. When he does not add (the guarantee), he remains a contractor from the side of the demanded party, so it depends on his ratification. He (the author) said: And there is another way: that he says 'I have settled with you for this thousand' or 'for this slave', and does not attribute it to himself, because when he specifies it for delivery, he becomes a stipulator of its safety for him, so it is complete by his statement. And if the slave is claimed back (by a third party) or finds a defect and returns it, then there is no recourse for him against the musalih (the fuduli), because he committed to deliver from a specific location and did not commit to anything else. If he delivers the location, the sulh is complete; if he does not deliver, he cannot claim anything from him. As opposed to when he settles for specified dirhams, guarantees them and pays them, then they are claimed back or found to be counterfeit, where he can claim from him (the fuduli), because he made himself a principal in terms of guarantee, and for this he is compelled to deliver; so when what he delivered is not safe for him, he can claim its substitute. Translation: And if he says 'I have settled with you for a thousand', then the contract is suspended. If the defendant gives permission, it becomes valid and the thousand becomes binding on him; and if he does not permit, it becomes void. Because the original party in the contract is the defendant, since the repelling of litigation is obtained by him. But the fuduli becomes asil by way of attributing the guarantee to himself. And when he did not attribute (the guarantee), he remains a contractor on behalf of the demanded party, so it depends on his permission. The author of the Hidayah says: There is another form: that the fuduli says 'I have settled with you for this thousand' or 'for this slave' and does not attribute it to himself... (continues with similar translation).
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth forms of fuduli's sulh as per the Hidayah. The third form occurs when the fuduli says 'I have settled with you for a thousand' without specifying or attributing the payment to his own property and without guaranteeing. In this case, the contract is mawquf (suspended) and requires the defendant's ratification (ijazah) to become binding. The reason is that the defendant is the true principal in the contract because he is the one who benefits from repelling the litigation (daf' al-khusumah). The fuduli only becomes an asil (principal) when he adds a guarantee to himself; lacking that, he remains a contractor on behalf of the defendant, so the contract is contingent on the defendant's approval. If the defendant ratifies, the sulh is valid and the defendant is liable for the thousand; otherwise, it becomes void. The fourth form, described as 'wajhun akhar' (another way), is when the fuduli specifies a particular property (e.g., 'this thousand' or 'this slave') without attributing it to himself. This sulh is valid because by specifying the property for delivery, he effectively stipulates its safety for the plaintiff, and the contract is perfected upon his statement. However, if the specified property is subsequently claimed by a third party (istihqaq) or found defective, the plaintiff has no recourse against the fuduli because the fuduli only committed to deliver that specific property, not any alternative. In contrast, if the fuduli had settled for specific dirhams and guaranteed them, then if those dirhams are found defective or claimed by another, the plaintiff can claim the substitute (badal) from the fuduli, because by guaranteeing, the fuduli made himself a principal in terms of liability and is compelled to deliver a sound equivalent.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A contract that is suspended and not yet binding, pending ratification by the principal party (the defendant).
اجازت (ijazah): Ratification or permission given by the defendant after the contract.
فضولی (fuduli): A person who acts without authority in a contract involving others.
ضمان (damn): Guarantee; taking liability for payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third form of fuduli's sulh, why is the contract considered mawquf?
A) Because the fuduli has no authority at all.
B) Because the defendant is the real principal who benefits from repelling litigation.
C) Because the plaintiff has not yet accepted.
D) Because the property is not specified.

Key Takeaway
The third form of fuduli's sulh is mawquf and requires defendant's ratification because the fuduli acts on the defendant's behalf without making himself liable.

The Specified Property Sulh: When a Fuduli's Offer is Valid but Limited
Explains the fourth form of fuduli's sulh: specified property, valid but limited.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a fuduli's sulh specifying a particular property is immediately valid, and explain why the plaintiff has no recourse if the property is defective or claimed by a third party.

Core Idea
Specifying property in a fuduli's sulh makes it valid and binding, but the risk falls on the plaintiff—no substitute if defective.

The fourth form of fuduli's sulh, also called the 'wajhun akhar', involves the fuduli naming a specific item like 'this thousand' or 'this slave'. Unlike the third form, this sulh is immediately valid because the fuduli stipulates the safety of that particular property. However, this also limits the plaintiff's remedies if something goes wrong. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth form
The fuduli says 'I have settled with you for this thousand' or 'this slave' without attributing it to himself.
The property is specified (mu'ayyan).
2
State the ruling
The contract is valid immediately (sahih) upon his statement. It is not suspended.
3
Understand the reason for validity
By specifying the property for delivery, the fuduli effectively stipulates its safety for the plaintiff. He makes himself a stipulator of safety, so the contract is perfected.
The passage says: 'when he specifies it for delivery, he becomes a stipulator of its safety for him'.
4
Explain the limited recourse
If the property is reclaimed by a third party (istihqaq) or found defective, the plaintiff cannot claim anything from the fuduli. The fuduli only promised that specific property, not a substitute.
Contrast with the case where the fuduli guarantees and pays: then he is liable for substitute.
5
Apply the contrast
If the fuduli had guaranteed and paid specific dirhams, and they are defective, the plaintiff can claim the badal (substitute) because the fuduli made himself a principal in guarantee. But here, no guarantee, so no recourse.
This shows the difference between specifying and guaranteeing.

And if he says 'I have settled with you for a thousand', then the contract is suspended (mawquf). If the defendant ratifies it, it becomes valid and the thousand becomes binding on him; and if he does not ratify it, it becomes void, because the original party in the contract is the defendant, since the repelling of litigation is obtained by him. But the fuduli becomes a principal (asil) through the addition of guarantee to himself. When he does not add (the guarantee), he remains a contractor from the side of the demanded party, so it depends on his ratification. He (the author) said: And there is another way: that he says 'I have settled with you for this thousand' or 'for this slave', and does not attribute it to himself, because when he specifies it for delivery, he becomes a stipulator of its safety for him, so it is complete by his statement. And if the slave is claimed back (by a third party) or finds a defect and returns it, then there is no recourse for him against the musalih (the fuduli), because he committed to deliver from a specific location and did not commit to anything else. If he delivers the location, the sulh is complete; if he does not deliver, he cannot claim anything from him. As opposed to when he settles for specified dirhams, guarantees them and pays them, then they are claimed back or found to be counterfeit, where he can claim from him (the fuduli), because he made himself a principal in terms of guarantee, and for this he is compelled to deliver; so when what he delivered is not safe for him, he can claim its substitute. Translation: And if he says 'I have settled with you for a thousand', then the contract is suspended. If the defendant gives permission, it becomes valid and the thousand becomes binding on him; and if he does not permit, it becomes void. Because the original party in the contract is the defendant, since the repelling of litigation is obtained by him. But the fuduli becomes asil by way of attributing the guarantee to himself. And when he did not attribute (the guarantee), he remains a contractor on behalf of the demanded party, so it depends on his permission. The author of the Hidayah says: There is another form: that the fuduli says 'I have settled with you for this thousand' or 'for this slave' and does not attribute it to himself... (continues with similar translation).
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth forms of fuduli's sulh as per the Hidayah. The third form occurs when the fuduli says 'I have settled with you for a thousand' without specifying or attributing the payment to his own property and without guaranteeing. In this case, the contract is mawquf (suspended) and requires the defendant's ratification (ijazah) to become binding. The reason is that the defendant is the true principal in the contract because he is the one who benefits from repelling the litigation (daf' al-khusumah). The fuduli only becomes an asil (principal) when he adds a guarantee to himself; lacking that, he remains a contractor on behalf of the defendant, so the contract is contingent on the defendant's approval. If the defendant ratifies, the sulh is valid and the defendant is liable for the thousand; otherwise, it becomes void. The fourth form, described as 'wajhun akhar' (another way), is when the fuduli specifies a particular property (e.g., 'this thousand' or 'this slave') without attributing it to himself. This sulh is valid because by specifying the property for delivery, he effectively stipulates its safety for the plaintiff, and the contract is perfected upon his statement. However, if the specified property is subsequently claimed by a third party (istihqaq) or found defective, the plaintiff has no recourse against the fuduli because the fuduli only committed to deliver that specific property, not any alternative. In contrast, if the fuduli had settled for specific dirhams and guaranteed them, then if those dirhams are found defective or claimed by another, the plaintiff can claim the substitute (badal) from the fuduli, because by guaranteeing, the fuduli made himself a principal in terms of liability and is compelled to deliver a sound equivalent.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): When a third party claims ownership of the property delivered as sulh payment.
بدل (badal): Substitute or compensation when the original payment is defective.
معین (mu'ayyan): Specified or particular property, as opposed to unspecific (mawquf).
شرط سلامة (shart salamah): Stipulation of safety; the fuduli implicitly guarantees the property is free from defects or claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fourth form of fuduli's sulh, what is the consequence if the specified property is reclaimed by a third party?
A) The fuduli must provide a substitute.
B) The plaintiff can cancel the sulh and claim the original debt.
C) The plaintiff has no recourse against the fuduli.
D) The defendant must pay instead.

Key Takeaway
The fourth form of fuduli's sulh is valid immediately but the plaintiff assumes the risk of the specific property; no substitute if it fails.

Five Scenarios of a Fuduli's Sulh
Explaining five scenarios of fuduli sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five scenarios of a fuduli's sulh and determine whether each is immediately valid, suspended, or subject to a guarantee, based on the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
A fuduli's sulh is valid only if he guarantees the consideration or specifies the property; otherwise it awaits ratification.

In this lesson, we examine the various ways an unauthorized person (fuduli) can validly conclude a sulh (settlement) on behalf of another. The classical Hanafi jurists identify five scenarios, each with distinct conditions. Understanding these helps determine when the fuduli becomes personally liable and when the contract is merely suspended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline: the fuduli acts without permission
Recognize that the default principal in a sulh is the defendant (مدعى عليه). The fuduli, being a stranger, cannot automatically bind the defendant. The scenarios show how he can become a principal.
2
Scenario 1: Fuduli guarantees the consideration
If the fuduli says 'I made sulh with you on a thousand dirhams, and I guarantee them' (with a guarantee الضمان), the sulh is immediately valid. The fuduli becomes a principal through his guarantee, analogous to a fuduli guaranteeing khula payments.
3
Scenario 2–3: Attribution to own property or delivery
If the fuduli attributes the consideration to his own property (e.g., 'on my slave') or delivers it without attribution, the sulh is valid because the plaintiff receives what he bargains for. The fuduli is obligated to deliver the specific item.
4
Scenario 4: No guarantee, no attribution, no delivery
If the fuduli simply says 'I made sulh with you on a thousand' without guarantee, attribution, or delivery, the contract is suspended (موقوف) until the defendant ratifies. The fuduli remains a contractor on behalf of the defendant.
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars consider it immediately valid like scenario 2.
5
Scenario 5: Specification without attribution
If the fuduli says 'on this thousand' or 'this slave' (pointing to a specific object) without attributing it to himself, the sulh is valid immediately. Specification implies a commitment to deliver that specific item only.
If the specific item is later claimed by a rightful owner or found defective, the plaintiff has no recourse against the fuduli.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

درہموں یا اپنے اس غلام پر صلح کی ۔ اس صورت میں بھی صلح صحیح ہوگی اور فضولی پر وہ ہزار درہم یا وہ غلام سپرد کر نالازم ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس نے صلح کی نسبت اپنے ذاتی مال کی طرف کی تو اس کے سپرد کرنے کا علیہ نے اجازت دے دی تو جائز ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس پر ہزار لازم ہوں گے اور اگر اجازت نہ دی تو باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ عقد میں اصل مدعی علیہ ہے اس لئے کہ دفع خصومت اسی کو حاصل ہے مگر فضولی ضمان کو اپنی طرف منسوب کرنے کے واسطہ سے اصیل ہو جاتا ہے اور جب اس نے اپنی طرف نسبت نہیں کی تو وہ مطلوب کی طرف سے عاقد رہا پس مطلوب کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک اور صورت یہ ہے کہ فضولی کہے میں نے ان ہزار پر یا اس غلام پر صلح کی اور اس کو اپنی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس نے ان کو تسلیم کے لئے معین کر دیا تو مدعی کو سپرد کرنے کی شرط کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ تو اس کے قول سے صلح پوری ہو جائے گی اور اگر غلام مستحق نکل آیا یا اس میں عیب پا کر واپس کیا تو اس کے لئے مصالح پر کوئی راہ نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایک معین محل سے ادائیگی کا التزام کیا تھا۔ اس کے علاوہ کا التزام نہیں کیا تھا۔ پس اگر وہ معین محل اس کو مسلم ہوا تو صلح پوری ہوگئی اور اگر مسلم نہ ہوا تو مصالح پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ بخلاف اس کے جب معین در اہم پر صلح کر کے خود ان کا ضامن ہو کر مدعی کو دے دے پھر وہ مستحق نکل آئیں یا ان کو کھوٹا پائے کہ اس صورت میں مدعی مصالح پر رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے ضمان کے حق میں خود کو اصیل بنایا ہے اسی لئے وہ سپر د کر نے پر مجبور کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس جب وہ مال مدعی کے لئے مسلم نہ رہا تو اس سے بدل صلح واپس لے گا۔ ...... تشریح قوله ولو قال صالحتك....(۴) نہ بدل صلح کا ضامن ہوا نہ اپنے ذاتی مال کی طرف نسبت کی نہ مدعی کو سپر د کیا بلکہ مطلق رکھتے ہوئے یوں کہا کہ میں نے ہزار درہم پر صلح کی اس صورت میں صلح موقوف ہوگی۔ اگر مدعلی علیہ نے اس کو جائز رکھا تو جائز ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ عقد میں اصل تو مدعی علیہ ہی ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ خصومت دفع ہونے کا فائدہ اسی کو حاصل ہوگا۔ لیکن اپنی ذات کی طرف نسبت نہیں کی تو وہ اصیل نہ ہوا بلکہ مطلوب یعنی مدعی علیہ کی جانب سے عقد کرنے والا رہ گیا۔ لہذا صلح اس کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگی۔ پھر یہ بعض مشائخ کے اختیار پر ہے اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قول مذکور بھی صالحنی علی الفی کے مرتبہ میں ہے کہ مصالح پر نافذ ہوگا۔ تو قف تو صرف اس قول میں ہے صالح فلانا۔ قوله قال صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں مذکورہ چار صورتوں کے علاوہ ایک پانچویں صورت بھی ہے اور وہ یہ کہ فضولی نے اپنے مال کی طرف نسبت تو نہیں کی مگر اشارہ سے معین کر کے یوں کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ان ہزار درہموں یا اس غلام پر صلح کی ۔ اس صورت میں بھی صلح صحیح ہو کیونکہ جب اس نے مادر را با کو پر کرنے کے کیاہے تو گویاس نے شہر کی کہ وہ یہ مال دی کو پر کرے گا۔ پس فضولی گی۔ کیونکہ جب اس نے ہزار درہم یا غلام کو سپرد کرنے کے واسطے معین کیا ہے تو گویا اس نے یہ شرط کر لی کہ وہ یہ مال مدعی کو سپر د کرے گا۔ پس فضولی کے قول سے صلح تمام ہو جائے گی۔ قوله ولو استحق العبد.... الخ - پھر اگر وہ غلام جس پر صلح کی تھی کسی نے استحقاق میں لے لیا۔ یا مدعی نے اس میں کوئی عیب پا کر واپس کر دیا یا اس کو آزاد یا مکاتب یامد بر پایا تو اس کو صلح کنندہ پر کوئی راہ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایک معین محل سے ادا ئیگی کا التزام کیا تھا اور وہ غلام ہے جو بدل صلح کے لئے معین ہے ) اس کے سوا اس نے کچھ اور التزام نہیں کیا تھا۔ پس اگر یہ معین محل اس کو مسلم ہوا تو صلح پوری ہوگئی اور اگر مسلم نہ ہوا تو وہ مصالح سے کچھ نہیں لے سکتا۔ (لیکن اپنے دعوی کی طرف رجوع کرے گا)۔ قوله بخلاف ما اذا اصالح ... الخ - اس کے برخلاف اگر اس نے کچھ عین در اہم پر صلح کی پھر خود ضامن ہو کر وہ مدعی کو دے دیئے اس کے بعد وہ مدعی کے پاس سے استحقاق میں لے لئے گئے۔ یا مدعی نے ان کو کھوٹے پا کر واپس کر دیئے تو مدعی کو اختیار ہو گا کہ وہ مصالح سے دوسرے در ہم لے۔ کیونکہ مصالح نے ضمانت کے حق میں خود کو اصیل بنایا ہے اسی لئے اُس پر جبر کیا جاتا ہے کہ مال صلح سپر دکر لے۔ اور جب وہ مال جو مصالح نے سپرد کیا تھا۔ مدعی کے لئے مسلم نہ رہا تو مدعی اس سے عوض صلح واپس لے گا۔
Explanation of his statement: 'And if he made a sulh on behalf of another...' A fuduli person made a sulh on behalf of another without his permission; there are four scenarios. 1) The fuduli made a sulh with a consideration and guaranteed the consideration himself. In this case, the sulh is completed because what the defendant gains is acquittal, and in the matter of acquittal, the defendant and a stranger are equal. So the stranger can become a principal when he guarantees it. Like in the case of a woman taking khula, if a fuduli guarantees the khula wealth, it is valid. And this is a voluntary favor from the stranger-settlor to the defendant, like if he pays the defendant's debt as a favor, it is valid. But if the mentioned sulh was by the defendant's command, he is not a volunteer; rather, despite the guarantee, he will take back the wealth. 2) His statement: 'And nothing belongs to this settlor...' Then that stranger-settlor gets nothing from what he made the sulh with in exchange for wealth from the plaintiff; rather, it remains for whoever has possession because to validate this sulh is as a release (isqat), meaning the plaintiff dropped his right and acquitted the defendant, so it is not an exchange. Then there is no difference regarding the settlor getting nothing whether the defendant admits or denies. His statement: 'On these thousand...' He attributed the consideration to his own property, e.g., he said, 'I made a sulh with you for my own thousand dirhams or my own slave.' In this case too, the sulh is valid, and the fuduli is obligated to deliver those thousand dirhams or that slave, because when he attributed the sulh to his own personal property, he committed to delivering it. He did not attribute to his own personal property, but he delivered the consideration. In this case too, the sulh is valid because the plaintiff's purpose was that he should receive compensation, and he did receive it. If he made a sulh on a thousand, the contract is suspended. If the defendant permits, it is valid; otherwise not. And if he said, 'I made a sulh with you for a thousand,' the contract is suspended; if the defendant authorizes it, it is valid and the thousand is binding; if he does not authorize, it becomes void, because the principal in the contract is the defendant, since the purpose of ending the dispute concerns him. However, the fuduli becomes a principal by attributing the guarantee to himself. So when he does not attribute, he remains a contractor on behalf of the defendant; thus it depends on his authorization. He (al-Marghinani) said: There is another way: he says, 'I made a sulh with you for this thousand or this slave' without attributing it to himself, because when he specified it for delivery, he becomes a stipulator of its delivery to him, so it is completed by his statement. And if the slave is claimed by a rightful owner, or he finds a defect and returns it, then there is no recourse for him against the settlor because he committed to payment from a specific subject matter and did not commit to anything else. If the subject matter is delivered to him, the sulh is complete; if not delivered, he cannot recourse to him for anything. Unlike when he made a sulh on named dirhams and guaranteed them and paid them, then they are claimed or found counterfeit, where he recourses against him, because he made himself a principal with respect to the guarantee; for this reason he is compelled to deliver. So if what he delivered is not secured for him, he recourses against him for its substitute. Translation: And if he said, 'I made sulh on a thousand,' the contract is suspended. If the defendant permits, it becomes valid and the thousand is binding; if he does not permit, it becomes void, because the principal in the contract is the defendant, since the ending of the dispute concerns him. However, the fuduli becomes a principal by attributing the guarantee to himself. When he did not attribute, he remained a contractor on behalf of the defendant; thus it depends on his authorization. The author of al-Hidayah says: There is a fifth scenario: the fuduli says, 'I made sulh on this thousand or this slave' without attributing it to himself, because when he specified them for delivery, he became a stipulator of their delivery to the plaintiff. So by his statement, the sulh is completed. And if the slave is claimed by a rightful owner, or he finds a defect and returns it, then there is no recourse for him against the settlor, because he committed to payment from a specific subject matter and did not commit to anything else. So if that specific subject matter is delivered to him, the sulh is complete; if not delivered, he cannot recourse to the settlor. (But he may return to his claim.) His statement: 'Unlike when he made a sulh...' - Contrary to if he made a sulh on specific dirhams, then himself guaranteed and gave them to the plaintiff, then they were taken by rightful claim, or the plaintiff found them counterfeit and returned them; in that case, the plaintiff has the option to take other dirhams from the settlor, because the settlor made himself a principal in the right of guarantee; for this reason he is compelled to deliver the sulh wealth. And when that wealth that the settlor delivered is not secured for the plaintiff, then the plaintiff takes the substitute from him.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the scenarios of a fuduli (unauthorized agent) making a sulh (settlement) on behalf of another without permission. The text, from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, expands on the matn's ruling. It presents five scenarios: (1) The fuduli makes sulh with a consideration and personally guarantees the consideration; the sulh is valid because the defendant's benefit (acquittal) is achieved, and the fuduli becomes a principal through his guarantee. (2) The fuduli attributes the consideration to his own property; the sulh is valid and he is bound to deliver. (3) The fuduli does not attribute the consideration to himself but delivers it; still valid because the plaintiff receives his due. (4) The fuduli simply says 'I made sulh on a thousand' without guarantee or attribution; the contract is suspended until the defendant ratifies it, because the fuduli is acting on the defendant's behalf. (5) The fuduli specifies the object (e.g., 'this thousand' or 'this slave') without attributing to himself; the sulh is valid because specification implies a commitment to deliver that specific item. If the item is later claimed by a rightful owner or found defective, the plaintiff has no recourse against the fuduli because he only committed to that item, unlike the first scenario where the fuduli guaranteed and is liable. The commentary also notes a difference among later scholars (mashayikh) on whether scenario (4) should be treated as suspended or immediately valid. The ruling follows Hanafi usul where the defendant is the principal in the contract, and the fuduli's authority is limited unless he undertakes personal liability.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudūlī): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without permission.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A contract of settlement ending a dispute, often involving a consideration.
بدل صلح (badal al-ṣulḥ): The consideration given in a sulh contract.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A rightful claim of ownership that invalidates a prior transaction.
موقوف (mawqūf): Suspended; a contract that is not immediately operative but awaits ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario does the fuduli become personally liable for a substitute if the delivered consideration is later claimed by a rightful owner?
A) Scenario 1: The fuduli guaranteed the consideration.
B) Scenario 2: The fuduli attributed the consideration to his own property.
C) Scenario 4: The fuduli said 'on a thousand' without guarantee.
D) Scenario 5: The fuduli specified 'this slave' without attribution.

Key Takeaway
A fuduli's sulh is valid if he guarantees the consideration, attributes it to own property, delivers it, or specifies the object; if none of these, the contract is suspended pending defendant's ratification.

Chapter on Sulh in Debt - Understanding the Scope
Introducing the chapter on sulh concerning debts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific subject of this chapter and explain why it follows the general chapter on sulh.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, specific rules follow general ones; sulh in debt has its own unique considerations.

This opening section of the chapter on sulh in debt (dayn) establishes the context. The author has already covered sulh in general claims. Now, he narrows the focus to debts, which carry distinct rules because a debt is not a specific physical asset but a liability. Understanding this structure helps you navigate the fiqh text and anticipate the specialized rulings ahead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chapter title
Read the Arabic title: 'باب الصلح في الدين'. Note that it specifies 'في الدين' (in debt), indicating the chapter's focus is sulh (compromise) related to debts.
Compare with the previous chapter which was general (الصلح in absolute terms).
2
Understand the sequence of topics
The commentary states: 'because the specific always comes after the general.' Recognize the pedagogical principle: general rulings are taught first, then specific cases. This helps in building a systematic understanding.
This sequence is common in Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah.
3
Define 'dayn' in Hanafi context
In Hanafi fiqh, dayn is a debt or liability not tied to a specific physical asset. It is distinct from 'ayn (specific property). Sulh in debt has its own conditions and rulings, which will be detailed later.
Keep this distinction in mind as it affects the validity and effect of sulh.
4
Appreciate the purpose of the chapter
The chapter's purpose is to provide detailed rules for sulh when the subject is a debt. This includes how a compromise can be made, what is permissible, and the legal consequences.
Subsequent lessons will elaborate on the specific rulings.

Source Text

بـاب الــصــلــح فـــي الــديــن
ترجمہ یہ باب قرضہ میں صلح کرنے کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح قولہ باب ۔ عام دعووں کی طرف سے صلح کا حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد بولی خاص یعنی دعوی دین سے صلح کا حکم بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ کیونکہ خصوص ہمیشہ عموم کے بعد ہی ہوتا ہے۔ (غایه )
Chapter on Sulh in Debt. Translation: This chapter is about making sulh in debt. Explanation of his statement 'Chapter': After explaining the ruling of sulh in general claims, he now addresses a specific type, namely sulh concerning a debt claim, because the specific always comes after the general. (Ghayah)
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This is the opening of a new chapter in the book of Sulh. The author transitions from discussing sulh in general claims (which was covered in the preceding pages) to a specialized treatment of sulh when the subject matter is a debt (dayn). The order is deliberate: general rules first, then specifics. This structure is standard in Hanafi fiqh texts to ensure comprehensive understanding.

Key Terms
باب (bāb): A chapter or section in a fiqh book.
دين (dayn): A debt or liability that is not a specific physical asset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
This chapter narrows the discussion from general sulh to sulh specifically in debts, following the Hanafi pedagogical principle of general-to-specific.
