صاحبین کی دلیل، امام صاحب کی دلیل
لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُه الوُصُولُ إِلى عَيْنِ حَقِهِ صُورَةً وَامْكَنَهُ مَعْنى بِالْقِسْمَةِ مَعَهُ فَكَانَ إِسْتِهْلَاكًا مِنْ وَجْهِ دُونَ وَجْهِ فَيَمِيلُ إِلَى ايْهِمَا شَاءَ وَلَهُ انَّهُ اِسْتِهْلاكَ مِنْ كُلَّ وَجْهِ لِأَنَّهُ فِعْلٌ يَتَعَدَّرُ مَعَهُ الْوُصُولُ إِلَى عَيْنِ حَقِهِ وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِالْقِسْمَةِ لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ مُوجِبَاتِ الشَّرْكَةِ فَلَا تَصْلُحُ مُوجِبَةَ لَهَا وَلَوْ أَبرَأَ الْخَالِطَ لَا سَبِيلَ لَهُ عَلَى الْمَخْلُوطِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ لأَنَّهُ لَا حَقَّ لَهُ إِلَّا فِي الدَّيْنِ وَقَدْ سَقَطَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا بِالْإِبْرَاءِ يَسْقُطُ خِيَرَةُ الصَّمَانِ فَيَتَعَيَّنَ الشَّرْكَةُ فِي الْمَخْلُوطِ وَخَلْطَ الْحِلَّ بِالزِيْتِ وَكُلُّ مَائِعِ بِغَيْرِ جِنْسِهِ يُوجِبُ انْقِطَاعَ حَقَّ الْمَالِكِ إِلَى الصَّمَانِ وَهَذَا بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ إِسْتِهْلَاکَ صُورَةً وَكَذَا مَعْنَى لِتَعَذَّرِ الْقِسْمَةِ بِاعْتِبَارُ اخْتِلَافِ الْجِنْسِ وَمِنْ هَذَا الْقَبِيلَ خَلْطُ الْحِنْطَةِ بِالشَّعِيرِ فِي الصَّحِيحِ لِاَنَّ اَحَدَهُمَا لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ حَبَّاتِ الْآخَرِ فَتَعَدَّرَ التَّمْيِيرُ وَالْقِسْمَةُ وَلَوْ خَلَطَ الْمَائِعَ بِجِنْسِهِ فَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ يَنْقَطِعُ حَقُّ الْمَالِكُ إِلَى الصَّمَانِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يُجْعَلُ الْأَقَلُّ تَابِعًا لِلاكْثَرِ اِعْتِبَارًا لِلْغَالِبِ أَجْزَاءً وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ شِرْكُهُ بِكُلِّ حَالَ لِاَنَّ الْجِنْسَ لَا يَغْلُبُ الْجِنْسَ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فِى الرَّضَاعَ وَنَظِيرُهُ خَلْطُ الدَّرَاهِم بِمِثْلِهَا إِذَابَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مَائِعًا بِالْإِذَابَةِ ترجمه صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کو اپنا عین حق ملنا صور تا ممکن نہیں اور معنی ممکن ہے اس کے ساتھ بٹوارہ کر کے پس یہ من وجہ استبلاک ہے اور من وجہ نہیں ہے تو جس طرف چاہے مائل ہو جائے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو ہر طرح سے استقبلاک ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایسا فعل ہے جس کے ہوتے ہوئے عین حق تک رسائی متعدد ہے اور بٹوارہ کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ شرکت کے احکام میں سے ہے تو موجب شرکت ہونے کے لائق نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر موزع نے خلط کو بری کر دیا۔ تو اس کے لئے مخلوط پر کوئی راہ نہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ اس کا حق صرف دین میں تھا جو ساقط ہو چکا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بری کرنے سے صرف تاوان کا اختیار ساقط ہوا تو مخلوط میں شرکت متعین ہو گئی ۔ تل کے تیل کو روغن زیتون کے ساتھ اور ہر رقیق چیز کو اس کی غیر جنس کے ساتھ ملانا حق مالک کے منقطع ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے ضمان کی طرف اور یہ بالا جماع ہے کیونکہ یہ صورةُ استبلاک ہے۔ اور اسی طرح معنی بھی ہوارہ متعزر ہونے کی بنا پر اختلاف جنس کے اعتبار سے اور اسی قبیل سے ہے۔ گیہوں کو جو کے ساتھ ملانا صحیح قول میں کیونکہ ان میں سے ایک دوسرے کے دانوں سے خالی نہیں ہوتا تو امتیاز اور بٹوارہ معزر ہو گیا۔ اگر رقیق چیز کو اس کی جنس میں خلط کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مالک کا حق منقطع ہو جائے گا۔ ضمان کی طرف اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقل کو اکثر کے تابع کیا جائے گا از راہ اجزاء غالب کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ہر حال میں مودع کا شریک ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک ایک جنس اپنی جنس پر غالب نہیں ہوتی ۔ جیسا کہ کتاب الرضاع میں گزر چکا اور اس کی نظیر درا ہم کو اب کے مثل کے ساتھ خلط کرنا ہے پگھلا کر کیونکہ پگھلانے سے وہ بھی سیال ہو گئے ۔ تشریح قوله لهما انه لا يمكنه صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موقع کے لئے عین حق تک رسائی صورۃ تو ممکن ہیں لیکن از راویعنی ممکن ہے بایں طور کہ مستودع کے ساتھ بٹوارہ کرلے اس لئے کہ جو چیزیں کیل وزن کی جاتی ہیں۔ ان مین قسمت بالا جماع افراز وتعین ہوتی ہیں اس لئے شریکین میں سے ہر ایک اپنا حصہ بلا رضاء وقضاء لے سکتا ہے۔ پس ودیعت ایک لحاظ سے مستہلک ہوئی اور ایک لحاط سے غیر مستہلک۔ پس چاہے ...... جانب قیام کی طرف مائل ہو کر اس کے مثل کا ضامن کر دے اور چاہے جانب قیام کی طرف مائل ہو کر مخلوط میں ساتھی ہو جائے۔ قوله وله انه ... امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خلط کرنا ہر لحاظ سے ودیعت کا استہلاک ہے ۔ کیونکہ خلط ایک ایسا فعل ہے کہ اس کے ہوتے ہوئے عین حق تک مودع کی رسائی محال ہے اور بندوں کی جانب سے استبلاک یہی ہے کہ مئی کو عیب دار کر دے۔ واما انعدام المحل فبتخليق الله تعالی رہا پوارہ سواس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ تو شرکت کے احکام میں سے ہے تو یہ موجب شرکت ہونے کے لائق نہیں ہو سکتا۔ یعنی جب شرکت ہو جانے پر یہ حکم ہوتا ہے کہ بڑارہ کر لیا جائے تو ہوارہ ایسی چیز نہیں ہوسکتا جو شرکت کو واجب کرے۔ قوله ولو ابرأ الخالط ... امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے مذکورہ اختلاف کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مودع نے خلط کنندہ کو بری کردیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مخلوط کے بٹوارہ کی کوئی صورت نہیں۔ کیونکہ آپ کے نزدیک مودع کو صرف تاوان کا اختیار تھا جو مستودع کے ذمہ واجب تھا۔ اور وہ بری کر دینے سے ساقط ہو گیا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بری کرنے سے صرف تاوان کا اختیار جاتا رہا۔ نہیں مخلوط مال میں شرکت کر لینا متعین ہو گیا۔ قوله ومن هذا القبيل. یعنی گیہوں کو جو کے ساتھ ملا دینا بھی صحیح قول میں اسی قبیل سے ہے کہ بالا تفاق مالک کا حق منقطع ہو کر تاوان واجب ہوتا ہے اس واسطے کہ گیہوں اور جو میں سے ہر ایک مین دوسرے کے دانے ملے ہوئے ہوتے ہیں تو عین ودیعت کو حقیقہ ممتاز کرنا متعزر ہے۔ نیز حکما یعنی بذریعہ قسمت بھی تمیز کرنا متعا ر ہے اس لئے کہ غیر جنس ہونے کی وجہ سے بٹوارہ نہیں ہو سکتا کہ یہ غیر مشروع ہے تو لا محالہ تاوان متعین ہوگا۔ پس اپنی ودیعت کے مثل تاوان لے۔ قوله ولو خلط المانع اگر رقیق و سیال چیز کو اس کی جنس میں خلط کر دیا مثلا روغن زیتون ودیعت تھا۔ اس کو روغن زیتون ہی میں ملا دیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مالک کا حق منقطع ہو کر تا وان واجب ہو گا۔ کیونکہ یہ ہر لحاظ سے استہلاک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اجزاء غالب کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اقل کو اکثر کے تابع کریں گے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مودع ہر حال میں مستودع کا ساتھی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اسول یہی ہے کہ ایک جنس خود اپنی جنس پر غالب نہیں ہوتی۔ چنانچہ کتاب الرضاع میں گزر چکا کہ اگر دو عورتوں کا دودھ ملا کر کسی بچہ کو پلایا گیا تو رضاعت دونوں سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا کہ جس عورت کا دودھ غالب ہو اسی سے رضاعت ثابت ہو۔ کیونکہ دونوں دودھ ایک جنس ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر ودیعت کے دراہم کو اپنے دراہم کے ساتھ گلا ڈالا تو اس میں بھی یہی مذکورہ اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ گلانے سے دراہم بھی رقیق و سیال چیز ہوگئی۔
He said: And if he mixed it... If the depositor mixed the deposit with his own property, there are four scenarios: 1. Mixing by adjacency with easy distinction - like mixing white dirhams with black dirhams, or dirhams with dananir, or walnuts with almonds - then without dispute he is not liable. 2. Mixing by adjacency with difficult distinction - like mixing wheat with barley - then without dispute he is liable. 3. Mixing of different kinds by complete intermingling - like mixing sesame oil with olive oil - then without dispute he is liable. 4. Mixing of the same kind - like white dirhams with white dirhams, black dirhams with black dirhams, wheat with wheat, barley with barley - this case is disputed. Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad hold that he is liable, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he has a choice: either he may take liability or become a partner in the mixture. (And Malik said: he becomes a partner without choice.) The proof of the two companions and the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: Their proof is that it is not possible for him to access the exact same property in form, but it is possible in meaning by dividing it with him, so it is consumption from one aspect and not from another, so he may lean towards whichever he wishes. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that it is consumption from every aspect, because it is an act after which access to the exact same property is impossible, and division is not considered because it is among the requirements of partnership, so it cannot be the cause of partnership. And if the depositor discharges the mixer, he has no way over the mixture according to Abu Hanifa, because his right is only in the debt, and it has fallen. According to them, by discharge the choice of liability falls, so partnership in the mixture is determined. Mixing sesame oil with olive oil and every liquid with a different kind necessitates cutting off the owner's right to liability, and this is by consensus, because it is consumption in form and also in meaning due to the difficulty of division due to difference of kind. And of this category is mixing wheat with barley in the correct opinion, because one does not lack grains of the other, so distinction and division become difficult. And if one mixes a liquid with its own kind, then according to Abu Hanifa the owner's right is cut off to liability for what we mentioned; according to Abu Yusuf, the lesser is made a follower of the greater, considering the predominant parts; and according to Muhammad, he is a partner in any case, because according to him one kind does not overcome another kind, as passed in the chapter on suckling. And its analogy is mixing dirhams with their like by melting, because by melting they become liquid. Translation: The proof of the two companions is that the depositor cannot obtain his exact right in form, but he can in meaning by dividing with him. So this is consumption from one aspect and not from another, so he may lean towards whichever he wishes. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that it is consumption in every respect, because it is an act that makes access to the exact right impossible, and division is not considered because it is from the effects of partnership, so it is not suitable to necessitate partnership. And if the depositor discharges the mixer, then he has no way over the mixture according to Imam Abu Hanifa because his right is only in the debt, which has fallen. According to the two companions, by discharge only the choice of liability falls, so partnership in the mixture is determined. Mixing sesame oil with olive oil and every liquid with a different kind necessitates cutting off the owner's right to liability, and this is by consensus, because it is consumption in form and similarly in meaning due to the difficulty of division due to difference of kind. And of this category is mixing wheat with barley in the correct opinion, because each contains grains of the other, so distinction and division become difficult. If a liquid is mixed with its own kind, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the owner's right is cut off to liability for the reason we mentioned. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the lesser is made a follower of the greater, considering the predominant parts. According to Imam Muhammad, the depositor becomes a partner in any case, because according to him one kind does not overcome its own kind, as passed in the chapter on suckling. And its analogy is mixing dirhams with their like by melting, because by melting they become liquid. Elaboration: He said: Their proof is that... The proof of the two companions is that for the depositor, access to the exact right is impossible in form, but possible in meaning by dividing with the depositary, because items that are measured by weight or measure can be divided by consensus by separation and allocation. So each partner can take his share without consent or court. Thus the deposit is consumed from one aspect and not from another. So he may either lean towards the side of liability and become a guarantor of its like, or lean towards the side of remaining and become a partner in the mixture. He said: And his proof is that... The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that mixing is in every respect consumption of the deposit, because mixing is an act after which the depositor's access to the exact right is impossible. And consumption from the side of people is to make the thing defective. As for the non-existence of the substance, that is by creation of Allah. And division is of no consideration because it is among the effects of partnership, so it cannot be the cause of partnership. That is, when partnership exists, it is ruled that division may be done, so division cannot be something that necessitates partnership. He said: And if he discharges the mixer... The fruit of the mentioned disagreement between Imam and the two companions is that if the depositor discharges the mixer, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is no way for division of the mixture, because according to him the depositor only had the choice of liability, which was obligated on the depositary's responsibility, and it fell due to discharge. According to the two companions, by discharge only the choice of liability fell, so partnership in the mixed property became determined. He said: And of this category... Meaning, mixing wheat with barley is also of this category in the correct opinion, that by agreement the owner's right is cut off and liability is obligated, because wheat and barley each contain grains of the other, so true distinction of the deposit is difficult. Also, legally, by means of division, distinction is difficult because being of different kinds, division is not possible as it is not legitimate, so inevitably liability is determined. So he takes the like of his deposit as liability. He said: And if he mixed the liquid... If a liquid thing is mixed with its own kind, e.g., olive oil was deposited and he mixed it with olive oil, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the owner's right is cut off and liability is obligated, because it is consumption in every respect. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, considering the predominant parts, the lesser is made a follower of the greater. According to Imam Muhammad, the depositor is a partner in any case, because according to him the principle is that one kind does not overcome its own kind. As passed in the chapter on suckling, that if milk of two women is mixed and fed to a child, then suckling is established from both, and it is not considered which woman's milk was predominant, because both milks are of the same kind. The author of Al-Hidayah says that its analogy is if the deposited dirhams were melted with his own dirhams, then the same disagreement applies, because by melting the dirhams also become liquid.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on mixing a deposit (wadi'ah) with the depositary's own property. It begins by presenting four scenarios of mixing. The first scenario is mixing by 'adjacency' (mujawarah) where the items can be easily distinguished (e.g., white and black dirhams). Here, the depositary is not liable (ghayr dhamin) by consensus. The second scenario is also mixing by adjacency but with difficult distinction (e.g., wheat with barley). Here, the depositary is liable by consensus. The third scenario is complete intermingling (mumazajah) of different kinds (e.g., sesame oil with olive oil). Again, liability is established by consensus. The fourth scenario is mixing the same kind (e.g., white dirhams with white dirhams). This is the disputed case. According to Imam Abu Hanifa (and also Imams Shafi'i and Ahmad), the depositary is liable and must pay compensation. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the depositor has a choice: either claim liability and take the equivalent, or become a partner in the mixture. Imam Malik adds that the depositor becomes a partner without choice. The passage then presents the proofs. The two companions argue that since the deposit cannot be physically retrieved (consumption in form) but can be retrieved in meaning through division (since items of the same kind can be divided by weight or measure), it is only partially consumed. Therefore, the depositor may choose liability or partnership. Abu Hanifa argues that mixing constitutes complete consumption because it prevents access to the exact property, and division is not a cause of partnership—it is an effect. If partnership existed, division would be possible; but the mixing act itself does not create partnership. A practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is when the depositor discharges (ibra') the depositary from liability: according to Abu Hanifa, since the depositor's right was only in the debt (liability), it falls with discharge; according to the two companions, only the option of liability falls, so partnership becomes determined. The passage then discusses liquids: mixing a liquid with a different kind (e.g., sesame oil with olive oil) cuts off the owner's right to liability by consensus. Similarly, mixing wheat with barley is like mixing different kinds because grains are indistinguishable. For mixing a liquid with its own kind, there is further intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa says liability; Abu Yusuf says the lesser is treated as a follower of the greater (considering majority parts); Muhammad says the depositor is a partner in all cases, as one kind does not overpower another (analogy from suckling where mixed milk of two women establishes relationship from both). Finally, the passage mentions that melting dirhams is analogous to liquid mixing.

Key Terms
خلط (khalṭ): Mixing the deposited property with the depositary's own property, which may result in liability or partnership depending on the type.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate the depositor for the loss of the deposit, usually by paying its equivalent (mithl) or value (qimah).
استہلاک (istihlāk): Consumption or destruction of the deposit, either in form or meaning, such that the depositor cannot retrieve the exact item.
قسمت (qismah): Division of property among co-owners, often by allotting specific parts. In this context, division is considered possible for same-genre items measured by weight or volume.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership or co-ownership in the mixed property, where the depositor owns a share corresponding to his deposit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a depositary mixes a deposit of the same genre (e.g., white dirhams with white dirhams), the depositor has which option?
A) Only claim liability
B) Only become a partner
C) Choose between liability and partnership
D) The depositary is not liable

Key Takeaway
The ruling on mixing deposits depends on the possibility of retrieval; for same-genre items, the Hanafi school offers a choice between liability and partnership.

Mixing Deposit with Different Genus: Liability by Consensus
Establishes ruling for mixing deposit with different genus within the Hanafi school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a deposit of a liquid is mixed with a different genus and identify the evidence of consensus (Ijma) on the liability.

Core Idea
Mixing a deposit with a different genus makes specific return impossible, so the depositee becomes liable (daman) by consensus.

In this lesson, we explore a key rule in the law of deposits (wadi'ah): when a depositee mixes the deposited item with another item of a different genus, the ownership is severed and the depositee incurs liability. This ruling is established by the consensus of scholars (Ijma) and applies to all liquid and similar substances. We will examine the reasoning and the scope of this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is mixing a deposit with a different genus (e.g., liquid with different liquid, wheat with barley). The ruling is that the depositee becomes liable (daman wajib) to compensate with the equivalent (mithl).
The text states 'وجوب ضمان' (obligation of liability).
2
Locate the dalil
The text explicitly says 'بالا جماع' (by consensus), indicating the ruling is established by Ijma. Ijma is a qati' (definitive) evidence.
Ijma of the Companions is the likely source, though not specified.
3
Understand the basis
The reason is that mixing with a different genus constitutes istihlak (destruction) because the original property cannot be distinguished or returned. The owner's right is severed.
The text says 'صورة استهلاک' (a form of destruction).
4
Apply the principle to a specific example
The passage applies the same ruling to mixing wheat with barley, as they are different species. In the correct opinion, each becomes inseparable from the other, so liability arises.
This shows the ruling extends beyond liquids to solids of different genus.
5
Note the authority
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh), not disputed between the three imams.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf reported here.

Source Text

ساتھ اور ہر رقیق چیز کو اس کی غیر جنس کے ساتھ ملانا حق مالک کے منقطع ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے ضمان کی طرف اور یہ بالا جماع ہے کیونکہ یہ صورةُ استبلاک ہے۔ اور اسی طرح معنی بھی ہوارہ متعذر ہونے کی بنا پر اختلاف جنس کے اعتبار سے اور اسی قبیل سے ہے۔ گیہوں کو جو کے ساتھ ملانا صحیح قول میں کیونکہ ان میں سے ایک دوسرے کے دانوں سے خالی نہیں ہوتا تو امتیاز اور بٹوارہ معذر ہو گیا۔
And mixing every liquid thing with its non-genus obligates the severance of the owner's right towards liability, and this is by consensus, because it is a form of destruction. And similarly in meaning, due to the difficulty of distinction based on difference of genus, and from this category is mixing wheat with barley in the correct opinion, because each of them is not free from the grains of the other, so distinction and division becomes difficult.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling for mixing a deposit with something of a different genus (ghayr jins). The depositee becomes liable (daman) because the original property cannot be identified. This is by consensus (ijma). The same applies to mixing wheat with barley, as they are different species and cannot be separated.

Key Terms
رقیق (raqiq): Liquid or flowable substance
غیر جنس (ghayr jins): Different genus or category
استہلاک (istihlak): Destruction or consumption such that the specific item cannot be returned
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate with the like value

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When mixing a deposit with a different genus makes return impossible, the depositee must compensate with the like value, established by consensus.

Mixing Deposit with Same Genus: Three Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mixing same-genre deposits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on mixing a deposit with the same genus and explain the legal consequence of ibra' (discharge) under each view.

Core Idea
Mixing a deposit with its own genus triggers a three-way Hanafi dispute: liability, annexation, or partnership.

When a depositee mixes the deposited item with another of the same genus – for example, mixing deposited olive oil with his own olive oil – the Hanafi imams diverge on the legal effect. Does the depositor lose his specific right and become entitled only to compensation? Or does he remain a co-owner? This lesson parses the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, their proofs, and the practical consequence when the depositor later forgives the depositee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the ruling of each imam: Abu Hanifa (liability/daman), Abu Yusuf (tabi' – minority annexed to majority), Muhammad (partnership/shirkah).
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the owner can still access his specific share through division because the items are measurable. Hence the deposit is only partially consumed.
This proof leads to two sub-positions: Abu Yusuf prefers tabi', Muhammad prefers partnership.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa considers mixing a complete destruction (istihlak) because the owner cannot identify his specific item. The possibility of division is a consequence of partnership, not a cause of it.
4
Apply the thamarah (consequence): ibra'
If the depositor discharges the depositee, Abu Hanifa says no division remains; the Sahibayn say partnership becomes definitive. This illustrates the practical difference.
5
Examine examples
Wheat/barley (different genus) leads to liability by consensus. Olive oil (same genus) triggers the dispute. Melting dirhams is analogous to liquids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہے کہ بڑارہ کر لیا جائے تو ہوارہ ایسی چیز نہیں ہوسکتا جو شرکت کو واجب کرے۔ قوله ولو ابرأ الخالط ... امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے مذکورہ اختلاف کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مودع نے خلط کنندہ کو بری کردیا تو امام دو عورتوں کا دودھ ملا کر کسی بچہ کو پلایا گیا تو رضاعت دونوں سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا کہ جس عورت کا دودھ غالب ہو اسی سے رضاعت ثابت ہو۔ کیونکہ دونوں دودھ ایک جنس ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر ودیعت کے دراہم کو اپنے دراہم کے ساتھ گلا ڈالا تو اس میں بھی یہی مذکورہ اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ گلانے سے دراہم بھی رقیق و سیال چیز ہوگئی۔
If a liquid thing is mixed with its own genus, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the owner's right severs towards liability, for the same reason we mentioned. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the lesser is made subject to the greater by considering the dominant parts. According to Imam Muhammad, the depositor will be a partner in any case, because near him, one thing of the same genus does not dominate another. As passed in Kitab al-Rada'. And its example is mixing dirhams with similar by melting, because by melting they become liquid. Explanation: The proof of the Sahibayn is that the owner can access his actual right in form, because it is possible to divide with the depositee, since things measured by weight and measure can be divided by consensus, so each sharer can take his share without consent or court order. Thus the deposit is in one aspect consumed and in another not consumed. So he may lean towards the side of consumption and hold the depositee liable for its like, or lean towards the side of non-consumption and become a partner. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that mixing is in every aspect consumption of the deposit, because mixing is an act where the owner's access to the specific thing is impossible, and from the perspective of servants, destruction is that which makes the thing defective. As for the absence of the site, that is by Allah's creation, so the aspect of division is not considered, because it is among the rulings of partnership, so it cannot necessitate partnership. The consequence of this difference: if the owner discharges the mixing depositee, then according to Abu Hanifa there is no possibility of division, because the owner only had the option of compensation which was owed, and it falls with discharge. According to the Sahibayn, discharge only removes the option of compensation, and instead partnership in the mixed property becomes definite. And from this category is mixing wheat with barley, in the correct opinion, because by consensus the owner's right severs and compensation becomes obligatory, because each contains grains of the other, so actual distinction is difficult, and also legally division is impossible because of difference of genus, so inevitably compensation is determined. So he takes compensation like his deposit. The statement: 'And if he mixes' — if a liquid thing is mixed with its like, e.g., olive oil deposit mixed with olive oil, then according to Abu Hanifa the owner's right severs and compensation becomes obligatory, because it is consumption in every respect. According to Abu Yusuf, the lesser is made subject to the greater by considering dominant parts. According to Muhammad, the depositor will be a partner in any case, because his principle is that one species does not dominate its own species. As passed in Kitab al-Rada': if the milk of two women is mixed and fed to a child, rada' is established from both, and it is not considered which woman's milk was dominant, because both are the same species. The author of Hidayah says: its parallel is if the depositee melts the deposit dirhams with his own dirhams, then there is the same dispute, because by melting the dirhams become liquid.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on mixing a deposit with the same genus. Three positions: Abu Hanifa: liability (daman) because mixing is complete destruction (istihlak); Abu Yusuf: the lesser is made tabi' to the greater, considering the dominant parts; Muhammad: the depositor becomes a partner (sharik) because one species does not dominate another. The Sahibayn's proof: since weight/measure items can be divided, the owner can recover his specific share, so the deposit is only partially consumed. Abu Hanifa's proof: mixing completely prevents identification, so it is destruction. The consequence is illustrated by the case of ibra' (discharge). If the owner forgives, Abu Hanifa says no division remains; the Sahibayn say partnership is confirmed. Examples: wheat/barley (different genus, so liability) and olive oil (same genus, dispute). Reference to Kitab al-Rada' of milk mixing. Also analogized to melting dirhams.

Key Terms
خلط (khalat): Mixing or blending
جنس (jins): Genus or species
استہلاک (istihlak): Consumption or destruction making identification of the specific item impossible
تبعی (tabi'i): Annexed as a follower to the dominant portion
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The depositee can always return the exact item.
B) The owner can divide the mixture because the items are measurable.
C) The deposit is sacred and cannot be destroyed.
D) The depositee's ownership prevails over the depositor's.

Key Takeaway
Mixing a deposit with the same genus produces an intra-Hanafi dispute between liability (Abu Hanifa), annexation (Abu Yusuf), and partnership (Muhammad), with practical consequences for discharge.

Accidental Mixing Without Action: Partnership, Not Liability
Ruling on accidental mixing without depositee's action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a deposit mixes with the depositee's property without his action and identify the condition that prevents liability.

Core Idea
Accidental mixing without depositee action creates co-ownership, not liability.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a key principle in the law of deposit (wadi'ah): when the deposited property mixes with the depositee's own property without any act on his part, the depositee is not liable. Instead, the owners become partners in the mixed property. This ruling is unanimous among the schools, as the text explicitly states 'by consensus' (bil-ittifaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mixing of the deposit with the depositee's property without any action by the depositee. The ruling is that the depositee is not liable, and the owners become partners.
2
Note the critical condition
The absence of any action (fi'l) by the depositee is the key condition. Without this condition, the ruling would be different (liability).
3
Understand the consequence: partnership
Since there is no wrongdoing, the owners become co-owners in proportion to their contributions. The depositee does not become a guarantor.
4
Recognize the consensus
The text ends with 'and this is by consensus' (wa hadha bil-ittifaq), indicating that all scholars agree on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ خَلَطَتْ بمَالَهُ مِنْ غَيْر فَعَلَهُ فَهُوَ شَرِيكَ لِصَاحِبَهَا كَمَا إِذَا انْشَقَّ الْكِيْسَانُ فَاخْتَلَطَا لأَنَّهُ لَا يَضْمَنهَا لِعَدْمِ الصُّنْعِ فَيَشْتَرِكَانِ وَهَذَا بِالْإِتِفَاقِ. ترجمہ اگر مل گئی ودیعت مودع کے مال میں اس کے کچھ کئے بغیر تو وہ صاحب ودیعت کا سا جبھی ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے دونوں تھیلیاں پھٹ کر دراہم مل گئے ۔ کیونکہ وہ ضامن نہیں ہوگا کوئی حرکت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پس دونوں شریک ہو جائیں گے اور یہ بالا تفاق ہے
He said: And if it mixes with his property without his action, then he is a partner of its owner, just as when two bags tear and mix, because he is not liable due to lack of action, so they become partners, and this is by consensus. Translation: If the deposit mixes with the depositee's property without any action of his, then he becomes a partner of the owner. Like when both bags tear and the dirhams mix. Because he will not be liable due to no action, so both become partners, and this is by consensus.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This is a ruling on accidental mixing where the depositee did not cause the mixing (e.g., bags splitting). Since there is no wrongdoing, the depositee is not liable, and the owners become partners in the mixed property by consensus.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'ah): Deposit; property left with another for safekeeping.
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation; guarantor.
شريك (sharik): Partner; co-owner in the mixed property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The owners become partners in the mixed property.
C) The deposit is considered lost.
D) The contract is void.

Key Takeaway
Accidental mixing without depositee action leads to partnership, not liability, by consensus.

Spending Part of Deposit and Replacing: Liability for All
Ruling on depositee spending part of deposit and mixing its like

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a depositee spends part of a deposit and replaces it with like and mixes it with the remainder, and explain why this leads to full liability.

Core Idea
Mixing a replacement with the remaining deposit destroys identity, imposing full liability.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in wadi'ah (deposit). The depositee has breached trust by spending part of the deposit. Even if he later replaces an equivalent amount, mixing the replacement with the remaining deposit causes confusion of ownership, leading to full liability. You will learn the legal rationale and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the depositee's initial act
The depositee spends part of the deposit, which is a breach of trust (ta'addi). This act alone makes him liable for the spent portion.
2
Describe the subsequent action
He replaces the spent portion with an equivalent amount of the same kind and mixes it with the remaining deposit.
The replacement is his own property.
3
Apply the ruling
Because he mixed his own property with the deposit, the identity of the remaining deposit is destroyed (istihlak). Consequently, he becomes liable for the entire deposit.
4
Understand the rationale
Mixing another's property with one's own without permission renders the original deposit indistinguishable, so the depositee must compensate for all of it.
This follows the earlier principle of istihlak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَانُ انْفَقَ الْمُوْدَعُ بَعْضَهَا ثُمَّ رَدَّ مِثْلَهُ فَخَلَطَهُ بِالْبَاقِي ضَمِنَ الْجَمِيعَ لأَنَّهُ خَلَطَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ بِمَالِهِ فَيَكُونُ إِسْتِهْلاكًا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ. اگر خرچ کرلی مودع نے کچھ ودیعت پھر اسی کے مثل لے کر باقی میں ملا دی تو پوری کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے مال غیر کو اپنے مال میں ملا دیا تو یہ استہلاک ہوا جو پہلے گزر چکی
He said: If the depositee spends some of it, then returns its like and mixes it with the remainder, he is liable for all of it, because he mixed another's property with his own, so it is destruction on the basis mentioned earlier. If the depositee spends some of the deposit, then brings its like and mixes it with the remainder, he will be liable for the whole. Because he mixed someone else's property with his own, so this is the destruction that passed.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This case: the depositee first spends (consumes) part of the deposit, then later obtains an equal amount of the same kind and mixes it with the remaining part of the deposit. Since he deliberately mixed his own property (the replacement) with the deposit (still partly existing), he is effectively destroying the deposit's identity. Thus he becomes liable for the entire deposit (the part he spent and the remaining part). This is consistent with the earlier principle: mixing with one's own property when there is no right to do so makes the depositee liable.

Key Terms
وَدِيعَة (wadi'ah): A deposit; an item entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
إستِهْلاك (istihlak): Destruction; the act of rendering property indistinguishable by mixing it with one's own, making the owner unable to identify his property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the depositee spends part of the deposit, then buys an equal amount and mixes it with the remaining deposit, what is the ruling?
A) He is liable only for the part he spent.
B) He is liable for the entire deposit.
C) He is not liable because he replaced it.
D) He becomes a partner with the owner.

Key Takeaway
A depositee who spends part of a deposit and then mixes a replacement with the remainder becomes liable for the entire deposit.

6 min
Transgression and Its Removal: Daman Ends
Dispute on liability removal after transgression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a depositee's liability ends after transgression and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of incompatibility.

Core Idea
Liability ends when transgression stops; the trust contract revives automatically.

When a depositee exceeds the bounds of trust by using the deposit, he becomes liable. But what happens if he stops? The Hanafi school holds that the liability lifts once the transgression is removed, because the original command to keep the deposit remains absolute. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial effect
When the depositee uses the deposit (riding, wearing, etc.), he becomes liable (daman). The contract of deposit is not nullified but its ruling (trust) is suspended.
Transgression creates liability, but does it terminate the contract?
2
State the Hanafi ruling
If the depositee removes the transgression and retakes possession, liability ceases. He becomes a trustee again without returning to the owner.
The act of entrustment (ida') is still valid and covers all times.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that liability only ends by returning the deposit to the owner because the contract ended upon transgression due to incompatibility between liability and trust.
The contract cannot coexist with liability, so it is permanently severed.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof uses the absolute nature of the command ('keep this property') and the analogy of a hired guard who neglects duty then resumes. The contract's ruling returns when the opposite (liability) is removed.
This is a qiyas: the hired guard becomes trustee again after resuming protection.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi allows the depositee to become trustee again without owner's involvement; Shafi'i requires return to owner. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
In practice, Hanafi depositee can be trusted again after ceasing misuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّى الْمُوْدَعُ فِي الْوَدِيعَةِ بِأنْ كَانَتْ دَابَّةٌ فَرَكِبِهَا أَوْ ثَوْبًا فَلَبِسَهُ أَوْ عَبْدًا فَاسْتَخْدَمَهُ أَوْ أَوْدَعَهَا عِندَ غَيْرِهِ ثُمَّ أَزَالَ التَّعَدِى فَرَدَّهَا إِلى يَدِهِ زَالَ الضَّمَانُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَبْرَأَ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ لِأَنَّ عَقْدَ الْوَدِيْعَةِ ارْتَفَعَ حِيْنَ صَارَ ضَامِنًا لِلْمُنَافَاةِ فَلَا يَبْرَأُ إِلَّا بِالرَّدَّ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ وَلَنَا أنَّ الْأمْرَ بَاقِ لِاطْلَاقِهِ وَارْتِفَاعُ حُكْمِ الْعَقْدِ ضَرُورَةُ ثُبُوتِ نَقِيضِهِ فَإِذَا ارْتَفَعَ عَادَ حُكْمُ الْعَقْدِ كَمَا إِذَا اسْتَاجَرُهُ لِلْحِفْظِ شَهْرًا فَتَرَكَ الْحِفْظِ فِي بَعْضِهِ ثُمَّ حَفَظَ فِي الْبَاقِي فَحَصَلَ الرَّدُّ إِلَى نَائِبِ الْمَالِكِ. تشریح قوله واذ العدی - اگر مودع نے ودیعت پر کسی قسم کی تعدی کی مثل اور بیعت کوئی کپڑا تھا اسکو پہن لیا یا جا نو تھا اس پرسوار ہو گیا یا غلام تھا اس سے خدمت لی۔ اس کے بعد اس نے تعدی ختم کر دی تو ضمان بھی ختم ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں ضمان سے بری نہ ہو گا اس واسطے کہ جب مودع تعدی کی وجہ سے ضامن ہو گیا تو عقد ودیعت مرتفع ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ مضان اور امانت میں منافات ہے۔ لہذا جب تک مالک کے پاس واپس نہ کرے بری نہ ہو گا۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ امر بالحاظ یعنی ایداع ابھی باقی ہے کیونکہ مودع كا قول احفظ هذا المال مطلق ہے جو جمیع اوقات کو شامل ہے۔ رہا ارتفاع حکم عقد یعنی عدم ضمان سودہ اس لئے تھا کہ اس کی نقیض ثابت تھی اور جب نقیض مرتفع ہوگئی تو حکم عقد پھر لوٹ آئے گا۔
He said: When the depositee transgresses in the deposit, such as if it is an animal and he rides it, or a garment and he wears it, or a slave and he uses his service, or he deposits it with another, then removes the transgression and returns it to his own hand, the liability ceases. Al-Shafi'i said: He is not free from liability, because the contract of deposit was terminated when he became liable due to incompatibility, so he is not freed except by returning to the owner. Our proof: The command remains due to its absoluteness, and the raising of the contract's ruling was a necessity due to the establishment of its opposite. So when the opposite is removed, the contract's ruling returns, just as if he hires him for protection for a month, and he leaves the protection for part of it, then protects for the remainder, so the return is to the owner's deputy. Explanation: If the depositee commits any transgression, e.g., wearing a garment, riding an animal, using a slave, then removes the transgression, liability also ends. According to al-Shafi'i, he is not freed from liability because when the depositee became liable due to transgression, the contract of deposit was terminated. Because liability and trust are incompatible. So he is not freed until he returns to the owner. We say: The command (i.e., the entrustment) remains because the depositee's statement 'keep this property' is absolute covering all times. As for the lifting of the contract's ruling (i.e., non-liability), it was only due to the existence of its opposite. When the opposite is removed, the contract's ruling returns.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This section addresses the effect of transgression (ta'addi) by the depositee. If the depositee uses the deposit (e.g., riding an animal, wearing clothes, using a slave, or re-depositing) but then stops the transgression and retakes possession, according to Abu Hanifa (and the Hanafi school), the liability (daman) ends because the act of entrustment is still valid and the contract revives when the transgression ceases. Al-Shafi'i argues that the contract ends upon transgression, so liability continues until the owner receives the property. The Hanafi proof is that the original command (to keep) is absolute, and the contract's ruling is suspended temporarily due to transgression but returns when the transgression is removed. An analogy is given of an hired guard who neglects his duty for part of the month but then resumes; he is considered to have returned the trust to the owner's deputy (himself as the original guardian). So the ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression exceeding the bounds of the trust, e.g., using the deposit without permission
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a depositee rides the deposited animal (transgression) but then dismounts and keeps it safely, what happens to his liability?
A) He remains liable until returning the animal to the owner.
B) His liability ends because he removed the transgression.
C) He becomes a partner in the animal.
D) The contract is void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a depositee's liability ends the moment he removes the transgression and holds the deposit as a trustee again, without needing to return it to the owner.

Depositee's Liability After Demand and Denial
Ruling on depositee's liability after demand and denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a depositee becomes liable when the owner demands the deposit and the depositee denies it, and explain why the liability persists even if the depositee later admits to the deposit.

Core Idea
Demand plus denial severs the trust; later admission does not revive it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical moment in a deposit (wadi‘ah) contract: what happens when the owner demands the return of the deposited item and the depositee refuses to acknowledge it? The ruling establishes that the depositee becomes liable (damin) immediately upon denial, and even a subsequent admission does not relieve that liability. Understanding the reasoning—based on termination of the contract from both sides—is essential for correctly applying the law of trusts in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: owner demands the deposit, depositee denies it. The ruling: the depositee becomes liable (daman).
Liability here means obligation to compensate the value of the deposit if it is lost or damaged after the denial.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta‘lil)
The text explains: the demand for return (talab al-radd) effectively removes (azl) the depositee from the trust position, and the denial (jahd) is a dissolution (faskh) of the contract. With the trust terminated, withholding the item becomes wrongful possession (ghasb), hence liability.
'Ghāṣib' (usurper) is a legal category that triggers strict liability.
3
Consider the effect of subsequent admission
Even if the depositee later admits (i‘tirāf) to the deposit, the liability remains because the contract was already terminated. The owner's demand and the depositee's denial together dissolved the contract irrevocably.
This prevents a depositee from 'undoing' the breach by changing his story.
4
Analogize to similar cases
The text draws an analogy to an agent (wakil) who denies the agency. If the principal demands return of authority and the agent denies, the agency is dissolved. The same principle applies across fiduciary contracts.
This shows consistency in Hanafi law for contracts based on trust (amānah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ طَلَبَهَا صَاحِبُهَا فَجَحَدَهَا ضَمِنَهَا لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا طَالَبَهُ بِالرَّةِ فَقَدْ عَزَلَهُ عَنِ الْحِفْظِ فَبَعْدَ ذَالِكَ هُوَ بالْإِمْسَاكِ غَاصِبُ مَانِعٌ مِنْهُ فَيَضْمَنُهَا فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى الْإِعْتِرَافِ لَمْ يَبْرَأُ عَنِ الصَّمَانِ لِارْتِفَاعِ الْعَقْدِ إِذِ الْمُطَالَبَةٌ بِالرَّةِ رَفْعَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ وَالْجُحُودِ فَسْخٌ مِنْ جِهَةِ الْمُودَعِ كَجُحُودِ الْوَكِيلِ الْوَكَالَةِ وَجُحُودِ أَحَدِ
He said: If its owner demands it and he denies it, he becomes liable for it, because when he demanded its return, he removed him from the trust, so after that, by withholding, he is a usurper preventing it, so he is liable. If he returns to acknowledging, he is not freed from liability because the contract is lifted, since the demand for return is a revocation from his (the owner's) side, and the denial is a dissolution from the depositee's side, like the denial of the agent of the agency and the denial of one...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when the owner demands his deposit and the depositee denies having it. The depositee becomes liable (daman) because the demand for return effectively revokes the trust, and the denial is a breach. Even if he later admits, he remains liable because the contract has been terminated by both sides (demand = termination by owner; denial = dissolution by depositee). An analogy is made to an agent who denies his agency.

Key Terms
جحد (jahd): Denial, refusal to acknowledge the deposit
عزل (azl): Removal from the trust position
فسخ (faskh): Dissolution of the contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because his admission is a new contract that makes him liable.
B) Because the owner's demand and his denial together terminated the original trust contract.
C) Because he never actually had the deposit.
D) Because the owner did not accept the admission.

Key Takeaway
A depositee who denies the deposit after the owner's demand becomes liable, and that liability is not undone by later admission because the trust contract was already dissolved.

Liability for Commingling Deposit with Own Property
Two contrasting rulings on commingling of deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for commingling of a deposit with the depositary's property, distinguishing between accidental mixing and intentional replacement.

Core Idea
No liability for accidental mixing; intentional spending and replacement creates full guarantee.

This lesson presents two key rulings from al-Hidayah on the commingling (ikhtilat) of a deposited property (wadi'ah) with the depositary's own property. The rule hinges on whether the mixing occurred through the depositary's deliberate action or without any act on his part. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when the depositary becomes liable (damin).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) mixing without any action (e.g., two bags breaking accidentally), and (2) mixing after spending and replacing part of the deposit.
2
Determine the presence of deliberate action
In scenario 1, there is no action by the depositary, so he remains a trustee (amin). In scenario 2, he spends and replaces, which is a deliberate act that breaches trust.
The key factor is the depositary's 'fi'l' (action).
3
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For scenario 1: the property becomes a shared partnership (sharik) proportional to each owner's share. For scenario 2: the depositary guarantees the entire amount because mixing after spending constitutes destruction (istihlak) of the deposit.
The agreement (bil-ittifaq) on scenario 1 indicates no intra-madhhab difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ خَلَطَتْ بِمَالِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ فِعْلٍ فَهُوَ شَرِيكٌ لِصَاحِبِهَا كَمَا إِذَا انْشَقَّ الْكِيسَانِ فَاخْتَلَطَا لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَضْمَنُهَا لِعَدَمِ الصُّنْعِ فَيَشْتَرِكَانِ وَهَذَا بِالِاتِّفَاقِ. قَالَ فَإِنْ أَنْفَقَ الْمُوْدَعُ بَعْضَهَا ثُمَّ رَدَّ مِثْلَهُ فَخَلَطَهُ بِالْبَاقِي ضَمِنَ الْجَمِيعَ لِأَنَّهُ خَلَطَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ بِمَالِهِ فَيَكُونُ اسْتِهْلَاكًا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ.
He said: And if it mixes with his property without any action, then it is a partner with its owner, just as when two bags split and they mix, because he does not guarantee it due to the absence of action, so they become partners. And this is by agreement. He said: And if the depositary spends some of it, then returns its like and mixes it with the remainder, he guarantees all of it, because he mixed another's property with his property, and thus it is destruction in the manner that preceded.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the matn of al-Hidayah regarding the commingling of a deposited property (wadi'ah) with the depositary's own property. The first ruling: if the mixture occurs without any deliberate act by the depositary—such as two bags containing coins accidentally tearing and the coins mixing—the property becomes a common pool in proportion to each owner's share. The depositary does not become a guarantor (damin) because he did no action (la yadmanuha li-'adam al-sun'). The second ruling: if the depositary intentionally spends a portion of the deposit, then replaces it with similar property and mixes it with the remainder, he becomes liable (damin) for the entire amount. This is because by mixing another's property with his own, he has effectively destroyed the other's property (istihlak) as discussed earlier. The agreement (bil-ittifaq) on the first ruling indicates no intra-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
وَدِيعَة (wadī'ah): Property entrusted by one person to another for safekeeping without compensation.
مُودَع (mūdi'): The person who deposits property (the depositor).
تَعَدِّي (ta'addī): Transgression or exceeding proper bounds; any act that breaches the trust of the deposit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The depositary guarantees the entire mixed amount.
B) The depositary and owner become partners in proportion.
C) The depositary is not liable but must separate the coins.
D) The owner loses his property.

Key Takeaway
Accidental mixing creates partnership; deliberate spending and replacement creates full liability.

8 min
Removal of Ta'addi Restores Amana
Inter-madhhab dispute on ta'addi removal and amana restoration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when a depositary's guarantee ceases after ta'addi and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A depositary who stops his transgression and regains custody becomes an amin again—the contract is suspended, not dissolved.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of ceasing a transgression (ta'addi) after it has occurred. The Hanafis argue that the depositary's liability (daman) ends as soon as he stops the unauthorized act and takes the property back into his own custody. Al-Shafi'i, however, maintains that only returning the item to the owner can restore the trust. We will explore the proofs from both sides and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Read the opening statement: when the depositary removes ta'addi and returns the property to his own hand, the guarantee ceases. Notice the examples given.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that the contract of deposit is dissolved when liability arises, so only direct return to the owner nullifies the guarantee.
The key concept is 'munafah' (contradiction) between amana and daman.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the original command to keep remains; the contract's ruling was only removed by necessity. When the necessity ceases, the ruling returns. They support this with an analogy of a hired guard.
Note the istihsan (juristic preference) in the analogy.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a depositary who stops using the item and regains custody is no longer liable; under Shafi'i, liability continues until the owner receives the item.
This difference affects real-life scenarios like borrowed items or valet parking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّى الْمُوْدَعُ فِي الْوَدِيعَةِ بِأَنْ كَانَتْ دَابَّةً فَرَكِبَهَا أَوْ ثَوْبًا فَلَبِسَهُ أَوْ عَبْدًا فَاسْتَخْدَمَهُ أَوْ أَوْدَعَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِ ثُمَّ أَزَالَ التَّعَدِّي فَرَدَّهَا إِلَى يَدِهِ زَالَ الضَّمَانُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَبْرَأُ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ لِأَنَّ عَقْدَ الْوَدِيعَةِ ارْتَفَعَ حِينَ صَارَ ضَامِنًا لِلْمُنَافَاةِ فَلَا يَبْرَأُ إِلَّا بِالرَّدِّ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْأَمْرَ بَاقٍ لِإِطْلَاقِهِ وَارْتِفَاعُ حُكْمِ الْعَقْدِ ضَرُورَةُ ثُبُوتِ نَقِيضِهِ فَإِذَا ارْتَفَعَ عَادَ حُكْمُ الْعَقْدِ كَمَا إِذَا اسْتَأْجَرَهُ لِلْحِفْظِ شَهْرًا فَتَرَكَ الْحِفْظَ فِي بَعْضِهِ ثُمَّ حَفَظَ فِي الْبَاقِي فَحَصَلَ الرَّدُّ إِلَى نَائِبِ الْمَالِكِ
He said: And when the depositary commits ta'addi in the deposit—such as it being an animal and he rides it, or a garment and he wears it, or a slave and he employs him, or he deposits it with someone else—then he removes the ta'addi and returns it to his own hand, the guarantee ceases. Al-Shafi'i said: He is not freed from the guarantee because the contract of deposit was terminated when he became liable due to the contradiction; so he is not freed except by returning to the owner. And our proof is that the command (to keep) remains due to its absoluteness, and the removal of the contract's ruling is a necessity of the existence of its opposite; so when the opposite ceases, the ruling of the contract returns—like hiring him for safekeeping for a month, and he leaves the safekeeping for part of it, then safeguards for the remainder, so the return to the owner's deputy is achieved.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of ceasing transgression (ta'addi) after it has occurred. The Hanafi ruling: if the depositary (mustawda') commits any act of ta'addi—such as riding a deposited animal, wearing a garment, using a slave, or re-depositing with another—but then removes that transgression and resumes physical custody (yad), the guarantee (daman) ceases. The depositary once again becomes an amin (trustee). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that once the depositary becomes liable (damin), the contract of wadi'ah is dissolved due to the inherent contradiction between amana (trust) and daman (liability). Therefore, only returning the property directly to the owner (owner's hand) can nullify the guarantee. The Hanafi response: the original command of safekeeping remains in effect (al-amr baqi) because it was absolute. The termination of the contract's ruling (i.e., the amana status) was only a necessary consequence of the ta'addi—it was a suspension, not an annulment. Once the cause (the ta'addi) is removed, the original ruling of amana returns, just as a hired guard who neglects his duty for a part of the month but then resumes is still a custodian for the remainder. Thus, returning the property to his own custody (which is a return to the owner's deputy) restores his status as amin.

Key Terms
تَعَدِّي (ta'addī): Any act by the depositary that exceeds the limits of safekeeping, such as use, riding, wearing, or re-depositing without owner's permission.
ضَمَان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of the deposited property due to ta'addi or negligence.
أَمَانَة (amānah): The trust status of a depositary; he is not liable for loss without his fault.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a depositary wears a deposited cloak, then takes it off and returns it to his own custody, what is the ruling?
A) He remains liable until the cloak is returned to the owner.
B) The guarantee ends and he becomes an amin again.
C) The contract of deposit is void ab initio.
D) He must pay compensation but is still an amin.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a depositary who ceases his transgression and regains custody of the deposit is restored to the status of an amin (trustee), and his liability (daman) ceases.

Denial of Deposit: Owner Demand vs Non-Owner Inquiry
Rulings on depositary's denial and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal effect of a depositary's denial when it occurs after the owner's demand versus when it occurs in front of a non-owner, and apply the mufta bihi (Abu Yusuf's position) to determine liability.

Core Idea
Denial to owner dissolves contract and imposes liability; denial to non-owner is protective and does not.

This passage explores a critical nuance in the law of deposits: does every denial by a depositary trigger liability? The owner's demand terminates the trust, so denial thereafter makes the depositary a usurper. But denial to a third party is seen as a protective measure. Understanding this intra-Hanafi dispute sharpens your ability to apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Scenario A: Denial after owner's demand
Identify the depositary's liability upon denial after the owner demands return. Note that the contract is dissolved and liability is fixed even if the depositary later admits.
Key: the owner's demand is an implicit termination (azl).
2
Scenario B: Denial to a non-owner
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says no liability, Zufar says liability. Understand Abu Yusuf's reasoning: denial to others is protective and the depositary cannot unilaterally terminate his custody.
Distinguish between denial to owner and denial to non-owner.
3
Trace the qiyas argument
See how the ruling on denial to owner is analogized to denial of agency and denial of sale. Recognize that the owner's demand acts as termination (azl) from his side, and denial dissolves from the depositary's side.
Analogy reinforces that the contract is fully terminated.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
Determine the relied-upon position: Abu Yusuf's view that denial to a non-owner does not impose liability. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Knowing the mufta bihi prevents incorrect application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ طَلَبَهَا صَاحِبُهَا فَجَحَدَهَا ضَمِنَهَا لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا طَالَبَهُ بِالرَّدِّ فَقَدْ عَزَلَهُ عَنِ الْحِفْظِ فَبَعْدَ ذَلِكَ هُوَ بِالْإِمْسَاكِ غَاصِبٌ مَانِعٌ مِنْهُ فَيَضْمَنُهَا فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى الِاعْتِرَافِ لَمْ يَبْرَأْ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ لِارْتِفَاعِ الْعَقْدِ إِذِ الْمُطَالَبَةُ بِالرَّدِّ رَفْعٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ وَالْجُحُودُ فَسْخٌ مِنْ جِهَةِ الْمُودَعِ كَجُحُودِ الْوَكِيلِ الْوَكَالَةَ وَجُحُودِ أَحَدِ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ الْبَيْعَ فَتَمَّ الرَّفْعُ أَوْ لِأَنَّ الْمُودِعَ يَتَفَرَّدُ بِعَزْلِ نَفْسِهِ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الْمُسْتَوْدَعِ كَالْوَكِيلِ يَمْلِكُ عَزْلَ نَفْسِهِ بِحَضْرَةِ الْمُوَكِّلِ وَإِذَا ارْتَفَعَ لَا يَعُودُ إِلَّا بِالتَّجْدِيدِ فَلَمْ يُوجَدِ الرَّدُّ إِلَى نَائِبِ الْمَالِكِ بِخِلَافِ الْخِلَافِ ثُمَّ الْعَوْدُ إِلَى الْوِفَاقِ وَلَوْ جَحَدَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِهَا لَا يَضْمَنُهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرٍ لِأَنَّ الْجُحُودَ عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِ مِنْ بَابِ الْحِفْظِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ قَطْعَ طَمَعِ الطَّامِعِينَ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ عَزْلَ نَفْسِهِ بِغَيْرِ مَحْضَرٍ مِنْهُ أَوْ طَلَبِهِ فَبَقِيَ الْأَمْرُ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ
He said: If the owner demands it and he denies it, he guarantees it, because when he demanded its return, he removed him from safekeeping, so after that, by retaining it, he is a usurper preventing it, so he guarantees it. Then if he returns to acknowledgment, he is not freed from the guarantee due to the termination of the contract, since the demand for return is a dissolution from his side, and the denial is a cancellation from the depositary's side—like the denial of agency by an agent and the denial of sale by one of the two contracting parties, so the dissolution is complete. Or because the depositor alone must terminate himself in the presence of the depositary, like an agent who can terminate himself in the presence of the principal. And when it is terminated, it does not return except by renewal, so the return to the owner's deputy is not found—unlike opposition then return to agreement. And if he denies it in the presence of someone other than the owner, he does not guarantee it according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Zufar, because denial in the presence of another is a form of preservation, for it cuts the greed of the greedy, and because he does not have the power to remove himself without his presence or his demand, so the command remains—unlike when it is in his presence.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal consequences of a depositary denying the deposit after the owner demands its return. Two scenarios are covered: (A) Denial in front of the owner, and (B) Denial in front of a non-owner. For scenario A: When the owner demands the deposit and the depositary denies having it, the depositary becomes liable (damin). The reason is that the owner's demand constitutes an implicit termination of the depositary's authority to keep, and the denial is a cancellation of the contract from the depositary's side. Therefore, the contract is dissolved. Even if the depositary later admits the deposit, he does not revert to being an amin because the contract has been terminated from both sides—analogous to an agent denying his agency or a party denying a sale. The only way to restore the amana is through a new contract. This is contrasted with the earlier case of ta'addi (khilaf khilaf) where returning from violation restored the trust; here the contract is fully dissolved. For scenario B: If the depositary denies the deposit to someone other than the owner (e.g., a third party), the ruling according to Abu Yusuf is that he does not become liable. Zufar disagrees. Abu Yusuf's reasoning: denial before a non-owner is actually a protective measure—it discourages potential claimants (qat' tama' al-tami'in). Moreover, the depositary cannot unilaterally terminate his own custody without the owner's presence or demand. Therefore, the original command of safekeeping remains intact. The distinction is that in front of the owner, the demand itself effects termination; in front of others, no termination occurs. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
جُحُود (juḥūd): Denial or refusal to acknowledge possession of the deposit when demanded by the owner or asked by a third party.
عَزْل (ʿazl): Removal or termination of the depositary's authority over the deposit, either by the owner's demand or by the depositary's own action.
غَاصِب (ghāṣib): Usurper; one who wrongfully withholds property belonging to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, if a depositary denies the deposit to a stranger who asks about it (not the owner), what is the ruling?
A) The depositary becomes liable for the deposit.
B) The depositary does not become liable.
C) The deposit contract is dissolved.
D) The depositary must compensate the stranger.

Key Takeaway
A depositary's denial after owner's demand dissolves the contract and imposes liability; denial to a non-owner does not, according to the preferred Hanafi position.

6 min
Ruling on Denial of Deposit After Demand
Ruling with proof on deposit denial after demand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deposit denial after demand, explain why subsequent acknowledgment does not remove liability, and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning denial in front of a non-owner.

Core Idea
Denial after demand terminates the deposit contract and imposes permanent liability — even later admission does not restore trust.

This passage from a classical Hanafi text addresses what happens when an owner demands his deposit and the depositee denies having it. The ruling is not only about liability but also about the legal effect of denial on the contract itself. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar regarding denial in front of third parties. Understanding this ruling requires parsing the key terms: طلب (demand), جحد (denial), ضمان (liability), and عزل النفس (self-removal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its immediate consequence
Locate the phrase 'فَإِنْ طَلَبَهَا فَجَحَدَهَا ضَمِنَ'. This establishes that demand + denial = liability. Note the verb ضَمِنَ (he becomes liable).
The word ضَمِنَ is the legal term for being held responsible for compensation.
2
Understand the legal reason (علة)
The text says 'لِأَنَّهُ حِينَ طَلَبَ عَزَلَهُ عَنِ الْحِفْظِ'. The demand removes the depositee from his role as trusted custodian. His subsequent retention is that of a wrongful holder (مانع).
The concept of 'عزل' (removal) is key: the owner's demand cancels the trust relationship.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy) to confirm contract termination
The text compares the situation to an agent who removes himself and to two contracting parties who cancel a sale. Both examples show that mutual termination ends the contract permanently.
The analogy is: demand = termination from owner's side, denial = termination from depositee's side, together they complete the rescission.
4
Distinguish physical breach (تعدي) from verbal denial
The text notes that if the depositee had previously violated instructions but later returned to compliance, the contract remains. But verbal denial is different because it is a statement that explicitly terminates the relationship.
Physical acts of misuse (تعدي) do not automatically rescind the contract; verbal denial does.
5
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute on denial in front of non-owner
Find the phrase 'وَلَوْ جَحَدَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِهَا لَا يَضْمَنُهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ'. Abu Yusuf says no liability because it is protective; Zufar holds otherwise. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's.
The reasoning is based on the inability of the depositee to remove himself without the owner's presence or request.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ طَلَبَهَا فَجَحَدَهَا ضَمِنَ لِأَنَّهُ حِينَ طَلَبَ عَزَلَهُ عَنِ الْحِفْظِ فَبَقِيَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مَانِعًا فَيَضْمَنُ فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلَى الِاعْتِرَافِ لَا يَخْرُجُ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ لِارْتِفَاعِ الْعَقْدِ لِأَنَّ الطَّلَبَ رَفْعٌ مِنْ جَانِبِهِ وَالْجُحُودَ رَفْعٌ مِنْ جَانِبِهِ كَوَكِيلٍ عَزَلَ نَفْسَهُ وَكَالْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ رَفَعَا الْبَيْعَ فَتَمَّ الرَّفْعُ أَوْ لِأَنَّ الْمُودَعَ يَتَفَرَّدُ بِعَزْلِ نَفْسِهِ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الْمُسْتَوْدَعِ كَالْوَكِيلِ يَمْلِكُ عَزْلَ نَفْسِهِ بِحَضْرَةِ الْمُؤَكِّلِ وَإِذَا ارْتَفَعَ لَا يَعُودُ إِلَّا بِالتَّجْدِيدِ فَلَمْ يُوجَدِ الرَّدُّ إِلَى نَائِبِ الْمَالِكِ وَبِخِلَافِ الْخِلَافِ ثُمَّ الْعَوْدِ إِلَى الْوِفَاقِ وَلَوْ جَحَدَهَا عِنْدَ غَيْرِ صَاحِبِهَا لَا يَضْمَنُهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ لِأَنَّ الْجُحُودَ عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِ مِنْ بَابِ الْحِفْظِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ قَطْعَ طَمَعِ الطَّامِعِينَ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ عَزْلَ نَفْسِهِ بِغَيْرِ مَحْضَرٍ مِنْهُ أَوْ طَلَبِهِ فَبَقِيَ الْأَمْرُ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ
If [the owner] demands it [the deposit] and [the depositee] denies it, he becomes liable [for compensation] because when [the owner] demanded, he removed him from the guardianship [of the deposit], so after that he remains a preventer [i.e., wrongful holder] and thus he is liable. Then if he returns to acknowledgment, he does not exit from liability due to the termination of the contract, because the demand is a termination from [the owner's] side and the denial is a termination from [the depositee's] side, like an agent who removes himself and like two contracting parties who cancel a sale, so the termination is complete. Or because the depositor is exclusively entitled to remove himself in the presence of the depositee, like the agent who has the right to remove himself in the presence of the principal. And when [the contract] is terminated, it does not return except by renewal, so the return to being the owner's deputy is not found. And contrary to [the case of] violation then return to compliance. And if he denies it [the deposit] in the presence of other than its owner, he does not become liable for it according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Zufar, because denial in front of others is from the category of protection, because in it there is cutting off the greed of the greedy, and because he does not have the right to remove himself without his [the owner's] presence or his request, so the matter remains, contrary to when it [the denial] is in his presence.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the depositee's denial of the deposit after the owner demands its return. The author presents the Hanafi position, then an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar, and explains the reasoning.

First ruling: When the owner demands the deposit and the depositee denies having it, the depositee becomes a guarantor (ضامن) and is liable for compensation if the deposit is lost. The reason: the demand effectively removes the depositee from his role as an entrusted custodian (أمين). After that, his retention of the deposit becomes that of a usurper (غاصب), so he is liable.

Second ruling: If the depositee later admits to the deposit, he does not become free from liability because the contract of deposit (عقد الوديعة) has been terminated. The demand acts as a rescission from the owner's side, and the denial acts as a rescission from the depositee's side, just as an agent rescinds his own agency in the principal's presence, or as two contracting parties rescind a sale. Once the contract is terminated, it cannot revive without a new agreement. Therefore, even after admission, the depositee remains a guarantor until he actually returns the deposit to the owner.

Third ruling: If the depositee denies the deposit to someone other than the owner, he does not become liable according to Imam Abu Yusuf, contrary to Imam Zufar. The reasoning is that denial in front of others is a form of protection because it discourages thieves and greedy people. Moreover, the depositee cannot remove himself from the role of custodian without the owner's presence or demand. Therefore, the trust relationship (امانت) remains intact. This is unlike denial in the owner's presence, which does terminate the contract.

The commentary also notes the difference between this case and a previous case where the depositee acts contrary to the owner's instructions but later returns to compliance. In that case, the depositee remains a custodian. The difference is that acting contrary to instructions is a physical act (فعل), not a verbal rescission (قول), so the contract does not terminate. Denial, being a statement (قول), can terminate the contract like the owner's demand.

Key Terms
جحد (juhud): Denial by the depositee of having received the deposit.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation, meaning the depositee must pay the value if the deposit is lost.
عزل النفس (azl al-nafs): Self-removal from the role of custodian or agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the owner demands his deposit and the depositee denies it in front of a third party, what is the ruling?
A) The depositee becomes liable in all cases.
B) The depositee becomes liable only if the denial is in front of the owner.
C) The depositee does not become liable if the denial is in front of others, according to Abu Yusuf.
D) The depositee becomes liable only if he later admits.

Key Takeaway
Denial of a deposit after demand terminates the deposit contract and makes the depositee liable for compensation; this liability persists even if the depositee later admits.
