Ruling on Traveling with the Deposit
Presents Hanafi positions on whether depositee may travel with deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on traveling with a deposit and evaluate the proofs of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The depositee may travel with the deposit; the command is absolute, and costs are his burden.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Hanafi fiqh: may the depositee travel with the entrusted deposit? Abu Hanifa permits it absolutely, while his two disciples restrict it for heavy items, and Imam al-Shafi'i forbids it completely. Understanding the reasoning behind each position reveals important usul principles about absolute commands, custom, and analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify the rulings of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and al-Shafi'i on traveling with a deposit.
Abu Hanifa permits even if heavy; Sahibayn permit only if no extra cost; Shafi'i prohibits absolutely.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
His proof is the absolute command (itlaq al-amr) and analogy to a father/guardian traveling with a minor's property.
The command to protect the deposit gives the depositee broad discretion.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's objection
They argue that the cost of returning a heavy deposit restricts permission, as the owner would not consent to such expense.
Custom and implied consent are their basis.
4
Evaluate al-Shafi'i's position
He restricts protection to cities by custom and analogizes to hired custody.
Hanafi response: hired custody is a contract of exchange, so place matters; deposit is gratuitous.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the depositee can travel with any deposit; according to Sahibayn, he cannot if heavy; according to Shafi'i, he cannot at all.
The depositee's liability differs: under Abu Hanifa, no liability unless owner explicitly prohibits travel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلِلْمُودَعِ أَنْ يُسَافِرَ بِالْوَدِيعَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهَا حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهَا حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ لِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِطْلَاقُ الْأَمْرِ وَالْمَفَازَةُ مَحَلٌّ لِلْحِفْظِ إِذَا كَانَ الطَّرِيقُ آمِنًا وَلِهَذَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْأَبُ وَالْوَصِيُّ فِي مَالِ الصَّبِيِّ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُهُ مُؤْنَةُ الرَّدِّ فِيمَا لَهُ حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَرْضَى بِهِ فَيُقَيَّدُ بِهِ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُقَيِّدُهُ بِالْحِفْظِ الْمُتَعَارَفِ وَهُوَ الْحِفْظُ فِي الْأَمْصَارِ وَصَارَ كَالْإِسْتِحْفَاظِ بِأَجْرٍ قُلْنَا مُؤْنَةُ الرَّدِّ يَلْزَمُهُ فِي مِلْكِهِ ضَرُورَةَ امْتِثَالِ أَمْرِهِ فَلَا يُبَالِي بِهِ وَالْمُعْتَادُ كَوْنُهُمْ فِي الْمِصْرِ لَا حِفْظُهُمْ وَمَنْ يَكُونُ فِي الْمَفَازَةِ يَحْفَظُ مَالَهُ فِيهَا بِخِلَافِ الْإِسْتِحْفَاظِ بِأَجْرٍ لِأَنَّهُ عَقْدُ مُعَاوَضَةٍ فَيَقْتَضِي التَّسْلِيمَ فِي مَكَانِ الْعَقْدِ وَإِذَا نَهَاهُ الْمُودِعُ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ بِالْوَدِيعَةِ فَخَرَجَ بِهَا ضَمِنَ لِأَنَّ التَّقْيِيدَ مُفِيدٌ إِذِ الْحِفْظُ فِي الْمِصْرِ أَبْلَغُ فَكَانَ صَحِيحًا
He said: The depositee may travel with the deposit, even if it has carrying cost and expense, according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not have that [right] when it has carrying cost and expense. And Al-Shafi'i said: He does not have that in either case. For Abu Hanifa: the command is absolute, and the desert is a place of protection if the road is safe, and for this reason the father and the guardian have that right over the property of the minor. And for the two: that the cost of return becomes binding on him for that which has carrying cost and expense, so apparently [the owner] is not pleased with it, so it is restricted accordingly. And Al-Shafi'i restricts it by customary protection, which is protection in cities, and it becomes like hired custody. We say: The cost of return is binding on him in his ownership out of necessity to comply with his command, so he does not mind it. And the custom is that they are in the city, not their protection [that matters]; and whoever is in the desert guards his property there. Contrary to hired custody, because it is a contract of exchange, so it requires delivery at the place of contract. And if the depositor prohibits him from taking the deposit out [of the city] and he takes it out, he becomes liable because the restriction is beneficial, since protection in the city is more effective, so it is valid.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether the depositee (المودع) may travel with the deposit. Three positions are stated: Abu Hanifa permits it even if the deposit is heavy and incurs expense; the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prohibit it if it has weight and expense; Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits it absolutely.

Abu Hanifa's proof: The command to safeguard the deposit is absolute (إطلاق الأمر), meaning the depositee may choose any safe place, including travel. Moreover, a desert journey (مفازة) can be a place of protection if the road is safe. By analogy, a father or guardian may travel with the orphan's property for its protection, and the same applies here. The depositee is entrusted with the deposit and may decide what is best for its safety.

The Sahibayn's proof: If the deposit is heavy and has carrying costs, the expense of returning it would fall on the depositee. Since the owner would not normally consent to such expense, the permission is restricted to cases without extra cost. Their reasoning is based on custom: typically, deposits are kept in the city where no extra travel cost is incurred.

Al-Shafi'i's position: He restricts the depositee's authority to customary protection, which means keeping the deposit in the city (مصر). He analogizes it to a hired custodian, who must keep the item at the place of contract. The Hanafi response refutes this: the cost of return is borne by the depositee as part of complying with the owner's command (امتثال أمره), so the owner does not mind. Additionally, protection in the desert is sometimes better than in the city. The analogy to hired custody is invalid because that is a contract of exchange (معاوضة), where the place of delivery is specified, unlike a deposit which is a gratuitous contract.

Lastly, if the owner explicitly prohibits travel, the depositee must comply; if he violates, he becomes liable because the owner's restriction is valid and protection in the city is more reliable.

Key Terms
إطلاق الأمر (itlaq al-amr): The absolute nature of the command to protect the deposit, implying no restriction on location.
مؤنة الرد (mu'nat al-radd): The expense of returning the deposit, which according to Sahibayn is a consideration but Abu Hanifa dismisses it.
الاستحفاظ بأجر (al-istihfath bi-ajr): Hired custody, a contract of exchange where the custodian is paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is it permissible for the depositee to travel with the deposit even if it incurs cost?
A) Because the depositee can charge the owner for the cost.
B) Because the command to protect is absolute and the cost is borne by the depositee.
C) Because traveling is always safer than staying in the city.
D) Because the owner has given explicit permission.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the depositee may travel with the deposit, even if heavy, because the command to protect is absolute and he bears the cost; however, the owner's explicit prohibition must be respected.

Custodian's Liability: Contradiction vs. Denial of Deposit
Ruling on custodian liability after compliance after contradiction vs. confession after denial with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule distinguishing custodian liability after contradiction versus denial and list the five conditions for liability after denial.

Core Idea
Contradiction is an act, not a verbal rejection; compliance restores trust. Denial is verbal, breaks trust, but liability requires conditions.

A custodian (mustawda‘) is a trustee, not liable for loss unless he transgresses. But what happens if he first disobeys the depositor's instructions or denies the deposit outright? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: the status of the custodian depends on whether his breach was an action (contradiction) or a statement (denial). Even after denial, liability is not automatic—five specific conditions must be met for compensation to be wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage to differentiate: (1) custodian first contradicts (acts against command) then complies; (2) custodian first denies (verbally rejects receipt) then confesses. Note the different outcomes.
The key is that a command is a statement, so only a statement can properly respond to it.
2
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The author draws an analogy: a person who disobeys a divine command (e.g., skips prayer) does not become a disbeliever, but one who denies the command does. Similarly, contradictory action does not nullify the trust, but verbal denial does.
This analogy (qiyas) shows why action vs. statement matters in law.
3
List the five conditions for liability after denial
Memorize the five conditions from the passage: (1) denial after owner's demand, (2) custodian moved the deposit during denial, (3) no fear of a third party destroying the deposit, (4) custodian did not produce the deposit after denial, (5) denial made in presence of the owner.
Each condition must be present; absence of any one prevents liability.
4
Apply the rules to a new scenario
Take a case: owner demands deposit, custodian denies, moves it, but later produces it. Determine liability by checking each condition. Practice with multiple hypotheticals.
Focus on condition 4: if the custodian produces the deposit so the owner can take it, liability is removed (new bailment if owner says keep it).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخالفت کے بعد موافقت کی صورت میں مستودع رہے گا اور انکار کے بعد اقرار کی صورت میں مستودع نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی اصل وجہ یہ ہے کہ کرنے سے مودع کے امر کار نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ امر ایک قول ہے جس کا ردو اس کے مثل قول ہی سے ہو سکتا ہے حالانکہ خلاف کرنا قول نہیں ہے بلکہ فعل و ہے۔ بخلاف جو دو انکار کے کہ یہ قول ہے اور امر آمر کا رد ہے کیونکہ انکار کنندہ خود کو عین شئی کا مالک کہتا ہے اور یہ طاہر ہے کہ مالک اپنی ملک میں غیر کی طرف سے حفاظت کا مامور نہیں ہوتا اس اصل کی دلیل اور امر شرعیہ ہیں کہ اگر کوئی شخص کسی امر خداوندی کا انکار کر دے تو وہ کافر ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور کسی حکم کی خلاف ورزی کرے مثلاً نماز نہ پڑھے تو کافر نہیں ہوتا۔
فائده .... انکار ودیعت کے بعد اقرار کرنے سے تاوان کا وجوب چند شرطوں کے ساتھ مشروط ہے۔
۱۔ انکار ودیعت مالک کے مطالبہ کے بعد ہو تو اگر مالک نے موقع سے ودیعت کا حال دریافت کیا کہ وہ کیسی ہے اور موزع نے ودیعت کا انکار کیا پھر وہ تلف ہوگئی تو تاوان نہ ہو گا۔
۲۔ موڈع نے انکار کے زمانہ میں ودیعت کو اس جگہ سے منتقل کر لیا اگر منتقل نہیں کیا اور وہ تلف ہو گئی تو تاوان نہ ہوگا۔ انکار کے وقت کوئی ایسا شخص موجود نہ ہو جس سے ودیعت تلف کر ڈالنے کا اندیشہ ہو۔ اگر کوئی ایسا شخص موجود ہو تو انکار ودیعت سے تاوان لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسے شخص کے سامنے انکار کرنا حفاظت و نگہبانی میں داخل ہے۔
۴۔ انکار کے بعد ودیعت کو حاضر نہ کیا ہوا اگر اس نے ودیعت کو اس طرح حاضر کر دیا کہ مالک اس کو لینے پر قادر تھا۔ پھر مالک نے اس سے کہا کہ تو اس کو اپنے پاس ودیعت رہنے دے تو مودع پر تاوان باقی نہ رہے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ ابداع جدید ہے۔
۵۔ ودیعت کا انکار مالک کے سامنے ہو اگر کسی اور کے سامنے انکار کیا تو تاوان نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ انکار حفظ ودیعت میں داخل ہے۔
In the case of compliance after contradiction, the custodian remains a custodian; in the case of confession after denial, he does not become a custodian. The fundamental reason is that doing (the contradictory act) does not respond to the depositor's command, because a command is a statement and its response can only be by a similar statement, whereas contradiction is not a statement but an action. Unlike denial, which is a statement and a rejection of the commander's command, because the denier claims ownership of the very thing, and it is clear that an owner is not commanded by another to guard his own property. The proof of this principle is from divine commands: if someone denies a divine command, he becomes an infidel; but if he violates a command (e.g., does not pray), he does not become an infidel. Benefit: The obligation of compensation after denying a deposit is conditional upon several conditions: 1. The denial of the deposit occurred after the owner's demand; if the owner asked about the deposit and the custodian denied it, then it was lost, no compensation. 2. The custodian moved the deposit during the time of denial; if he did not move it and it was lost, no compensation. 3. At the time of denial, there was no person present from whom there was fear of the deposit being destroyed; if such a person was present, denial does not necessitate compensation because denying in front of such a person is a form of protection. 4. After denial, the deposit was not produced; if he produced it such that the owner could take it, then the owner said 'leave it as a deposit with you', the custodian is no longer liable because that is a new bailment. 5. The denial of the deposit was in front of the owner; if he denied in front of someone else, no compensation because denial is included in protection of the deposit.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the nuanced rulings regarding a custodian's liability when he first contradicts the depositor's instructions and later complies, or when he denies the deposit and later confesses. The author states that if the custodian initially acts contrary to the depositor's command (e.g., uses the deposit or moves it without permission) but then later complies with the command, he remains a trusted custodian (mustawda') and is not liable for any loss that occurs after compliance. However, if he denies the deposit outright (saying 'I never received it' or 'it is mine') and later admits to it, he does not regain the status of a trusted custodian; instead, he remains a trespasser and is liable for the deposit unless certain conditions are met. The reasoning is that a command (amr) is a verbal act, and only a verbal response can properly answer it. Contradiction is an action, not a verbal response, so it does not nullify the command; it is like someone who disobeys a divine command but does not deny it—such a person does not become an infidel. Denial, on the other hand, is a verbal rejection of the command itself, and thus it destroys the trust relationship entirely. However, liability for compensation after denial is not absolute. The author lists five conditions that must be present for compensation to be obligatory: (1) the denial must occur after the owner demands the deposit; (2) the custodian must have moved the deposit during the period of denial; (3) there must be no fear of a third party destroying the deposit at the time of denial; (4) the custodian must not have produced the deposit for the owner after denial; and (5) the denial must be made in the presence of the owner. These conditions reflect the Hanafi principle that the custodian's liability arises only when he truly acts in breach of trust.

Key Terms
مستودع (mustawda‘): The person who receives the deposit and is entrusted with its safekeeping; a trustee (amin) as long as he abides by the terms.
تاوان (tawān): Compensation or monetary liability for the deposit if it is lost or damaged due to the custodian's fault.
انکار (inkār): Denial of the deposit, i.e., the custodian asserts that he never received it or that it belongs to him.
مخالفت (mukhalafa): Acting contrary to the depositor's command or instructions (e.g., using the deposit without permission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for liability (tawān) after denial of a deposit?
A) The denial must be made in the presence of the owner.
B) The custodian must have moved the deposit during the denial period.
C) The denial must have occurred after the owner demanded the deposit.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Contradiction (action) does not break the trust; compliance restores it. Denial (speech) breaks trust, but liability for compensation after denial is conditional upon five specific circumstances that reflect true breach of trust.

Custodian Traveling with Deposit: Inter-Madhhab Analysis
Dispute on traveling with deposit: three positions with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, Shafi'i) on whether a custodian may travel with a deposit, explain each school's proof, and apply the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
A custodian may travel with a deposit according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn and Shafi'i disagree based on expense and custom.

This lesson tackles a classic dispute in the law of deposits (wadiah). The basic permission to travel with a deposit becomes contested when the deposit is heavy or expensive to transport. We will explore the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, his two disciples, and Imam al-Shafi'i, and see how the Hanafi school settles the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and al-Shafi'i regarding travel with a deposit. Note the key difference: Abu Hanifa permits unconditionally; Sahibayn permit only if no weight/expense; Shafi'i never permits.
The passage begins with 'Qala' (al-Quduri) stating Abu Hanifa's view, then 'Wa qala' for the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
Examine his proof: the absolute nature of the depositor's command (itlaq al-amr), the desert as a safe place if the road is safe, and the analogy to a father or guardian taking a minor's property on travel.
The text says: 'Li Abi Hanifata itlaq al-amr wa al-mafazatu mahallun lil-hifzi idha kana al-tariqu aminan.'
3
Analyze the opposing proofs
Study the Sahibayn's concern over expense of return (mu’nat al-radd) and Shafi'i's reliance on customary safekeeping (hifz muta‘arif), which he defines as keeping in the city.
The Sahibayn argue that the owner would not consent to bearing the return expense; Shafi'i analogizes to a hired guard who must keep the item at the contract place.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand the rebuttal: the expense of return is borne by the custodian voluntarily as part of executing the owner's command, so the owner does not object; custom does not restrict safekeeping to cities — people in deserts protect their property there.
The text says: 'Qulna mu’nat al-raddi yalzimuhu fi milkihi darurata imthali amrihi fala yubali bihi wa al-mu‘tadu kawnuhum fi al-misri la hifzuhum.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast practical outcomes: under Abu Hanifa, a heavy deposit like a cow or bag of grain can be taken on a journey; under the Sahibayn, it must be left behind unless light; under Shafi'i, never without explicit permission from the owner.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, but if the owner explicitly forbids travel, all agree the custodian must obey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلِلْمُودَعِ اَنْ يُسَافِرَ بِالْوَدِيْعَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهَا حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَالَا لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَالِكَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهَا حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَالِكَ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ لِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِطْلَاقُ الْأَمْرِ وَالْمَفَازَةُ مَحَلٌّ لِلْحِفْظِ إِذَا كَانَ الطَّرِيقُ مِنًا وَلِهَذَا يَمْلِكُهُ الآبُ وَالْوَصِيُّ فِى مَالِ الصَّبِيِّ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُهُ مُؤْنَةُ الرَّةِ فِيمَا لَهُ حِمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَرْضَى بِهِ فَيُقَيَّدُ بِهِ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُقَيدُهُ بِالْحِفْظِ الْمُتَعَارَفِ وَهُوَ الْحِفْظُ فِي الْأَمْصَارِ وَصَارَ كَالْإِسْتِحْفَاظِ بِأَجْرٍ قُلْنَا مُؤْنَةُ الرَّةِ يَلْزَمُهُ فِى مِلْكِهِ ضَرُورَةَ اِمْثَالَ اَمْرِهِ فَلَا يُبَالِي بِهِ وَالْمُعْتَادُ كَوْنُهُمْ فِي الْمِصْرِ لَا حِفْظُهُمْ وَمَنْ يَكُونُ فِي الْمَفَازَةِ يَحْفَظُ مَالَهُ فِيهَا بِخِلَافِ الْإِسْتِحْفَاطِ بِأَجْرٍ لِأَنَّهُ عَقْدٌ مُعَاوَضَةٌ فَيَقْتَضِي التَّسْلِيمَ فِي مَكَانِ الْعَقْدِ وَإِذَا نَهَاهُ الْمُوْدِعُ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ بِالْوَدِيْعَةِ فَخَرَجَ بِهَا ضَمِنَ لِأَنَّ التَّقْسِيدَ مُفِيدٌ إذِ الْحِفْظِ فِي الْمِصْرَ ابْلَعُ فَكَانَ صَحِيحًا
He (al-Quduri) said: The custodian may travel with the deposit, even if it has weight and expense, according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may not do so if it has weight and expense. Al-Shafi'i said: He may not do so in either case. For Abu Hanifa (the proof is) the absolute nature of the command (to keep); and the desert is a place of safekeeping if the road is safe; for this reason the father and guardian may take it (the deposit) regarding the property of a minor. For the two (the proof is) that the expense of return becomes obligatory on him for something that has weight and expense, so it is apparent that the owner would not consent, so the absolute is restricted by this. And al-Shafi'i restricts it by customary safekeeping, which is safekeeping in cities, and it becomes like safekeeping for hire. We reply: The expense of return becomes obligatory on him in his own property out of necessity to execute his (the owner's) command, so he has no concern; and it is customary that they (people) are in the city, not that they protect (their property there); one who is in the desert protects his property there, unlike safekeeping for hire because that is a compensatory contract and requires delivery in the place of contract. And if the depositor forbids him to take the deposit out (of the city) and he takes it out, he becomes liable, because the restriction is beneficial as safekeeping in the city is more complete, so the restriction is valid.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents a classic dispute in the law of deposits (wadiah) concerning whether the custodian (mustawda‘) may take the deposit on a journey. The base text (from al-Hidaya) states the ruling: Abu Hanifa permits it unconditionally, even if the deposit is heavy or costly to transport. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) forbid it if the deposit involves expense or burden. Imam al-Shafi'i forbids it entirely, allowing travel only with customary safekeeping, which in his view means keeping it in the city. The commentary provides the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the depositor's command to keep the deposit is absolute (mutlaq) and not restricted to a particular place. Moreover, if the traveler takes the deposit with him, it may be safer on a safe road, just as a father or guardian may take a minor's property on a journey. The Sahibayn argue that if the deposit requires expense (like porterage or fodder), the owner would likely not consent to such expense, so the absolute command is restricted by implicit conditions. Al-Shafi'i's view is that the default understanding (urf) is safekeeping in the city; any travel would require extra care, akin to a hired guard who must keep the item at the place of contract. The Hanafi response is that the expense of return falls on the custodian as part of executing the owner's command, so the owner would not mind; and people commonly protect their property wherever they are, including in the desert. However, if the depositor explicitly prohibits travel, then the custodian must obey, because the restriction enhances safekeeping. This dispute illustrates how different schools apply the principles of absolute vs. restricted commands, customary practice (urf), and the nature of the deposit contract.

Key Terms
ودیعة (wadī‘ah): A deposit; property entrusted by the owner (mūdi‘) to a custodian (mustawda‘) for safekeeping without compensation.
مؤنہ الرَّد (mu’nat al-radd): The expense or cost of returning the deposit to the owner, e.g., transportation costs.
حفظ متعارف (hifẓ muta‘ārif): Customary safekeeping; the manner of protection that is normal and expected in a given context.
إطلاق الأمر (iṭlāq al-amr): The absolute nature of a command; an unrestricted directive that does not specify conditions or limitations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the primary proof for allowing the custodian to travel with the deposit?
A) The deposit is the custodian's property.
B) The depositor's command is absolute and not restricted to a location.
C) The owner explicitly allowed travel.
D) The deposit is always safe in deserts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (mufta bihi) permits a custodian to travel with a deposit even if heavy, as long as the owner has not prohibited it.

Delivering One Depositor's Share: The Sahibayn Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint deposit delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on joint deposit delivery and explain why Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi over the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A custodian cannot divide joint property; only a court can order qismah.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when two people jointly deposit a fungible item with one custodian, and only one depositor appears to claim his share, should the custodian hand it over? Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say yes. The disagreement hinges on whether giving a share is a division (qismah) requiring authorization, or simply a return of the depositor's own property. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the rules of joint ownership and the limits of a custodian's authority.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that the custodian must not deliver the share until all depositors are present. Identify the key principle: the depositor's right is in the common (mushtarak) property, not in a specific separated portion (mufraz).
The same ruling applies to any fungible (makil/mawzun) item.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The Sahibayn say the custodian may deliver the share to the present depositor. They analogize to joint debt: a debtor can pay one creditor his share without the others' consent.
The dispute is limited to items measured by volume or weight.
3
Analyze the proof of each side
Abu Hanifa: delivering a part is a de facto division (qismah). The custodian has no authority to divide co-owned property. The Sahibayn: the depositor demands what he himself deposited, which is his right; the custodian should comply.
Contrast with joint debt: debts are discharged by equivalents, not by specific items.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Sahibayn's analogy to debt fails because debt is paid from the like (mithl), not from the exact same physical item. Here, the deposit is a specific item, so giving a part is a division.
The text also notes that the depositor could theoretically take his share himself, but that does not compel the custodian to hand it over.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the school. It is more cautious and protects the rights of all depositors until they can jointly decide on division.
This ruling applies today: if two people deposit a bag of grain with a neighbor, the neighbor cannot give half to one without the other present.

قَالَ وَإِذَا أَوْدَعَ رَجُلَانِ عِندَ رَجُلٍ وَدِيْعَةً فَحَضَرَ أَحَدَهُمَا يَطْلُبُ نَصِيبَهُ لَمْ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ نَصِيبَهُ حَتَّى يَحْضُرَ الآخَرُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ نَصِيبَهُ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ ثَلَاثَةٌ إِسْتَوْدَعُوا رَجُلًا أَلْفًا فَغَابَ إِثْنَانِ فَلَيْسَ لِلْحَاضِرِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ نَصِيبَهُ عِنْدَهُ وَقَالَا لَهُ ذَالِكَ وَالْخِلَافُ فِي الْمَكِيْلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ وَهُوَ الْمُرَادُ بِالْمَذْكُورٍ فِى الْمُخْتَصَر لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ طَالَبَهُ بدَفَع نَصِيبهِ فَيُؤْمَرُ بالدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي الدَّيْنِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِتَسْلِيم مَا سَلَّمَ إِلَيْهِ وَهُوَ النِّصْفُ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ فَكَذَا يُؤْمَرُ هُوَ بِالدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةٌ أَنَّهُ طَالَبَهُ بِدَفْعِ نَصِيْبِ الْغَائِبِ لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِالْمُفْرَزِ وَحَقَّهُ فِى الْمُشَاعِ وَالْمُفْرَزُ الْمُعَيَّنَ يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى الْحَقَّيْنِ وَلَا مَيَّزُ حَقَّهُ إِلَّا بِالْقِسْمَةِ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُودَعِ وِلَايَةُ الْقِسْمَةِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَقَعُ دَفْعُهُ قِسْمَةٌ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ بِخِلَافِ الدَّيْنِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِتَسْلِيمٍ حَقِهِ لاَنَّ الدُّيُون تُقْضَى بِاِمْثَالِهَا وَقَوْلُهُ لَهُ اَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ قُلْنَا لَيْسَ مِنْ ضَرُورَتِهِ أَنْ تجْبَرَ الْمُوْدَعُ عَلَى الدَّفْعِ كَمَا إِذَا كَانَتْ لَهُ أَلْفُ دِرْهَمٍ وَدِيْعَةً عِنْدَ إِنْسَانِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْقُ بِغَيْرِهِ فَلِغَرِيْمِهِ أَنْ
He (al-Quduri) said: When two men deposit something with a man (as a deposit), and one of them comes asking for his share, he (the custodian) shall not give him his share until the other comes, according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He gives him his share. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Three men deposit 1000 (dirhams) with a man; two are absent, the one present may not take his share according to him (Abu Hanifa). And the two said: He may do so. And the dispute is concerning things measured by volume or weight, which is meant by what is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar. For the two (the proof is): He demands the payment of his share, so he (the custodian) is ordered to pay him, as in a joint debt. This is because he demands delivery of what he himself handed over, which is half. For this reason he (the depositor) may take it himself; similarly, the custodian is ordered to pay him. For Abu Hanifa (the proof is): He demands the payment of the absent one's share, because he demands a separated (mufraz) part, but his right is in the common (mushtarak) property. A specific separated part contains both rights, and his right cannot be distinguished except by division. The custodian has no authority to divide; for this reason, his delivery is not considered a division by consensus. Unlike a joint debt, because he demands delivery of his right, since debts are discharged by their equivalents. And his statement that he (the depositor) may take it himself: We say it does not necessarily follow that the custodian is compelled to pay, just as if he (someone) has a thousand dirhams as a deposit with a person and owes a debt to another, then his creditor may... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: two or more persons jointly deposit a fungible item (like grain or money) with one custodian. If one depositor comes later and demands his share, can the custodian hand it over in the absence of the other depositor(s)? Abu Hanifa prohibits this, ruling that the custodian cannot deliver any part until all owners are present. The two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, permit it, analogizing to a joint debt where the debtor can pay one creditor his share. The disagreement stems from the nature of the deposit: Abu Hanifa considers the deposited item as a physical, joint property (mushtarak). To give a specific portion (mufraz) to one owner would be a de facto division (qismah), which the custodian is not authorized to perform. The Sahibayn argue that since each depositor has a right to his share of what he entrusted, he can demand it just as a partner can demand his share of a debt. Abu Hanifa's view is stronger because the custodian is not a qasim (divider) and cannot partition a co-owned physical asset. The dispute is limited to items that are measured by volume or weight (makil or mawzun), not distinctive items. The passage then begins to discuss another analogy with a creditor claiming a deposit, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā‘): Common or joint property; an undivided share in a physical item that is not yet separated.
مفرز (mufraz): Separated or distinct portion; a physically delineated part of a co-owned item.
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of co-owned property into shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason given by Abu Hanifa for not allowing the custodian to deliver one depositor's share in the absence of the other?
A) The custodian does not trust the depositor.
B) The custodian has no authority to divide co-owned property.
C) The depositor has not shown proof of ownership.
D) The other depositor has forbidden it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's ruling: a custodian must not deliver one joint depositor's share until all owners are present, because doing so is an unauthorized division of joint property.

Ruling on Traveling with a Deposit and the Dispute on its Conditions
Expansion probe of the dispute on depositary's travel with deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a depositary traveling with a deposit and distinguish it from the views of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The depositary may travel with the deposit even at the owner's expense, because the duty of protection is absolute.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school and beyond: when may a depositary (custodian) travel with the entrusted property? The matn states a general permission, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i impose restrictions. By working through this passage, you will understand the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences for the depositary and owner.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling from the matn
Identify the basic ruling: the depositary may travel with the deposit. This is the default position presented in the text.
The matn says 'the depositary may travel' – this is the starting point.
2
Identify the conditions for the depositary's travel
From the commentary, extract the two conditions: the owner must not have prohibited, and there must be no fear of loss. Without these, the permission is lost.
If the owner prohibits, the depositary becomes liable (dhaman) if he takes the deposit out.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ: Abu Hanifa allows travel even if carriage hire is needed; the Sahibayn prohibit if carriage hire is needed. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the depositary must bear the expense or leave the deposit behind.
This is a legitimate difference of ijtihad within the Hanafi school.
4
Map the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits travel with the deposit entirely, because he restricts the contract of deposit to customary protection within cities. Understand why his premise differs.
Shafi'i considers 'customary protection' (hifz muta'raf) to be location-specific.
5
Trace the Hanafi response to objections
Analyze how the Hanafi school (via Abu Hanifa) responds to both objections: the expense is part of fulfilling the order of protection; protection is not tied to a city but to whatever place the person is in.
The command to protect is absolute and not restricted by time or place.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوديعة.
شہروں میں حفاظت کرنا ہے اور یہ اجرت پر حفاظت کرانے کی طرح ہو گیا۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ واپسی کا خرچہ اس کی ملک میں اس کے حکم کی ضرورت سے لازم ہوگا تو اس کی کوئی پرواہ نہیں کی جائے گی اور معتاد خودان کا شہر میں ہونا ہے نہ کہ ان کا حفاظت کرنا اور جو شخص جنگل میں ہو وہ اپنے مال کی حفاظت جنگل ہی میں کرتا ہے بخلاف اجرت پر حفاظت کرانے کے۔ کیونکہ یہ عقد معاوضہ ہے۔ پس عقد کی جگہ میں سپرد کرنے کا مقتضی ہے اگر مودع نے اس کو ودیعت باہر لے جانے سے منع کر دیا اور وہ باہر لے گیا تو ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ قید لگانا مفید ہے اس لئے کہ شہر میں پوری حفاظت ہوتی ہے تو قید لگا نا صحیح ہوا۔
یہی ہے کہ مالک اس سے راضی نہ ہوگا۔ پس مطلق کو اس کے ساتھ مقید کیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی اس کو حفظ متعارف کے ساتھ مقید کرتے ہیں۔
تشریح قوله وللمودع ان يسافر - موقع کے لئے ودیعت کو سفر میں لے جانا جائز ہے۔ گو اس کے اٹھانے میں جانور یا اجرت حملال کی ضرورت ہو بشر طیکہ مالک نے منع نہ کیا ہو۔ اور ودیعت کے ضائع ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر بار برداری کی احتیاج ہو تو سفر میں لے جانا جائز نہیں۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں لے جانا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں حفظ متعارف پر محمول ہے (وهو الحفظ في الامصار) صاحبین یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صورت مفروضہ میں اس پر بار برداری کی اجرت لازم ہے۔ اور ظاہر یہی کہ مودع اس سے راضی نہ ہوگا۔ امام صاحب یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مودع کی جانب سے حفظ ودیعت کا امر مطلق ہے تو جیسے یہ زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ایسے ہی کسی مکان کے ساتھ بھی مقید نہ ہو گا۔ قوله قلنا مؤنة الر... صالحین کے قول يلزمه مؤلة الرد اط" کا جواب ہے کہ یہ خر چہاس کی ملکیت میں اس ضرورت سے لازم آیا تا کہ اس کے محکم حفاظت کی تعمیل کی جائے لہذا اس خرچہ کے پڑنے کی کوئی پرواہ نہ ہوگی۔
قوله والعتاد كونهم یا امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے کہ امر معتاد تو صرف یہی ہے کہ مودع اور مودع خود شہر میں ہوتے ہیں۔ رہی حفاظت سو وہ صرف شہرہی میں معتاد نہیں بلکہ جو شخص جنگل میں ہو وہ اپنے مال کی حفاظت جنگل یہ میں کرتا ہے بخلاف اجرت پر حفاظت کرانے کے کہ یہ مانحن فیہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ عقد معاوضہ ہے تو جہاں عقد ہوا ہے وہیں سپر د کر نے کا مقتضی ہے۔
The book of deposits. In cities, protection (of deposits) is (customary), and it is like hiring for protection. We say that the cost of returning (the deposit) becomes necessary in his (the depositor's) possession due to the need of his order, so no attention will be paid to it. And the customary (practice) is that they are in the city, not their protection. And the person who is in the jungle, he protects his property in the jungle, contrary to hiring for protection. Because it is a contract of exchange. So the requirement of delivery is at the place of contract. If the depositary prohibits him from taking the deposit out, and he takes it out, he will become liable. Because placing this restriction is beneficial because complete protection is available in the city, so restricting is correct. This is that the owner will not be pleased with this. So the absolute will be restricted with it. And Imam Shafi'i restricts it with customary protection. Commentary on his statement: 'And the depositary may travel' - For a place, it is permissible to take the deposit on a journey, even if there is a need for an animal or hire for carrying, provided that the owner has not prohibited it. And there is no fear of loss of the deposit. According to the Sahibayn, if there is need for carriage, taking it on a journey is not permissible. According to Imam Shafi'i, in both cases it is not permissible. Because in their (Shafi'i's) view, it is interpreted on customary protection (which is protection in cities). The Sahibayn say that in the assumed case, the hire for carriage is necessary. And it is apparent that the depositary would not be pleased with that. Imam (Abu Hanifa) says that the command for protection of the deposit from the depositary is absolute, so just as it is not restricted by time, similarly it will not be restricted by any place. His statement: 'We say: the expense...' This is a response to the Sahibayn's statement that the expense of return is necessary. (Imam Abu Hanifa says) that this expense becomes necessary in his possession due to the need to implement his order of protection, so no attention will be paid to this expense. His statement: 'And the customary is that they are...' This is a response to Imam Shafi'i's proof that the customary thing is only that the depositor and depositary themselves are in the city. As for protection, it is not only customary in the city; rather, the person who is in the jungle protects his property in the jungle. As opposed to hiring for protection, which is not from our subject, but it is a contract of exchange, so the requirement is delivery where the contract took place.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn stating that the depositary may travel with the deposit. It discusses the limits of this permission. The author first explains that the cost of returning the deposit is borne by the depositor because it is necessary to fulfill the depositary's order of protection. If the depositary prohibits taking the deposit out of the city, and the depositor does so, he becomes liable. Imam Shafi'i restricts the deposit to customary protection in cities. Then the commentary elaborates on the ruling: the depositary may take the deposit on a journey even if it requires hire, provided the owner did not prohibit and there is no risk of loss. The Sahibayn disagree if hire is needed; they argue it imposes expense on the owner without consent. Imam Shafi'i disallows it entirely. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the command of protection is absolute, not restricted by time or place, and the expense is part of implementing the order. The response to Shafi'i is that protection is customary wherever the person is, not only in cities. The passage clarifies the Hanafi position that the depositary's authority is broad, limited only by explicit prohibition by the owner.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadīʿah): A deposit: property entrusted by one person to another for safekeeping without compensation.
مودع (mūdiʿ): The depositary: the person who receives the deposit for safekeeping.
حفظ متعارف (ḥifẓ mutaʿāraf): Customary protection: the level of care that is usual in the community, typically in cities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does the depositary become liable (dhaman) if he takes the deposit on a journey?
A) If he incurs carriage expense
B) If the owner prohibited him from taking it out
C) If he travels without the owner's knowledge
D) If the deposit is lost during travel

Key Takeaway
The depositary may travel with the deposit unless the owner prohibits it or there is a genuine fear of loss; the expense of carriage does not invalidate this permission in Abu Hanifa's view.

Delivering a Share of a Joint Deposit: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delivering a share of a joint deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on delivering a share of a joint deposit, and state the practical consequence of each position.

Core Idea
A depositary cannot unilaterally divide a joint deposit; the undivided share belongs to all, and only mutual consent or court can partition.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a common practical scenario: when two people deposit property with a single depositary, can one co-depositor claim his share if the other is absent? Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples — Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani — disagree. The disagreement turns on the nature of undivided property and the authority of the depositary.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the depositary must not deliver the share until all depositors are present. This is the starting point of the dispute.
This is the view upheld in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, one of the six Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani permit the depositary to deliver the share to the present depositor, at least for measurable or weighable items.
They analogize to a joint debt where a creditor can demand his share.
3
Follow the proofs of each side
Work through the dalil of the Sahibayn (qiyas on joint debt) and then the dalil of Abu Hanifa (undivided share contains both rights; depositary lacks authority to partition).
Note the key distinction: debts are paid by equivalents, but deposited items are specific property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
See how Abu Hanifa's position rebuts the analogy: the right to take physically does not compel the depositary to deliver. The depositary is not an agent for division.
The response uses a counter-example of a depositor who is also a debtor.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the depositary withholds all until all are present. Under the Sahibayn, for fungible items, he may deliver the share to the present one and remains liable to the absent one.
The dispute only applies to measurable/weighable items; for non-fungibles, all agree the depositary must not deliver.

قَالَ وَإِذَا أَوْدَعَ رَجُلَانِ عِندَ رَجُلٍ وَدِيْعَةً فَحَضَرَ أَحَدَهُمَا يَطْلُبُ نَصِيبَهُ لَمْ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ نَصِيبَهُ حَتَّى يَحْضُرَ الآخَرُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ نَصِيبَهُ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ ثَلَاثَةٌ إِسْتَوْدَعُوا رَجُلًا أَلْفًا فَغَابَ إِثْنَانِ فَلَيْسَ لِلْحَاضِرِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ نَصِيبَهُ عِنْدَهُ وَقَالَا لَهُ ذَالِكَ وَالْخِلَافُ فِي الْمَكِيْلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ وَهُوَ الْمُرَادُ بِالْمَذْكُورٍ فِى الْمُخْتَصَر لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ طَالَبَهُ بدَفَع نَصِيبهِ فَيُؤْمَرُ بالدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي الدَّيْنِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِتَسْلِيم مَا سَلَّمَ إِلَيْهِ وَهُوَ النِّصْفُ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ فَكَذَا يُؤْمَرُ هُوَ بِالدَّفْعِ إِلَيْهِ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةٌ أَنَّهُ طَالَبَهُ بِدَفْعِ نَصِيْبِ الْغَائِبِ لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِالْمُفْرَزِ وَحَقَّهُ فِى الْمُشَاعِ وَالْمُفْرَزُ الْمُعَيَّنَ يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى الْحَقَّيْنِ وَلَا مَيَّزُ حَقَّهُ إِلَّا بِالْقِسْمَةِ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُودَعِ وِلَايَةُ الْقِسْمَةِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَقَعُ دَفْعُهُ قِسْمَةٌ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ بِخِلَافِ الدَّيْنِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ لِأَنَّهُ يُطَالِبُهُ بِتَسْلِيمٍ حَقِهِ لاَنَّ الدُّيُون تُقْضَى بِاِمْثَالِهَا وَقَوْلُهُ لَهُ اَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ قُلْنَا لَيْسَ مِنْ ضَرُورَتِهِ أَنْ تجْبَرَ الْمُوْدَعُ عَلَى الدَّفْعِ كَمَا إِذَا كَانَتْ لَهُ أَلْفُ دِرْهَمٍ وَدِيْعَةً عِنْدَ إِنْسَانِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْقُ بِغَيْرِهِ فَلِغَرِيْمِهِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ إِذَا ظَفَرَ بِهِ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُودَعِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهُ إِلَيْهِ
ترجمه: اگر دو آدمیوں نے ایک شخص کے پاس ودیعت رکھی پھر ان میں سے ایک آکر اپنا حصہ مانگنے لگا تو مودع اس کو اس کا حصہ نہ دے یہاں تک کہ دوسرا حاضر ہو۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا حصہ دیدے۔ جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ تین آدمیوں نے ایک شخص کے پاس ایک ہزار درہم ودیعت رکھے پھر دو غائب ہو گئے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حاضر کو اپنا حصہ لینے کا اختیار نہیں۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کو یہ اختیار ہے اور اختلاف کمیل و موزون میں ہے اور مختصر القدوری میں بھی یہی مراد ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے صرف اپنا حصہ دینے کا مطالبہ کیا ہے تو مستودع کو اس کے دینے کا حکم کیا جائے گا جیسے دین مشترک میں ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ اس نے جو حصہ سپر د کیا تھا صرف اسی کا مطالبہ کیا ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مقسوم و ممیز کا طلب گار ہے حالانکہ اس کا حق غیر مقسوم میں ہے اور جدا کردہ معین حصہ دونوں کے حق کو شامل ہوگا اور طالب کا حق بٹوارہ کے بغیر ممتاز نہیں ہو سکتا۔ حالانکہ مودع کو بٹوارہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا دینا بالا جماع بٹوارہ نہیں ہوتا بخلاف دین مشترک کے کہ اس میں قرض خواہ اپنا حق دینے کا مطالبہ کرتا ہے کیونکہ قرضوں کی ادائیگی اپنے بل سے ہوا کرتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے قول له ان ی اخذہ “ کے جواب میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس سے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ مودع کو دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے جیسے ایک شخص کے ہزار درہم کسی کے پاس ودیعت ہوں اور مودع پر کسی اور کے ہزار درہم آئے ہوں تو اس کے قرض خواہ کو اختیار ہے کہ جہاں قابو پائے اپنا حق لے لے لیکن مودع کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ ودیعت اس کو دے دے۔ تشریح قوله واذا اودع - دو آدمیوں نے کوئی چیز مودع کے پاس ودیعت رکھی پھر ایک شخص نے آکر اپنا حصہ واپس کر دینے کا مطالبہ کیاتو اگر وہ چیز ذوات القیم میں سے ہے تو مودع کے لئے اس کا حصہ دینا بالا جماع جائز نہیں تاوقتیکہ دوسرا شخص حاضر نہ ہو اور اگر وہ چیز کیلی یاوزنی ہے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔
قوله وفى الجامع .... جامع صغیر کی عبارت تین فوائد کے پیش نظر ذکر کر رہے ہیں: اول... موضع خلاف کی تعیین کہ اختلاف تکمیل و موزون میں ہے نہ کہ ان کے غیر میں کیونکہ جامع صغیر میں لفظ الف مذکور ہے جو موزون ہے بخلاف عبارت قدوری کے کہ اس میں لفظ ودیعہ ہے۔ دومید کہ عبارت قدوری میں اثنین کی تنصیص ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ثلثہ ہے۔ اب قدوری کی عبارت پر کوئی یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ تین میں سے جو حاضر ہو اس کا حصہ غائبین کے حصوں سے اقل ہے تو اس کو اکثر کے تابع کر دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے وہ مودع سے نہیں لے سکتا لیکن دو میں سے ایک اگر حاضر ہو تو اس کا حصہ برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے تابع نہیں کر سکتے تو اس کو لینے کا اختیار ہونا چاہیئے ۔ جامع صغیر کی عبارت نے بتلا دیا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں حکم برابر ہے۔ یعنی نہیں لے سکتا۔ سوم یہ کہ کتاب الودیعہ میں مذکور ہے القاضي لا يأمر المودع بالدفع اس سے یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ دیانہ لے سکتا ہے۔ جامع صغیر کے الفاظ ليس له ان يأخذ “ نے اس شبہ کو زائل کر دیا۔ وقد ناقش في ذالك كله صاحب النتائج
قـولـه لـهـمـا انـه طالبه ... صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے جو کچھ مودع کے سپر د کیا تھا یعنی نصف حصہ وہ اسکا مطالبہ کر رہا ہے، لہذا اسکو دیدینا چاہئے ۔ جیسے دین مشترک میں ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا دو شخصوں نے اپنا مشترک غلام فروخت کیا تو ان میں سے ایک شخص حاضر ہو کر مدیون سے اپنا حصہ کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔ قوله و لابی حنیفہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ صرف اپنا حصہ نہیں مانگ رہا بلکہ غائب کا حصہ بھی طلب کر رہا ہے اس واسطے کہ وہ
He said: When two men deposit a deposit with a man, and one of them comes demanding his share, he (the depositary) will not pay to him his share until the other is present, according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He pays to him his share. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: Three men deposited a thousand (dirhams) with a man; two were absent, so the present one does not have the right to take his share according to him (Abu Hanifa). And they said: He has that. And the disagreement is in measured and weighed items, and that is intended in Al-Mukhtasar. Their (Sahibayn's) proof: He demanded that he pay his share, so he is ordered to pay to him, as in a joint debt. This is because he is demanding delivery of what he delivered, which is half. For this reason he had the right to take it, so likewise he is ordered to pay to him. And for Abu Hanifa: He demanded the payment of the absent's share, because he is demanding the segregated (portion), and his right is in the undivided (share), and the specified segregated (portion) contains both rights, and his right is not distinguished except by division, and the depositary does not have the authority of division, for this reason his payment does not constitute division by consensus, contrary to a joint debt, because he demands delivery of his right, since debts are paid by their equivalents. And regarding his (Sahibayn's) statement: 'He has the right to take it', we say: It does not necessarily follow that the depositary is compelled to pay, as when someone has a thousand dirhams as a deposit with a person and owes a thousand to someone else, then his creditor may take it if he gets hold of it, but the depositary is not to pay it to him. Translation: If two men placed a deposit with a person, then one of them comes asking for his share, the depositary should not give him his share until the other is present, according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn say: Give him his share. In Al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is mentioned that three men deposited a thousand dirhams with a person, then two disappeared, so according to Abu Hanifa the present one does not have the right to take his share. The Sahibayn say: He has this right. And the disagreement is in measured and weighed items, and this is meant in Al-Mukhtasar. The proof of the Sahibayn: He demanded the payment of his share only, so the depositary should be ordered to give it, as in a joint debt. And this is because he demands delivery of what he delivered, which is half. Therefore, he has the right to take it, so similarly he is ordered to deliver. And the proof of Abu Hanifa: He is demanding the payment of the absent's share, because he demands the segregated portion, and his right is in the undivided, and the specified segregated portion includes both rights, and his right cannot be separated without division, and the depositary does not have authority over division. Therefore, his delivery does not count as division by consensus, contrary to joint debt, because the creditor demands delivery of his right since debts are paid by their equivalents. And the response to the Sahibayn's statement that he has the right to take: We say that it does not necessitate that the depositary be forced to pay, like the case where a person has a thousand dirhams deposit with someone and owes a thousand to another, then his creditor may take it when he finds it, but the depositary is not to pay it to him. Commentary on his statement: 'And when two deposit...' - If two men deposit something with a depositary, then one person comes asking for his share to be returned, then if the thing is among articles of value, it is not permissible for the depositary to give his share by consensus until the other person is present. And if the thing is measured or weighed, then according to the Sahibayn it is permissible; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is not. His statement: 'And in Al-Jami'...' The text of Al-Jami' al-Saghir is mentioned for three benefits: First, to specify the locus of disagreement that it is in measured and weighed items, not others, because in Al-Jami' al-Saghir the word 'alf' (thousand) is mentioned which is weighed, contrary to the text of Al-Quduri which has the word 'wadi'a' (deposit). Second, that the text of Al-Quduri specifies two people, and Al-Jami' al-Saghir mentions three. So someone might say that from among three, the present one's share is less than the absent ones' shares, so his share would be subsumed by the majority, therefore he cannot take. But if one of two is present, his share is equal, so he cannot be subsumed, so he should have the right to take. The text of Al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that the ruling is the same in both cases, i.e., he cannot take. Third, in Kitab al-Wadi'a it is mentioned that the judge does not order the depositary to pay, causing the misconception that he may take it voluntarily. The words of Al-Jami' al-Saghir 'he does not have the right to take' remove this doubt. And the author of Al-Nata'ij criticized all of this. His statement: 'Their proof: he demanded...' The proof of the Sahibayn: He is demanding what he deposited, i.e., half, so he should be given it, like in a joint debt. For example, two people sold their joint slave, then one of them can demand his share from the debtor. His statement: 'And for Abu Hanifa' - The proof of Abu Hanifa: He is not merely asking for his share, but also the absent's share, because he...

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a joint deposit. The matn states the ruling: if two people deposit an item with a depositary, and one demands his share, the depositary should not give it until the other is present, according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow giving the share. The disagreement is limited to measurable or weighable items (like grain or silver), not articles of value (like jewelry). The proof of the Sahibayn is analogical to joint debt: the depositary should give what was deposited by the claimant. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that the claimant is actually demanding the absent party's share, because the undivided property includes both rights. The depositary cannot partition the property, and delivering a specific portion would not constitute valid division by consensus. The commentary also includes three benefits from Al-Jami' al-Saghir, resolving apparent inconsistencies with Al-Mukhtasar and Al-Quduri. The passage clarifies that the Hanafi position, as upheld in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, is that a common depositary cannot deliver a share without the others' presence, but the Sahibayn differ for fungible items.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadīʿah): A deposit: property entrusted for safekeeping.
مشاع (mushāʿ): Undivided share in common property, not yet partitioned.
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of jointly owned property, requiring mutual consent or court order.
جامع صغیر (al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr): A foundational Hanafi text by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
مختصر القدوری (Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): A well-known Hanafi fiqh manual by al-Quduri, used as a matn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (muftā bihi) in this lesson, what should a depositary do when one of two joint depositors demands his share and the other is absent?
A) Deliver the share because the claimant has a right to his property.
B) Deliver the share only if the item is measurable or weighable.
C) Refuse to deliver until all depositors are present, regardless of the item type.
D) Refuse to deliver if the item is non-fungible, but deliver if it is fungible.

Key Takeaway
A depositary may not deliver a share of a joint deposit to one owner without the others present, because undivided property cannot be partitioned unilaterally.

intermediate
10 min
Handing Over a Share to One Joint Depositor: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial handover of joint deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on handing over a share to one joint depositor and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
A depositary cannot divide joint property without authority—Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits partial handover; Sahibayn allow it by qiyas on common debt.

When two or more people deposit a single item with one depositary, and one depositor later demands his share, a conflict arises: should the depositary hand over a portion, or must he wait until all depositors are present? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement, examining the proofs from Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and clarifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
What is the factual situation? Two or more depositors entrust a single item to one depositary. One depositor comes alone demanding his share. The depositary must decide.
The item may be measured/weighed or of value.
2
State the prima facie ruling from the matn
The matn says: 'The depositary may not give it to him.' This is the default position. Recognize that this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize to a common debt (dayn mushtarak): a creditor can demand his share from a debtor without other creditors. Similarly, the depositor is only asking for his own share, so the depositary should give.
Qiyas on debt repayment by equivalent (mithl).
4
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes deposits from debts. A deposit is a specific thing; the depositary cannot divide it without authority. Handing over a purported share would involve the absent party's right, as the share is undivided. The depositary lacks power to partition.
The exact thing must be returned, not an equivalent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: the depositary must refuse until all depositors are present. The Sahibayn's view is considered weaker in practice.
The story of the bathhouse (mas'alah hammami) illustrates the practical wisdom of Imam Abu Hanifa's position.

مطالبہ کیا ہے تو مستودع کو اس کے دینے کا حکم کیا جائے گا جیسے دین مشترک میں ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ اس نے جو حصہ سپر د کیا تھا صرف اسی کا مطالبہ کیا ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مقسوم و ممیز کا طلب گار ہے حالانکہ اس کا حق غیر مقسوم میں ہے اور جدا کردہ معین حصہ دونوں کے حق کو شامل ہوگا اور طالب کا حق بٹوارہ کے بغیر ممتاز نہیں ہو سکتا۔ حالانکہ مودع کو بٹوارہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا دینا بالا جماع بٹوارہ نہیں ہوتا بخلاف دین مشترک کے کہ اس میں قرض خواہ اپنا حق دینے کا مطالبہ کرتا ہے کیونکہ قرضوں کی ادائیگی اپنے بل سے ہوا کرتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے قول له ان ی اخذہ “ کے جواب میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس سے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ مودع کو دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے جیسے ایک شخص کے ہزار درہم کسی کے پاس ودیعت ہوں اور مودع پر کسی اور کے ہزار درہم آئے ہوں تو اس کے قرض خواہ کو اختیار ہے کہ جہاں قابو پائے اپنا حق لے لے لیکن مودع کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ ودیعت اس کو دے دے۔ تشریح قوله واذا اودع - دو آدمیوں نے کوئی چیز مودع کے پاس ودیعت رکھی پھر ایک شخص نے آکر اپنا حصہ واپس کر دینے کا مطالبہ کیاتو اگر وہ چیز ذوات القیم میں سے ہے تو مودع کے لئے اس کا حصہ دینا بالا جماع جائز نہیں تاوقتیکہ دوسرا شخص حاضر نہ ہو اور اگر وہ چیز کیلی یاوزنی ہے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔ قوله وفى الجامع .... جامع صغیر کی عبارت تین فوائد کے پیش نظر ذکر کر رہے ہیں: اول... موضع خلاف کی تعیین کہ اختلاف تکمیل و موزون میں ہے نہ کہ ان کے غیر میں کیونکہ جامع صغیر میں لفظ الف مذکور ہے جو موزون ہے بخلاف عبارت قدوری کے کہ اس میں لفظ ودیعہ ہے۔ دومید کہ عبارت قدوری میں اثنین کی تنصیص ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ثلثہ ہے۔ اب قدوری کی عبارت پر کوئی یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ تین میں سے جو حاضر ہو اس کا حصہ غائبین کے حصوں سے اقل ہے تو اس کو اکثر کے تابع کر دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے وہ مودع سے نہیں لے سکتا لیکن دو میں سے ایک اگر حاضر ہو تو اس کا حصہ برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے تابع نہیں کر سکتے تو اس کو لینے کا اختیار ہونا چاہیئے ۔ جامع صغیر کی عبارت نے بتلا دیا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں حکم برابر ہے۔ یعنی نہیں لے سکتا۔ سوم یہ کہ کتاب الودیعہ میں مذکور ہے القاضي لا يأمر المودع بالدفع اس سے یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ دیانہ لے سکتا ہے۔ جامع صغیر کے الفاظ ليس له ان يأخذ “ نے اس شبہ کو زائل کر دیا۔ وقد ناقش في ذالك كله صاحب النتائج قـولـه لـهـمـا انـه طالبه ... صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے جو کچھ مودع کے سپر د کیا تھا یعنی نصف حصہ وہ اسکا مطالبہ کر رہا ہے، لہذا اسکو دیدینا چاہئے ۔ جیسے دین مشترک میں ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا دو شخصوں نے اپنا مشترک غلام فروخت کیا تو ان میں سے ایک شخص حاضر ہو کر مدیون سے اپنا حصہ کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔ قوله و لابی حنیفہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ صرف اپنا حصہ نہیں مانگ رہا بلکہ غائب کا حصہ بھی طلب کر رہا ہے اس واسطے کہ وہ ...... مودع کو وارد کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف ذین مشترک کے کہ اس میں قرض خواہ اپنا حق دینے کا مطالبہ کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ دیوان کی ادائیگی بالمثل ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی قرض دار پر جو قرضہ ہے وہ بعینہ نہیں دیتا بلکہ اس کا مثل دیتا ہے پھر مقاصہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ مرز ( تیم شدہ) کو طلب کر رہا ہے حالانکہ اس کا حق مشاع میں ہے نہ کہ مینز میں اور اس کا حصہ ممیز اسی وقت ہوگا۔ جب بٹوارہ ہو جائے besture قوله وقوله ان يأخذه ... صاحبين كے قول ولهذا كان له ان ياخذه “ کا جواب ہے اور قولہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع بقول علامہ عینی معہود نی الذه ن قائل ہے ای قول القائل نصرة لقولهما - لیکن بقول صاحب نتائج بہتر یہ ہے کہ مرجع خصم ہے۔ ای قول الخصم في هذه المسئلة وهو الامامان بہر کیف صاحبین نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ مودع جہاں قابو پائے اپنا حق لے سکتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہاں لے سکتا ہے لیکن اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ مودع پر دے دینے کا جبر کیا جائے۔ چنانچہ ایک شخص کے ہزار درہم کسی کے پاس ودیعت ہوں اور مودع پر کسی اور کے ہزار درہم آتے ہوں تو اس کے قرض خواہ کو اختیار ہے کہ جہاں اس کا مال پائے لے لے مگر مودع کہ یہ اختیار نہیں کہ ودیعت اس کو دے دے اور یہاں پر گفتگو اسی میں ہے کہ مودع کو دے دینا جائز ہے یا نہیں۔ فائده فوائد ظہیر یہ میں ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کو مسئلہ حمامی کہتے ہیں جس کا قصہ یہ ہے کہ دو آدمی حمام کے مالک کو ایک ہمیانی ودیعت دے کر حمام میں داخل ہوئے ۔ پھر ان میں سے ایک باہر آیا اور ہمیانی لے کر چلتا بنا اس کے بعد دوسرے نے آکر ہمیانی کا مطالبہ کیا ( یہ غالبا ان دونوں کی سازش تھی)۔ تمام کا مالک حیران رہ گیا کہ اب کیا کروں تو اس سے کسی نے کہا کہ اس کی تدبیر امام ابو حنیفہ ہی بتلا سکتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ اس نے آپ کی خدمت میں حاضر ہو کر قصہ سنایا ، امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا ۔ کہ تو اس سے یہ مت کہہ میں ہمیانی دے چکا ہوں بلکہ یوں کہہ کہ جب تک تیرا ساتھی نہ آئے گا ہمیائی نہیں دوں گا اس نے ایسا ہی کیا۔ پس اس شخص نے لاچار ہو کر حمام کے مالک کو چھوڑ دیا۔
He may take it when he gets hold of it, and the depositary may not give it to him. Translation: If two men deposit something with a person, then one of them comes asking for his share, the depositary should not give him his share until the other comes. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn say: give him his share. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: Three men deposited one thousand dirhams with a person, then two became absent. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the present one has no right to take his share. The Sahibayn say he has that right, and the dispute is over kumail and mawzun, and that is the same meaning in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The Sahibayn's proof: He only demanded the giving of his share, so the depositary should be ordered to give it to him, like in a common debt. And that is because he demanded only the share he deposited, since he is seeking a divided and distinguished portion, whereas his right is in an undivided thing, and a separated specific share includes both parties' rights, and the claimant's share cannot be distinguished without division. However, the depositary has no authority to divide, so his giving it does not constitute division, unlike a common debt where the creditor demands his right because debts are repaid by their equivalent. And regarding the Sahibayn's statement 'he has the right to take it', we say: from this it does not necessarily follow that the depositary can be forced to give, just as if a person has a thousand dirhams deposited with someone, and that depositary owes a thousand dirhams to another, the creditor has the right to take his due where he gets hold of it, but the depositary does not have the right to give the deposit to him. Explanation of his statement: 'When two deposit...' - If two men deposit something with the depositary, then one person comes demanding his share back, then if the thing is of value, it is not permissible for the depositary to give his share by consensus until the other person is present. If the thing is measured or weighed, then according to the Sahibayn it is permissible, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is not permissible. His statement: 'And in al-Jami'...' - He mentions the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir with three benefits: First, determination of the place of dispute that it is over kumail and mawzun, not otherwise, because in al-Jami' al-Saghir the word 'alf' (thousand) appears which is weighed, unlike the text of al-Quduri where the word 'wadi'ah' is used. Second, that the text of al-Quduri specifies two, while al-Jami' al-Saghir specifies three. One might say that when one of three is present, his share is less than the absent ones' shares, so it is subordinate to the majority; therefore he cannot take from the depositary. But if one of two is present, his share is equal, so it is not subordinate, so he should have the right to take. The text of al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that the ruling is the same in both cases: he cannot take. Third, that in the Book of Deposit it is mentioned: 'The judge does not order the depositary to give', so there is an impression that he can take by way of religious obligation. The words of al-Jami' al-Saghir 'he has no right to take' remove this doubt. And Sahib al-Nata'ij criticized all this. His statement: 'Their claim that he demanded...' - The Sahibayn's proof: He is demanding what he deposited with the depositary, i.e., half the share, so he should be given it, like in a common debt. For example, if two persons sold their common slave, one of them can present himself and demand his share from the debtor. His statement: 'And for Abu Hanifa...' - Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He is not only asking for his share, but also demanding the absent person's share because he... does not have the right to bring action against the depositary. Unlike a common debt where the creditor demands his right because debts are discharged by their equivalent. That is, the debtor does not give the exact same thing but its equivalent, then set-off occurs. He is demanding a specific thing, whereas his right is in common ownership, not specific, and his share will only become specific when division occurs. His statement: 'And his statement: He may take it...' - This is the response to the Sahibayn's statement 'therefore he has the right to take it', and the pronoun in 'his statement' refers, according to Allama 'Ayni, to the one known in the mind, i.e., the speaker supporting them. But according to Sahib al-Nata'ij, it is better that it refers to the opponent, i.e., the statement of the opponent in this issue, which is the two Imams [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. In short, the Sahibayn said that the depositary can take his right wherever he gets hold of it. The response is: Yes, he can take it, but this does not necessitate that the depositary be coerced to give it. For example, if a person has a thousand dirhams deposited with someone, and that depositary owes a thousand dirhams to another, his creditor has the right to take his property wherever he finds it, but the depositary does not have the right to give the deposit to him. And the discussion here is whether it is permissible for the depositary to give it or not. Benefit: In Fawa'id al-Zahiriyyah it is mentioned that this issue is called the 'Bathhouse Issue', the story of which is: Two men gave a purse to the owner of a bathhouse as a deposit and entered the bathhouse. Then one of them came out, took the purse, and left. Afterwards the other came asking for the purse (this was probably a conspiracy between them). The bathhouse owner became perplexed as to what to do, so someone told him that only Imam Abu Hanifa could advise him. So he went to him and told the story. Imam Abu Hanifa said: Do not say 'I have already given the purse' but rather say 'I will not give the purse until your companion comes.' He did so, and so the man was forced to leave the bathhouse owner alone.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding deposits made by multiple depositors with a single depositary. When one depositor alone comes to claim his share, the question is whether the depositary must hand it over before the other depositor appears. The matn states the basic ruling: the depositary may not give it. The commentary then presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The Sahibayn argue by qiyas on a common debt: just as a creditor can claim his share from a debtor without the other creditor present, so here the depositor can claim his share. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in a debt, repayment is by equivalent (mithl), not the exact same item, so the debtor can give without dividing; but in a deposit, the exact item must be returned. Since the deposit is undivided, handing over a portion would entail an unauthorized division that the depositary lacks authority to perform. The text further cites al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Quduri to clarify that the dispute applies to both items of value (qimi) and weighed/measured items (kayli/wazni), and that the ruling is the same whether there are two or three depositors. The passage also includes the famous 'Bathhouse Issue' (مسئلہ حمامی) illustrating the practical application of Imam Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A deposit; a contract where one entrusts property to another for safekeeping without compensation.
مودع (mudi' / mustawda'): The depositary; the person who receives the deposit and is entrusted with safekeeping.
دین مشترک (dayn mushtarak): A common debt owed to multiple creditors, where each creditor has a share in the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if two people deposit a single item with a depositary and one comes to claim his share, what must the depositary do?
A) Hand over the share immediately
B) Refuse until the other depositor is present
C) Divide the item himself and give half
D) Give the entire item to the present depositor

Key Takeaway
In a joint deposit, the depositary must not hand over a share to one depositor alone; the mufta bihi is Imam Abu Hanifa's prohibition, based on the inability to divide without consent or authority.

intermediate
8 min
Dividing Custody When Two Depositaries Hold a Deposit
Explains how two depositaries must handle a deposit based on divisibility, with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for divisible vs indivisible deposits with two depositaries, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and apply the same reasoning to analogous cases (pledgees, agents).

Core Idea
Depositaries of a divisible item must split custody; for indivisible items, one may keep it with the other's permission.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: one depositor leaves an item with two trustees. The ruling hinges on divisibility, and within the Hanafi school there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. You will learn the rule, the proof, and why it extends to pledgees and agents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Read the passage and note that it distinguishes between a divisible item (mimma yuqsamu) and an indivisible item (mimma la yuqsamu). For each, identify the ruling stated by the matn.
Divisible items: grains, liquids, money. Indivisible: a single animal, a unique artifact.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Ruling
For divisible items, depositaries must divide the deposit and each keep half. For indivisible items, one may keep it with the other's permission.
The matn attributes this to Abu Hanifa (Hadha inda Abi Hanifah).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's Objection
The Sahibayn argue that since the owner consented to their trustworthiness, either depositary may hand the whole to the other without liability, just as in the indivisible case.
Their reasoning: consent to emaanah (trustworthiness) implies permission to delegate custody.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's Rational Proof
Abu Hanifa counters: consent was to both keeping, not to one keeping all. When an action (like keeping) is attributed to something divisible, it applies to part, not the whole. Therefore, handing over the entire divisible item without owner's consent makes the giver liable.
This is a qiyas based on the nature of divisibility and the scope of consent.
5
Extend to Other Analogies
The same ruling applies to two pledgees (murtahinan) and two agents for purchase (wakilan bi al-shira'). Understand why the illa (effective cause) of divisibility is consistent.
The text explicitly says 'wa kadhalika al-jawab' (the answer is the same).

قَالَ وَإِنْ أَوَدَعَ رَجُلٌ عِندَ رَجُلَيْنِ شَيْئًا مِمَّا يُقْسَمُ لَمْ يَجُزْ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهُ أَحَدَهُمَا إِلَى الْآخَرِ وَلَكِنَّهُمَا يَقْتَسِمَانِهِ فيحفظ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِصْفَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَازَ أَنْ يَحْفَظَهُ اَحَدُهُمَا بِإِذْنِ الْآخَرِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَالِكَ الْجَوَابُ عِنْدَهُ فِي الْمُرْتَهِنَيْنِ وَالْوَكِيْلَيْنِ بِالشّرَاءِ إِذَا سَلَّمَ اَحَدُهُمَا إِلَى الْآخَرِ وَقَالَا لَأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَحْفَظَ بِإِذْنِ الْآخَرِ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ رَضِيَ بِاِمَانَتِهِمَا فَكَانَ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا أَنْ يُسَلَّمَ إِلَى الْآخَرِ وَلَا يَضْمَنُهُ كَمَا فِي مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ وَلَهُ إِنَّهُ رَضِيَ بِحِفْظِهِمَا وَلَمْ يَرْضَ بِحِفْظِ أَحَدِهِمَا كُلَّهُ لَانَّ الْفِعْلَ متَى أُضِيْفَ إِلَى مَا يَقْبَلُ الْوَصْفَ بِالتَّجَزِى يَتَنَاوَلُ الْبَعْضَ دُونَ الْكُلِ فَوَقَعَ التَّسْلِيمُ إِلَى الْآخَرِ مِنْ غَيْرِ رِضَاءِ الْمَالِكِ فَيَضْمَنُ الدَّافِعُ وَلَا يَضْمَنُ الْقَابِضُ لِاَنَّ مُودَعَ الْمُؤدَعُ عِندَهُ لا يَضْمَنَ وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا أَوْدَعُهُمَا وَلَا يُمْكِنُهُمَا الْإِجْتِمَاعُ عَلَيْهِ آنَاءَ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَامْكَنَهُمَا الْمُهَايَاةُ كَانَ الْمَالِكُ رَاضِبًا بدفع الكُلِّ إِلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فِي بَعْضَ الْأَحْوَالِ ترجمہ اگر ودیعت رکھی ایک شخص نے دو آدمیوں کے پاس ایسی چیز جو قسیم ہوسکتی ہے تو جائز نہیں یہ کہ وہ ساری چیز دے دے ان میں سے کوئی ایک دوسرے کو بلکہ اسے تقسیم کر لیں پھر ہر ایک اس کے نصف کی حفاظت کرے اور اگر وہ چیز ایسی ہے جو تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتی تو ان میں سے ایک دوسرے
He said: If a man deposits with two men something that can be divided, it is not permissible for one of them to give it to the other, but they should divide it and each keep half. If it is something that cannot be divided, it is permissible for one of them to keep it with the permission of the other. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, the answer according to him in the case of two pledgees and two agents for purchase when one of them hands over to the other. They both said: One of them may keep it with the permission of the other in both cases, for he consented to their trustworthiness, so each may hand over to the other and not be liable, as in the case of what cannot be divided. And He has: that he consented to both keeping it, but did not consent to one keeping it all, because when an action is attributed to something that admits of division, it includes part without the whole. So the handover to the other is without the owner's consent, so the giver is liable, but the receiver is not liable because a depositary of a deposit with him does not guarantee. This is unlike what cannot be divided, because when he deposited with both and it is not possible for them to both keep it at all times of night and day, and they can alternate (muhayah), the owner is content with giving the whole to one of them at some times. Translation: If a person deposits with two people something that is divisible, it is not permissible for one of them to give the whole thing to the other. Rather, they should divide it, then each one protects his half. If the thing is not divisible, then one of them may protect it with the other's permission.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn on a deposit (wadi'ah) made by one person with two depositaries (mustawda'ayn). The issue is how they should handle safekeeping. For a divisible item (e.g., a heap of wheat), it is not permissible for one depositary to hand over the entire deposit to the other; they must divide it equally and each keep his half. For an indivisible item (e.g., a single horse), it is permissible for one to keep the whole with the other's permission, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary extends this to pledgees (murtahinan) and agents for purchase (wakilan bi al-shira'). The Sahibayn argue that since the owner consented to their trustworthiness, each may hand over to the other without liability, just as in the indivisible case. Imam Abu Hanifa responds: the owner consented to both keeping the deposit, not to one keeping it all. When the action (keeping) is attributed to something that can be partially performed, it implies part, not the whole. Therefore, handing over the entire divisible item without the owner's consent makes the giver liable (damin), but the receiver is not liable because a sub-depositary does not guarantee. For indivisible items, the owner implicitly consents to the whole being with one because continuous co-possession is impractical and they can alternate (muhayah). Thus, the ruling distinguishes based on divisibility.

Key Terms
مما يقسم (mimma yuqsamu): Something that can be divided without loss or change of nature, e.g., grains, liquids.
مهاتاة (muhayah): Alternating possession or use; a schedule of time-sharing between co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone deposits a sack of wheat (divisible) with two depositaries, what must they do?
A) One keeps the whole sack with the other's permission
B) They must divide the wheat equally and each keep half
C) They must both stay with the sack together at all times
D) They may give the whole sack to a third party

Key Takeaway
For a divisible deposit with two depositaries, Hanafi law requires division and each depositary keeps his share; handing over the whole makes the giver liable.
